Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Dhimmis Not Attending the Prayer for Rain
States the ruling and proof that dhimmis do not attend salat al-istisqa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dhimmi attendance at salat al-istisqa' and explain the primary proofs (Umar's prohibition and Quranic principle) that support it.

Core Idea
Dhimmis are prohibited from the prayer for rain; their supplication is futile and mercy descends only upon believers.

This lesson focuses on a specific ruling within the chapter of salat al-istisqa': the prohibition of dhimmis attending. The author, after stating the ruling, provides a lengthy hadith describing the Prophet's ﷺ practice and then clarifies the reasoning. You will learn not only the ruling but also the underlying rationale and a glimpse of intra-Hanafi discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the attendance of a dhimmi at the prayer for rain (salat al-istisqa'). The ruling is explicitly stated: لا يحضره ذمي – a dhimmi does not attend it, which implies prohibition (haram).
The term 'ذمي' refers to a non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a lengthy hadith from Sunan Abi Dawood (from Aisha) that describes the Prophet's ﷺ performance of istisqa'. This hadith serves as the primary textual evidence for the practice itself.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) in transmission, making it zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith does not explicitly mention dhimmis. The prohibition is derived from post-Prophetic practice and reasoning: the commentary mentions Umar's prohibition, the Quranic principle that the supplication of disbelievers is in vain (Quran 40:50), and the purpose of the prayer – to seek mercy, which descends only upon believers.
The wajh al-dalalah connects the hadith's description of the prayer to the exclusion of dhimmis via these supplementary proofs.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The commentary notes a minority view (in al-Dirayah) that dhimmis should not be prevented, as their supplication might be answered in this world as a hastened portion. However, the relied-upon position (al-Kamal) upholds prohibition.
This ikhtilaf shows the range of opinion within the Hanafi school, but the mufta bihi is the prohibitionist view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Based on the tarjih from al-Kamal and the overall reasoning, the operative ruling for fatwa is that dhimmis are prohibited from attending salat al-istisqa'.
The authority weight is zahir riwayah, as the prohibition is well-established in the core texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يحضُرُه ذِمّي. «سنن أبي داود عن عائشة قالت: شكى النَّاسُ إِلَى رَسُول اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَحْطَ الْمَطَرِ فَأَمَرَ رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بِمِنْبَرِ فَوُضِعَ لَهُ فِي الْمُصَلَّى وَوَعَدَ النَّاسَ يَوْمًا يَخْرُجُونَ فِيهِ، قَالَ: فَخَرَجَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حِينَ بَدَا حَاجِبُ الشَّمْسِ، فَقَعَدَ عَلَى الْمِنْبَر فَكَبَّرَ وَحَمِدَ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلْ ثُمَّ قَالَ: «إِنَّكُمْ شَكَوْتُمْ جَدْبَ دِيَارِكُمْ، وَاسْتِنْخَارَ الْمَطَرِ عَنْ زَمَانِهِ عَنْكُمْ، وَقَدْ أَمَرَكُمُ اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ أَنْ تَدْعُوهُ، وَوَعَدَكُمْ أَنْ يَسْتَجِيبَ لَكُمْ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ مَلِكِ يَوْمِ الدِّينِ لَا إِلَهَ إِلا اللَّهُ يَفْعَلُ مَا يُرِيدُ اللَّهُمَّ أَنْتَ اللهُ الذي لا إِلَهَ إِلا أَنْتَ الْغَنِيُّ وَنَحْنُ الْفُقَرَاءُ، أَنْزِلْ عَلَيْنَا الْغَيْثَ، وَاجْعَلْ مَا أَنْزَلْتَ قُوَّةً وَبَلَاعًا إِلَى حِينٍ ثُمَّ رَفَعَ يَدَيْهِ، فَلَمْ يَزَلْ فِي الرَّفْعِ حَتَّى بَدَا بَيَاضُ إِبِطَيْهِ، ثُمَّ حَوَّلَ إِلَى النَّاسِ ظَهْرَهُ، وَقَلَبَ أَوْ حَوَّلَ رِدَاءَهُ وَهُوَ رَافِعٌ يَدَيْهِ ثُمَّ أَقْبَلَ عَلَى النَّاسِ وَنَزَلَ مِن المِنبَرِ، وَصَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ فَأَنْشَأَ اللَّهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى سَحَابَةٌ فَرَعَدَتْ وَبَرَقَتْ، ثُمَّ أَمْطَرَتْ بِإِذْنِ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، فَلَمْ يَأْتِ عليه الصلاة والسلام مَسْجِدَهُ حَتَّى سَالَتْ السُّيُولُ ، فَلَمَّا رَأى سُرْعَتَهُمْ إِلَى السَّكَنِّ ضَحِكَ حَتَّى بَدَتْ نَوَاجِدُهُ، فَقَالَ: أَشْهَدُ أَنَّ اللَّهَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ، وَأَنِّي عَبْدُ اللَّهِ وَرَسُولُهُ ، انتهى. (ولا يحضره ) أي : الاستسقاء ( ذِمّي) لنهي عمره، ولأن المقصود هو الدعاء، ومـا دعــاء الكافرين إلا في ضلال، ولأنه بالخروج تستنزل الرحمة، وإنما تنزل عليهم اللعنة، وإن جاز أن يقال : يستجاب دعاء الكافر كما في ( الخانية » ، وفي ( الدراية لا يُمنع أهل الذمة مـن ذلـك فلعل الله يستجيب دعاءهم استعجالاً لحظهم في الدنيا، وقال الكمال: لا يمكنون من أن يستسقوا وحدهم، لاحتمال أن يسقوا فقد يفتن به ضعفاء العوام والله أعلم.
And a dhimmi does not attend it. Sunan Abi Dawood from Aisha: The people complained to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about the lack of rain, so he ordered a pulpit to be placed for him in the prayer ground and appointed a day for the people to go out. He came out when the sun's edge appeared, sat on the pulpit, glorified Allah, praised Him, then said: 'You have complained of the drought of your lands and the delay of rain from its time. Allah has commanded you to call upon Him and promised to respond to you.' Then he said: 'Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, King of the Day of Judgment. There is no god but Allah, He does what He wills. O Allah, You are Allah, there is no god but You, the Self-Sufficient, and we are the needy. Send down rain upon us, and make what You send down a strength and a provision for a time.' Then he raised his hands, and he continued raising them until the whiteness of his armpits appeared. Then he turned his back to the people and turned his cloak while raising his hands. Then he faced the people, came down from the pulpit, and prayed two rak'ahs. Then Allah created a cloud, it thundered and lightened, then it rained by Allah's permission. Before he reached his mosque, the floods were flowing. When he saw their haste to take shelter, he laughed until his back teeth became visible and said: 'I testify that Allah is over all things Capable, and that I am Allah's servant and His Messenger.' End. (And he does not attend it) i.e., the prayer for rain (a dhimmi) due to Umar's prohibition, and because the purpose is supplication, and the supplication of disbelievers is but in vain, and because by going out mercy is sought to descend, and upon them only curses descend, even though it is said that the supplication of a disbeliever may be answered as in al-Khaniyyah, and in al-Dirayah: the dhimmis are not prevented from that, perhaps Allah will answer their supplication as a hastening of their portion in this world. And al-Kamal said: They should not be allowed to pray for rain by themselves, because if they are given rain, the weak commoners might be tempted. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling that a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject) must not attend the salat al-istisqa' (prayer for rain). The author then provides the proof through a lengthy hadith from Abu Dawood describing the Prophet's ﷺ istisqa'. After the hadith, the commentary explains the reasoning: Umar's prohibition, the nature of the prayer as supplication (which is futile from disbelievers, per Qur'an 40:50), and the fact that the congregation seeks the descent of mercy, whereas upon disbelievers, only curses descend. However, the commentary also acknowledges a dissenting view that dhimmis might be allowed, citing that their supplication could be answered as a hastening of their worldly portion. The final word from al-Kamal is that dhimmis should not be allowed to hold their own istisqa' due to the risk of fitna (temptation) for common Muslims. The lesson type is ruling with proof, and the argument is based on hadith and rational reasoning.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state who pays jizyah and is protected.
استسقاء (istisqā'): The prayer for rain, a sunnah performed in times of drought.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are dhimmis prohibited from attending the prayer for rain according to the commentary?
A) Because they are unclean.
B) Because their supplication is not accepted.
C) Because they might cause fitnah.
D) Because they do not believe in the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits dhimmis from attending salat al-istisqa' because their supplication is not accepted and the prayer is specifically for seeking mercy on believers.

Conditions for Permissibility of Salat al-Khawf
States conditions for fear prayer permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that make Salat al-Khawf permissible and explain why intense fear is not required according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Presence of enemy or danger suffices for the fear prayer; intense fear is not required.

This lesson examines the conditions that make the fear prayer permissible. The Hanafi school takes a lenient view, considering the mere presence of an enemy or a dangerous animal as sufficient cause, without requiring intense fear. The text also extends the concession to fear of drowning or burning. We will unpack the precise conditions and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Salat al-Khawf (fear prayer). Its ruling is permissible (ja'izah) under specific conditions, not an independent obligatory prayer.
It is a concession for performing obligatory prayers in dangerous situations.
2
List the conditions stated in the text
The base text lists: 1) presence of an enemy ('aduww), 2) presence of a beast (sabu'), 3) fear of drowning (gharaq), 4) fear of burning (harq).
These are the specific causes (asbab) that permit the prayer.
3
Analyze the key clarification
The commentator emphasizes that intense fear (ishtidād al-khawf) is NOT a condition. The mere presence of the enemy or beast is sufficient. This is the position of the majority of Hanafi scholars.
This distinction prevents unnecessary delay or restriction.
4
Understand the cause vs. condition distinction
The presence of enemy is both a cause (sabab) for the license and a condition (shart) for its application, depending on perspective. The text adds that the thing may be both cause and condition from two considerations.
This nuance helps in legal reasoning (takhrij).
5
Note the evidence from practice
The commentator cites that Ali (RA), Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and others performed it, establishing its legitimacy in early battles.
This historical evidence supports the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الخوف. هي جائزة بحضور عدو، أو سبع، وبخوف غرق، أو حرق. هذا من إضافة الشيء إلى شرطه، كذا في «الجوهرة»، وقال الكمال: حضرة العدو سبب الرخصة انتهى، فيكون من إضافة الشيء إلى سببه وقد يكون الشيء سبباً وشرطاً باعتبارين. و(هي) أي: صلاة الخوف بالصفة الآتية (جائزة بحضور عدو) لوجود المبيح للأفعال المنهي عنها في غيرها، وهو حضور العدو، فلذا لم يقل: إذا اشتد الخوف لأنه ليس بشرط لما قال الكمال قوله: أي: «الهداية» «كالكنز»: إذا اشتد الخوف، اشتداده ليس بشرط، بل الشرط حضور عدو (أو سبع) انتهى. وقال في «العناية»: ليس الاشتداد شرطاً عند عامة مشايخنا انتهى. وقال الكمال: روي أن عليا له صلاها يوم صفين، وصلاها أبو موسى الأشعري بأصبهان، وسعد بن أبي وقاص في حرب بطبرستان، ومعه الحسن بن علي، وحذيفة بن اليمان وعبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص وسألها سعيد بن العاص أبا سعيد الخدري فعلمه فأقامها. (و) جائزة أيضاً (بخوف غرق) من سيل، (أو حرق) لوجود سبب الرخصة.
Chapter of Salat al-Khawf: It is permissible in the presence of an enemy, or a beast, and due to fear of drowning or burning. This is from adding the thing to its condition, as in Al-Jawhara. Al-Kamal said: The presence of the enemy is the cause of the concession. So it is from adding the thing to its cause, and a thing may be a cause and a condition from two perspectives. 'It' i.e. Salat al-Khawf in the following description is permissible in the presence of an enemy due to the existence of what permits actions that are prohibited otherwise, which is the presence of the enemy. Hence he did not say: if fear becomes intense, because intensity is not a condition. As Al-Kamal said: intensity is not a condition, rather the condition is the presence of an enemy or a beast. And in Al-Inayah: intensity is not a condition according to the generality of our scholars. Al-Kamal said: It is narrated that Ali prayed it on the day of Siffin, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari prayed it in Isfahan, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas in the war of Tabaristan, with him al-Hasan ibn Ali, Hudhayfah ibn al-Yaman, and Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As. Sa'id ibn al-As asked Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and he taught him, so he performed it. And it is also permissible due to fear of drowning from a flood, or burning, due to the existence of the cause of the concession.
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh begins the chapter on the Fear Prayer. It first establishes the conditions that make the fear prayer permissible. The base text states that it is permissible with the presence of an enemy, a predator, or fear of drowning or burning. The commentator explains that the presence of the enemy is the cause (sabab) that permits normally prohibited actions in prayer, such as moving or speaking out of necessity. He clarifies, citing Al-Kamal, that severe fear (ishtidād al-khawf) is not a condition; rather, the mere presence of the enemy or a dangerous beast is sufficient. This is the position of the generality of Hanafi scholars, as noted from Al-‘Ināyah. The commentator then reports historical instances where the Companions performed the fear prayer, including Ali at Siffin, Abu Musa in Isfahan, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas with notable Companions. This demonstrates the established practice. Finally, the text reiterates that the concession also applies to fear of drowning or fire, as these too are valid causes.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salāt al-khawf): The fear prayer, a special form of prayer performed during battle or when facing danger, as described in the text.
ثنائية (thunā'iyyah): A two-rak'ah prayer, such as Fajr or a shortened prayer during travel.
رباعية (rubā'iyyah): A four-rak'ah prayer, such as Zuhr, Asr, and Isha.
مغرب (maghrib): The sunset prayer, which is three rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, what is the minimum condition for the permissibility of Salat al-Khawf?
A) Intense fear of death
B) Presence of an enemy or a dangerous beast
C) Actual combat taking place
D) Permission from the Imam

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf is permissible with the presence of an enemy, beast, or fear of drowning/fire; intense fear is not a condition.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Standard Hanafi Method of Salat al-Khawf with Two Groups
Describes the Hanafi procedure for the fear prayer with two groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the step-by-step procedure of the Hanafi fear prayer with two groups, distinguishing between the rulings for the first and second groups, and identify the correct application for two-rak'ah, four-rak'ah, and Maghrib prayers.

Core Idea
In the fear prayer, the Imam leads each group separately; the first group prays partially then guards, the second completes with the Imam, and the first later finishes without recitation.

The fear prayer (Salat al-Khawf) is a concession during battle. The Hanafi method, based on a narration of Ibn Mas'ud, involves dividing the congregation into two groups and praying in a staggered manner. This lesson details the standard procedure for different prayer lengths and clarifies the status of lahiq and masbuq followers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer type
Determine if the prayer has two rak'ahs (Fajr or qasr), four rak'ahs (Zuhr, Asr, Isha), or three (Maghrib). The number of rak'ahs the Imam prays with the first group depends on this.
For two-rak'ah prayers, the first group prays one rak'ah; for four or three, they pray two rak'ahs.
2
Divide the congregation into two groups
The Imam splits the congregation: one group stands facing the enemy for protection, the other prays with the Imam.
The group facing the enemy must be positioned such that they can guard the prayer.
3
First group prays with the Imam
The Imam leads the first group in the specified number of rak'ahs (one or two). After completing those rak'ahs, the first group does not make salam; they stand and then go to the enemy position walking.
They do not recite in subsequent rak'ahs when they rejoin because they are lahiqun.
4
Second group joins the Imam
The second group, which was guarding, now comes and begins their prayer with the Imam, reciting takbir. The Imam leads them in the remaining rak'ahs of his prayer.
If it is a two-rak'ah prayer, the second group prays one rak'ah with the Imam; if four, they pray two.
5
Imam completes his prayer and says salam alone
After finishing the second group's prayer, the Imam's own prayer is complete. He says salam by himself, as his prayer is complete.
The second group does not say salam with the Imam; they have missed some rak'ahs.
6
First group returns and completes their prayer without recitation
The first group (lahiqun) returns after the Imam has finished. They complete the remaining rak'ahs without recitation (no Fatiha or sura), because they are considered followers who missed part of the Imam's prayer.
They are lahiqun: they caught the beginning of the Imam's prayer but are now making up the end.
7
Second group completes their prayer with recitation
The second group (masbuqun) missed the first part of the Imam's prayer. They now stand and complete the missed rak'ahs on their own, reciting Fatiha and a sura.
They are masbuqun: they missed the beginning and must make it up with recitation.
8
Apply the principle of departure and return
The text discusses invalidation if the first group departs at the wrong time. Only if they depart at the proper time (after their assigned rak'ahs) is it valid. If they depart early or late incorrectly, the prayer may be invalid.
The principle: one who departs at the time of sitting (remaining) invalidates; one who returns at the time of departure does not invalidate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم شرع في بيان كيفيتها فقال: (وإذا تنازع القومُ في الصَّلاةِ خلف إمام واحدٍ فيجعلهم طائفتين)، يقيم (واحدةً بإزاء) أي مقابل: (العدو) للحراسة، (ويصلي) الإمام ( بـ) الطائفة ( الأخرى ركعة من الصلاة ) ( الثنائية ) الصبح والمقصورة بالسفر، (و) صلى بالأولى المذكورة (ركعتين من الرباعية، أو المغرب لأنه شرط الشفع لشطرها، ولذا شرع القعود عقبه، والواحدة لا تتجزئ، فكانت الطائفة الأولى [ أولى بها للسبق ] والركعة الثانية كالأولى حكماً، ولو أخطأ فصلى بالأولى ركعة من المغرب، وبالثانية ركعتين فسدت صلاتهما، لانصراف كل في غير أوانه، لأن الأولى انصرافها واضح قبل أوانه، والثانية لما أدركوا الركعة الثانية صاروا من الطائفة الأولى وقد انصرفوا في أوان رجوعهم فتبطل، والأصل فيه أن من انصرف في أوان القعود أي: البقاء تبطل صلاته، وإن عاد في أوان الانصراف لا تبطل صلاته لأنه مقبل، والأول معرض، فلا يعذر إلا في المنصوص عليه، وهو الانصراف في أوانه، وإن أخر الانصراف ثم انصرف قبل أوان عوده. (وَتَمْضِي هَذِهِ إلى العَدُوِّ، مُشاةَ) قيد به لأنها تبطل بالركوب كالعمل الكثير غير المشي لا القليل، كالرمية عن القوس لعدم الحاجة إليه، بخلاف المشي لضرورة الاصطفاف، والقيام بإزاء العدو، فما وقع في عدة من الكتب أنها تبطل بالمشي مؤول بافتتاحها ماشياً هارباً من العدو، أو المشي فيها لغير إرادة الاصطفاف بمقابلة العدو، وجاءت تلك الطائفة التي كانت في الحراسة، فأحرموا مع الإمام، فصلى بهم ما بَقِي من الصلاة ، ( وسلَّمَ) الإمام (وحده) لتمام صلاته، ( فذهبوا إلى) جهة ( العدو) مشاة، (ثُمَّ جاءتِ) الطائفة (الأولى) إن شاؤوا، (وَ) إن أرادوا (أَتموا) في مكانهم ( بلا قراءة)، لأنهم لاحقون، فهم خلف الإمام حكماً، فلا يقرؤون (وسلَّمُوا، وَمَضَوْا) إلى العدو، ( ثم جاءت) الطائفة ( الأخرى إن شاؤوا صلوا ما بَقِي) في مكانهم لفراغ الإمام، ويقضون ( بقراءة) فيما فاتهم، لأنهم مسبوقون والأصل فيه رواية ابن مسعود له أن النبي صلى صلاة الخوف على الصفة التي ذكرناها واعلم أنه ورد في صلاة الخوف روايات كثيرة، وأصحها ست عشرة رواية، وصلاها النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أربعاً وعشرين مرة، كذا في شرح المقدسي». واختلف العلماء في كيفيتها: وفي « المستصفى عن شرح أبي نصر البغدادي : أن كل ذلك جائز، والكلام في الأولى والأقرب من ظاهر القرآن، وهو الوجه الذي ذكرناه عندنا ( وإن اشتد الخوفُ) فلم يتهيأ لهم النزول عن الدواب والقيام للصلاة بالهجوم عليهم، (صَلَّوْا رُكباناً))، ولو مع السير مطلوبين بإجماع أهل العلم، فالراكب إن كان طالباً لا تجوز صلاته على الدابة لعدم ضرورة الخوف في حقه فينزل ، وقال الشافعي: إلا أن يكون بحال يخاف فوت المطلوب وذهبه حيث لا يعلم، حينئذ للصلاة.
Then he began to explain its method, saying: 'When the people disagree about praying behind one Imam, he makes them two groups, placing one group facing the enemy for protection, and he prays with the other group one rak'ah of a two-rak'ah prayer (Fajr or shortened travel prayer), and he prayed with the first mentioned group two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, or Maghrib because he is the condition for the even number for its half, and therefore sitting after it is prescribed, and the one rak'ah is not divisible, so the first group is more entitled to it due to precedence, and the second rak'ah is like the first in ruling. If he errs and prays with the first one rak'ah of Maghrib and with the second two rak'ahs, both their prayers become invalid because each departed at other than its proper time. For the first group departed clearly before their time, and the second when they caught the second rak'ah they became like the first group and had departed at the time of their return, so it becomes invalid. The principle is that whoever departs at the time of sitting (i.e., remaining) invalidates his prayer, and if he returns at the time of departure his prayer is not invalidated because he is facing, while the first is turning away, so he is not excused except in what is textually prescribed, which is departure at its proper time. And if he delays departure then departs before the time of his return... And this group goes to the enemy walking,' he conditioned it because it is invalidated by riding as much action that is not walking, not a little, like shooting an arrow because there is no need for it, unlike walking due to the necessity of lining up and standing facing the enemy. What occurs in several books that it is invalidated by walking is interpreted as starting while walking fleeing from the enemy, or walking in it without intending to line up facing the enemy. Then that group that was guarding came, and they began with the Imam, and he prayed with them what remained of the prayer, and the Imam made salam alone because his prayer was complete. Then they went to the enemy walking. Then the first group came, if they wished, they completed in their place without recitation because they are lahiqun, so they are behind the Imam in ruling, so they do not recite. And they made salam and proceeded to the enemy. Then the other group came, if they wished they prayed what remained in their place because the Imam had finished, and they make up with recitation for what they missed because they are masbuqun. The basis for this is the narration of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet prayed the fear prayer in the manner we mentioned. Know that many narrations have come about the fear prayer, the most authentic being sixteen narrations, and the Prophet prayed it twenty-four times, as in Sharh al-Maqdisi. The scholars differed about its method. In al-Mustasfa from Sharh Abi Nasr al-Baghdadi: all of that is permissible. The discussion is about the first and the closest to the apparent meaning of the Quran, which is the method we mentioned according to us. And if fear becomes severe, so they cannot dismount from their animals and stand for prayer due to the attack upon them, they pray while riding, even if being pursued, by consensus of the scholars. So the rider, if he is the pursuer, his prayer on the animal is not permissible because there is no necessity of fear in his case, so he must dismount. Al-Shafi'i said: except if he is in a state where he fears losing the pursued and his escape where he does not know, then at that time for prayer...
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage details the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf. The Imam divides the people into two groups: one group faces the enemy while the other prays with the Imam. For a two-rak'ah prayer (Fajr or travel qasr), the Imam leads the first group in one rak'ah. For a four-rak'ah prayer or Maghrib, he leads the first group in two rak'ahs. The first group then goes to the enemy position, and the second group comes and prays the remaining rak'ahs with the Imam. The Imam does tashahhud after the first two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer. After the Imam finishes, he says salam alone. The first group returns and completes their prayer without recitation (as they are lahiqun, followers behind the Imam). The second group completes their prayer with recitation (as they are masbuqun, having missed some rak'ahs). The commentator discusses the ruling if the Imam makes a mistake in assigning rak'ahs, and explains the principle regarding departure and return. He also addresses the requirement of walking (not riding) when moving to the enemy, and the permissibility of walking for necessity. Finally, he covers the case of extreme fear where prayer is offered while riding, with the condition that it is only allowed for those being pursued, not for the pursuer. He notes a difference with al-Shafi'i regarding the pursuer's fear of losing the quarry.

Key Terms
لاحق (lāḥiq): A latecomer to prayer who joins the Imam after the first rak'ah but is still considered behind the Imam in ruling; he does not recite in the remaining rak'ahs.
مسبوق (masbūq): One who misses part of the prayer with the Imam and must make it up with recitation.
طائفة (ṭā'ifah): A group or section of the congregation in the fear prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi method, what do the first group (lahiqun) do when they return to complete their prayer after the Imam has finished?
A) They recite al-Fatiha and a sura in their remaining rak'ahs
B) They complete their remaining rak'ahs without recitation
C) They wait for the second group to finish and then follow them
D) They join the second group and pray together

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi fear prayer, the first group (lahiqun) complete their missed rak'ahs without recitation, while the second group (masbuqun) complete with recitation.

Salah — Prayer

Special Rulings in Salat al-Khawf: Mistakes, Walking vs Riding, and Extreme Fear
Discusses special cases and rulings in the fear prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for common mistakes in rak'ah distribution, identify conditions for walking versus riding, and explain the rule for praying in extreme fear when riding, including the exception for the pursuer.

Core Idea
A mistake in rak'ah assignment invalidates both groups; walking is required for movement, but extreme fear permits riding, though not for the pursuer.

The fear prayer has special rulings that differ from normal prayer. The text addresses what happens if the Imam mistakenly assigns the wrong number of rak'ahs to the first group, whether walking is obligatory when moving to the enemy, and how to pray when fear becomes so severe that riding is necessary. These details ensure the prayer remains valid in the most difficult circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the mistake in rak'ah distribution
If the Imam gives the first group one rak'ah of Maghrib (instead of two) and the second group two rak'ahs, both prayers become invalid. The first group left before their proper time, and the second group, upon catching the second rak'ah, became like the first group and left at the wrong time.
The principle: departure at the time of sitting (i.e., when one should remain) invalidates; return at the time of departure does not invalidate.
2
Understand the walking requirement
When moving to the enemy, the group must walk. Riding would invalidate the prayer because it is excessive movement not required. However, walking for the necessities of lining up and facing the enemy is permissible.
Some books suggest walking invalidates, but that is interpreted as starting the prayer while walking fleeing the enemy, or walking without the intention of facing the enemy.
3
Identify the ruling for extreme fear
If fear is so severe that one cannot dismount and stand, the prayer may be offered while riding, even if being pursued, by consensus. The rider who is the pursuer (attacker) cannot pray on the animal because there is no necessity; he must dismount.
Al-Shafi'i made an exception for the pursuer if he fears losing the quarry.

Source Text

Salah — Prayer

Salat al-Khawf in Moderate Fear: The Two-Group Rotation
Describes the method of prayer when fear is moderate, with two groups rotating.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf in moderate fear, explain the roles of lahiq and masbuq, and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
In moderate fear, Salat al-Khawf uses two rotating groups: lahiqun do not recite, masbuqun recite in their missed rak'ahs.

This lesson details the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf (prayer of fear) when fear is moderate. You will learn how the prayer is performed with two groups rotating, the distinction between lahiq and masbuq, and the evidence from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ. The passage also addresses common objections about walking during the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Recognize that Salat al-Khawf is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) when the condition of fear is present. The passage describes the specific method for moderate fear.
Hanafis emphasize that this method is closest to the Quranic verse (4:102) and the Prophet's practice.
2
Trace the rotation sequence
Follow the two-group rotation: first group prays one rak'ah with imam, then walks to face enemy. Second group prays remaining rak'ahs with imam, imam says salam. First group completes without recitation (lahiqun), second group completes with recitation (masbuqun).
Walking is permissible due to necessity; riding would invalidate as 'much action'.
3
Understand the lahiq vs masbuq distinction
The first group is lahiqun: they are considered behind the imam in ruling and do not recite when completing. The second group is masbuqun: they make up missed rak'ahs with recitation.
In Hanafi fiqh, a lahiq joins after the imam has started but catches up within the same rak'ah, while a masbuq misses one or more rak'ahs.
4
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (Sunan Abi Dawud 1244) describing the Prophet's practice. The passage cites this as the origin of the method.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalalah).
5
Note the ikhtilaf and Hanafi tarjih
The passage states that sixteen authentic narrations exist on Salat al-Khawf, and scholars differed. The Hanafi position is that this method is the closest to the apparent meaning of the Qur'an and the most sound.
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) have different methods, but the Hanafi view is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَتَمْضِي هَذِهِ إلى العَدُوِّ، مُشاةَ، وَجَاءَتْ تِلْكَ، فَصَلَّى بِهِمْ مَا بَقِيَ، وَسَلَّمَ وَحدَهُ، فَذَهَبُوا إِلَى العَدُو، ثُمَّ جاءت الأولى، وَأَتُوا بِلا قِرَاءَةِ، وَسَلِّمُوا، وَمَضَوْا، ثمَّ جَاءَتْ الأخرى، إنْ شَاؤُوا صَلُّوا مَا بَقِيَ بقراءةٍ. صح، لأنه أوان انصرافه ما لم يجئ أوان عوده، كما في التبيين و الفتح. (وتمضي هذه) الطائفة (إلى) جهة ( العدو مشاةً)، قيد به لأنها تبطل بالركوب كالعمل الكثير لا القليل، كالرمية عن القوس لعدم الحاجة إليه، بخلاف المشي لضرورة الاصطفاف، والقيام بإزاء العدو، فما وقع في عدة من الكتب أنها تبطل بالمشي مؤول بافتتاحها ماشياً هارباً من العدو، أو المشي فيها لغير إرادة الاصطفاف بمقابلة العدو، وجاءت تلك الطائفة التي كانت في الحراسة، فأحرموا مع الإمام، فصلى بهم ما بقي من الصلاة وسلَّمَ الإمام وحده لتمام صلاته، فذهبوا إلى جهة العدو مشاة، ثم جاءت الطائفة الأولى إن شاؤوا، وإن أرادوا أتموا في مكانهم بلا قراءة، لأنهم لاحقون، فهم خلف الإمام حكماً، فلا يقرؤون وسلَّمُوا، وَمَضَوْا إلى العدو، ثم جاءت الطائفة الأخرى إن شاؤوا صلوا ما بقي في مكانهم لفراغ الإمام، ويقضون بقراءة فيما فاتهم، لأنهم مسبوقون والأصل فيه رواية ابن مسعود له أن النبي صلى صلاة الخوف على الصفة التي ذكرناها. واعلم أنه ورد في صلاة الخوف روايات كثيرة، وأصحها ست عشرة رواية، وصلاها النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أربعاً وعشرين مرة، كذا في شرح المقدسي. واختلف العلماء في كيفيتها: وفي المستصفى عن شرح أبي نصر البغدادي : أن كل ذلك جائز، والكلام في الأولى والأقرب من ظاهر القرآن، وهو الوجه الذي ذكرناه عندنا
And this group goes towards the enemy, walking, and that group came, so he (the imam) prayed with them what remained, and he said the salam alone, so they went to the enemy, then the first group came, and they completed without recitation, and they said salam, and they went, then the other group came, if they wish they pray what remained with recitation. Correct, because it is the time of his departure as long as the time of his return has not come, as in al-Tabyin and al-Fath. (And this group goes) to the direction of the enemy walking – restricted by this because it is invalidated by riding as it is much action, not little, like shooting an arrow due to lack of need, contrary to walking due to the necessity of forming ranks and standing opposite the enemy. What occurs in several books that it is invalidated by walking is interpreted as one who begins it walking while fleeing from the enemy, or walking in it without intending to form ranks facing the enemy. And that group which was in guarding came, so they entered ihram with the imam, and he prayed with them what remained of the prayer, and the imam said salam alone because his prayer was complete, so they went to the direction of the enemy walking, then the first group came, if they wish, and if they want, they complete in their place without recitation because they are lahiqun (followers in effect), so they are behind the imam in ruling, so they do not recite, and they say salam, and they go to the enemy, then the other group came, if they wish they pray what remained in their place because the imam has finished, and they make up with recitation for what they missed because they are masbuqun (caught up after the imam). The origin of this is the narration of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet ﷺ prayed salat al-khawf in the manner we mentioned. Know that many narrations have been reported about salat al-khawf, the most authentic of which are sixteen, and the Prophet ﷺ prayed it twenty-four times – as in Sharh al-Maqdisi. And the scholars differed as to its modality. In al-Mustasfa from Sharh Abi Nasr al-Baghdadi: that all of that is permissible, and the discussion is about the first and the closest to the apparent meaning of the Qur'an, and that is the method we mentioned according to us.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof describing the method of Salat al-Khawf (prayer of fear) in moderate fear according to the Hanafi school. The text explains the rotation of two groups: one group prays one rak'ah with the imam, then goes to face the enemy walking. The other group then comes and prays the remaining rak'ahs with the imam, who completes his prayer and says salam alone. The first group, having already prayed one rak'ah with the imam, completes the rest without recitation because they are considered 'lahiqun' (followers in effect) and do not recite behind the imam. The second group completes their missed rak'ahs with recitation because they are 'masbuqun' (catching up). The commentary emphasizes that walking is permissible due to necessity, while riding would invalidate the prayer because it is a much action. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud describing the Prophet's practice. The passage also notes that the most authentic narrations on salat al-khawf are sixteen, and the Prophet performed it twenty-four times. The Hanafi position is that this method is the closest to the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse (4:102).

Key Terms
لاحق (lāḥiq): A person who joins the prayer after the imam has started but catches up with the imam in the same rak'ah, or joins after the imam has already prayed a portion.
مسبوق (masbūq): A person who misses one or more rak'ahs with the imam and must complete them after the imam's salam.
صلاة الخوف (ṣalāt al-khawf): The specific form of congregational prayer performed during battle or when there is fear of enemy attack.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the first group (lahiqun) not recite when completing their prayer after the imam's salam?
A) Because they are considered behind the imam in ruling and thus do not recite.
B) Because they missed the entire prayer and must repeat it.
C) Because recitation is not required in any situation of fear.
D) Because they are walking and cannot recite.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf in moderate fear is a sunnah performed with two rotating groups, where the first group (lahiqun) completes without recitation and the second (masbuqun) recites in their missed rak'ahs.

Prayer While Riding During Intense Fear
Ruling for prayer when fear is intense, allowing riding and gestures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying while riding during intense fear and distinguish between the positions of the pursuer and the pursued.

Core Idea
If you are fleeing, pray on horseback with gestures; if chasing, get down and pray properly.

When fear reaches a level where dismounting from your mount is impossible due to enemy attack, the Hanafi school permits prayer while riding. This lesson explores the conditions, the key distinction between being pursued (the one who needs the concession) and pursuing, and the limits of the concession. The passage also contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i and provides practical guidance for such extreme situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing salah while riding an animal. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) when fear is intense and the person is being pursued (matlub). Note that the pursuer (talib) must dismount.
The permissibility is conditional upon necessity.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the Quranic verse: 'فَإِنْ خِفْتُمْ فَرِجَالاً أَوْ رُكْبَاناً' (If you fear, then (pray) on foot or riding). This verse gives general permission for prayer in a state of fear, including riding.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah in its application to riding.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'رُكْبَاناً' (riding) indicates that prayer while mounted is allowed. The Hanafi school understands this as a concession when fear prevents normal prayer (standing, bowing, prostrating). The verse does not specify direction or congregation, allowing gestures and any direction.
The concession is restricted to those who are in genuine danger.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Imam al-Shafi'i allows the pursuer (talib) to also pray while riding if he fears losing the target. The Hanafi school rejects this because the pursuer is not in immediate danger; he can dismount without losing the enemy.
The Shafi'i position is that fear of losing the quarry is a valid necessity.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school is that the pursuer must dismount and pray normally. The permissibility for the pursued is based on necessity and consensus (ijma'). The text also provides further conditions: the enemy must be present, and if mistaken, the followers' prayer is invalid but the imam's is valid.
The text also discusses scenarios of the enemy appearing/disappearing during prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنِ اشتد الخوفُ فلم يتهيأ لهم النزول عن الدواب والقيام للصلاة بالهجوم عليهم، صَلَّوْا رُكباناً، ولو مع السير مطلوبين بإجماع أهل العلم، فالراكب إن كان طالباً لا تجوز صلاته على الدابة لعدم ضرورة الخوف في حقه فينزل، وقال الشافعي: إلا أن يكون بحال يخاف فوت المطلوب وذهـا بـه حيث لا يعلم، حينئذٍ تجوز صلاته راكباً، وإن كان مطلوباً فلا بأس بأن يصلي وهو سائر، لأنه فعل الدابة حقيقة، وإنمـا أُضيف إليه معنى التسيير، وإذا جاء العذر انقطعت الإضافة إليه، بخلاف ما لو صلى وهو يمشي، حيث لا يجوز، لأن المشي فعله حقيقة وهو مناف للصلاة، كما في مجمع الروايات. فُــرادى بالإيماء، إلى أيّ جهةٍ قَدَرُوا إذ لا يصح الاقتداء؛ لاختلاف المكان حال الركوب، ولذا صح الاقتداء إذا كان الإمام والمقتدي به على دابة واحدة، كما لو كانا على خشبة، والغريق السابح كالماشي لا تجوز صلاته، لأن السباحة كالمشي عمل كثير. ولم تَجُزْ صلاة الخوف بلا حضور عدو، فلو رأوا سواداً ظنـوه عـدواً صلوها، فإن تبين كما ظنوا جازت لتبين سبب الرخصة، وإن ظهر خلافه لم تجز صلاة القوم، وأمـا صـلاة الإمام فصحيحة بكل حال، لعدم المفسد في حقه، إلا إذا تبين للطائفة الأولى غير ما ظنوه قبل أن تتجاوز الصفوف، فإن لهم البناء استحساناً، كمن انصرف على ظن الحدث، يتوقف الفساد إذا ظهر أنه لم يحدث على مجاوزة الصفوف في الصحراء. ولو شرعوا بحضرة العدو فذهب لا يجوز لهم الانحراف والانصراف لزوال سبب الرخصة، ولو شرعوا في صلاتهم ثم حضر ، جاز الانحراف لوجود المبيح، وهذا يفيد بطلان الصلاة، لزوال المبيح قبيل السَّلام على مقتضى المسائل الاثني عشرية، ويشمله زوال عذر المعذور كذا في الفتح.
And if fear becomes intense so that they cannot dismount from animals and stand for prayer due to the enemy's onslaught, they may pray while riding, even while moving if they are being pursued, by consensus of the scholars. As for the rider, if he is pursuing (the enemy), his prayer on the animal is not permissible because there is no necessity of fear in his case, so he must dismount. Al-Shafi'i said: Except if he is in a state where he fears losing the pursued and his going away where he does not know, then his prayer while riding is permissible. And if he is being pursued, there is no harm in his praying while moving, because the movement is actually that of the animal, and the meaning of moving is attributed to him, but when the excuse appears, the attribution ceases; unlike if he prays while walking, which is not permissible because walking is his own action and is contrary to the prayer, as in Majma' al-Riwayat. (They pray) individually with gestures, towards any direction they are able, because following (the imam) is not valid due to difference of location while riding; therefore following is valid if the imam and the follower are on the same animal, as if they were on a plank. And a drowning person swimming is like a walker; his prayer is not permissible because swimming is like walking, a much action. And salat al-khawf is not permissible without the presence of an enemy. If they see a dark mass and think it is the enemy and pray, if it becomes clear as they thought, it is permissible because the reason for the concession is confirmed, but if it turns out otherwise, the people's prayer is not valid. As for the imam's prayer, it is valid in any case because there is no nullifier on his part, except if it becomes clear to the first group otherwise before they pass the rows, then they may build upon (what they did) by istihsan, like one who leaves due to thinking he has broken wudu; nullification depends on passing the rows in the desert. And if they begin (the prayer) in the presence of the enemy and then he goes away, they are not allowed to deviate and leave because the reason for the concession has ceased. And if they begin their prayer and then the enemy comes, deviation is permissible because the permitting factor exists, and this implies the invalidity of the prayer because the permitting factor ceased before the salam, according to the twelve issues, and it includes the cessation of the excuse of the excused one, as in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage details the rulings for Salat al-Khawf when fear is intense. The text establishes that when fear is so severe that one cannot dismount, prayer is allowed while riding, even while moving if being pursued. A crucial distinction is made: if the rider is pursuing the enemy, there is no necessity for riding, so he must dismount and pray normally. However, if he is being pursued, riding is necessary and prayer is permissible. The commentary contrasts this with walking, which is not allowed because walking is a human action that conflicts with the prayer's requirements. The prayer is performed individually with gestures (i.e., bowing and prostrating with head movements) facing any direction possible, as congregation is not valid due to differing positions on mounts. The text also specifies conditions: the prayer is not permissible without the actual presence of the enemy. If they mistakenly think a black mass is the enemy, their prayer is valid only if it turns out to indeed be the enemy. The imam's prayer is always valid unless the first group realizes their mistake before passing through the ranks, in which case they may continue by istihsan. The text discusses scenarios where the enemy appears or disappears during prayer, affecting whether one may deviate from the normal prayer. According to the twelve issues, if the reason for the concession ceases before salam, the prayer becomes invalid.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmā'): Gestures with the head or body indicating ruku' and sujud when one cannot perform them normally due to fear or riding.
رُكباناً (rukbānan): Praying while riding on an animal (e.g., horse, camel) without dismounting.
مطلوب (maṭlūb): One who is being pursued by the enemy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when fear is intense, a person being pursued may pray while riding. However, what is the ruling for a pursuer?
A) Permissible, like the pursued.
B) Not permissible; he must dismount.
C) Permissible only if he also fears death.
D) Permissible only if he is on foot.

Key Takeaway
If you are being pursued, pray on horseback with gestures; if you are the pursuer, dismount and pray normally.

Salat al-Khawf: Carrying Weapons and Separate Imams
Rulings on carrying weapons and separate imams in Salat al-Khawf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on carrying weapons and preferring separate imams during Salat al-Khawf, distinguish them from opposing positions, and apply them to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
Carrying arms in fear prayer is recommended, not required; separate imams avoid extra movement.

This lesson clarifies two subsidiary rulings for Salat al-Khawf: whether to carry weapons and whether to have one imam or separate imams. The Hanafi school adopts a recommended (mustahabb) ruling for weapons and prefers separate imams when there is no dispute. Understanding these rulings requires attention to the school's method of interpreting commands and the underlying rationale of minimizing non-prayer movements.

Guided Path
1
Extract the two rulings
Identify the two distinct rulings in the passage: (1) carrying weapons during prayer in fear, (2) preference for separate imams if there is no dispute.
These are independent but both concern Salat al-Khawf.
2
Identify the legal status (hukm) for each
Note that carrying weapons is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. Separate imams is afdal (better), not obligatory.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between fard, wajib, sunnah, mustahabb, etc.
3
Contrast with opposing schools
Recognize that Shafi'i and Maliki consider carrying weapons wajib (obligatory) based on the apparent command in Quran 4:102. Hanafi interprets it as nadb (recommendation) because carrying weapons is not an act of worship.
This is a classic example of usul al-fiqh difference in interpreting amr.
4
Apply the rulings to a scenario
Consider a group of armed security guards praying Salat al-Khawf. According to Hanafi, they are not obliged to carry weapons, but it is recommended. If they agree, each subgroup should pray with its own imam to avoid walking.
The practical thamarah al-khilaf is that one does not sin if weapons are left aside.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُستحبُّ حَمْلُ السَّلاحِ في الصَّلاةِ عند الخوف. وإنْ لم يَتَنَازَعُوا في الصَّلاةِ خلف إمام واحد، فالأفضل صلاةُ كلِّ طائفة بإمام، مثل حالة الأمن، للتوقي عن المشي ونحوه، كذا في فتح القدير.
And it is recommended to carry weapons in prayer during fear. And if they do not dispute (i.e., the people agree) on praying behind one imam, then it is better for each group to pray with its own imam, like the case of security, to avoid walking and the like. As in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage outlines two subsidiary rulings for Salat al-Khawf. First, carrying weapons during prayer in a state of fear is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory, contrary to some other schools who consider it wajib based on the apparent command in the Quran (4:102). The Hanafi reasoning is that carrying weapons is not an act of prayer itself, so the command is interpreted as non-obligatory (nadb). Second, if the people do not dispute about praying behind a single imam, it is actually better for each group to have its own imam and pray separately, just as in normal security, because this avoids the need for walking and other movements that might compromise the prayer. This is the preferred view as stated in Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
سلاح (silāḥ): Weapons, such as swords, spears, shields, etc., that are carried for protection during battle.
تنازع (tanāzu'): Dispute or disagreement among the people about the imam or the mode of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To allow each group to pray longer.
B) To avoid the need for walking and extra movements.
C) Because it is easier for the imam.
D) To protect the weapons.

Key Takeaway
In Salat al-Khawf, the Hanafi school recommends carrying weapons and prefers separate imams when there is no dispute, emphasizing ease and minimizing extra movements.

Individual Prayer and Gestures in Fear Prayer
Concludes fear prayer rulings with individual prayer and gestures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid fear prayer and identify when individual prayer with gestures is permitted.

Core Idea
Fear prayer with gestures is valid only with the enemy present and when following an imam is impractical.

In extreme fear, the Shariah allows praying individually with simple gestures, even without facing the Qibla. However, this concession has strict conditions. Let us examine when this is permissible and what invalidates it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is performing the fear prayer individually (furādā) with gestures (īmā'). The ruling is that it is valid (jā'iz) only when the enemy is present and one cannot follow an imam due to different positions while riding.
The text explicitly states that the prayer is not valid without the presence of an enemy.
2
Distinguish between the follower and the imam
For the followers (the group), the fear prayer is valid only if the enemy is actually present. If they mistake a dark mass for the enemy, their prayer is invalid unless it turns out to be the enemy. The imam's prayer, however, remains valid regardless, as there is no source of invalidity for him.
This shows that the imam is not bound by the same strict conditions as the followers.
3
Understand the exception via istihsān
If the first group realizes their mistake (that the dark mass is not the enemy) before crossing the rows in the desert, they may continue their prayer by istihsān (juristic preference). This is similar to the case of someone who leaves the prayer on suspicion of having broken wudu and later finds he did not—the ruling depends on whether he has passed the rows.
Istihsān allows flexibility when strict analogy would cause hardship.
4
Learn the rule about change in enemy presence
If the enemy leaves after the prayer has started, the concession is lifted but the prayer must be completed in the same manner—it is not permissible to deviate. If the enemy arrives after the prayer has started, deviation (turning to normal prayer) is allowed but this invalidates the prayer because the permissive factor appeared before the salām.
This aligns with the principle that removal of an excuse before completing the prayer invalidates it, as listed in the twelve issues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرادى، بالإيماء، إلى أي جهةٍ قَدَرُوا ولم تَجُز بلا حضور عدو. ويُستحبُّ حَمْلُ السلاح في الصَّلاةِ عند الخوف. وإنْ لم يَتَنَازَعُوا في الصَّلاةِ خلف إمام واحد، فالأفضل صلاةُ كلِّ طائفة بإمام، مثل حالة الأمن. تجوز صلاته راكباً، وإن كان مطلوباً فلا بأس بأن يصلي وهو سائر، لأنه فعل الدابة حقيقة، وإنمـا أُضيف إليه معنى التسيير، وإذا جاء العذر انقطعت الإضافة إليه، بخلاف ما لو صلى وهو يمشي، حيث لا يجوز، لأن المشي فعله حقيقة وهو مناف للصلاة، كما في مجمع الروايات»، (فُــرادى بالإيماء، إلى أيّ جهةٍ قَدَرُوا ) إذ لا . يصح الاقتداء؛ لاختلاف المكان حال الركوب، ولذا صح الاقتداء إذا كان الإمام والمقتدي به على دابة واحدة، كما لو كانا على خشبة، والغريق السابح كالماشي لا تجوز صلاته، لأن السباحة كالمشي عمل كثير . ( ولم تَجُزْ) صلاة الخوف بلا حضور عدو، فلو رأوا سواداً ظنـوه عـدواً صلوها، فإن تبين كما ظنوا جازت لتبين سبب الرخصة، وإن ظهر خلافه لم تجز صلاة القوم، وأمـا صـلاة الإمام فصحيحة بكل حال، لعدم المفسد في حقه، إلا إذا تبين للطائفة الأولى غير ما ظنوه قبل أن تتجاوز الصفوف، فإن لهم البناء ،استحساناً، كمن انصرف على ظن الحدث، يتوقف الفساد إذا ظهر أنه لم. يحدث على مجاوزة الصفوف في الصحراء. ولو شرعوا بحضرة العدو فذهب لا يجوز لهم الانحراف والانصراف لزوال سبب الرخصة، ولو شرعوا في صلاتهم ثم حضر ، جاز الانحراف لوجود المبيح، وهذا يفيد بطلان الصلاة، لزوال المبيح قبيل السَّلام على مقتضى المسائل الاثني عشرية)، ويشمله زوال عذر المعذور كذا في «الفتح». ويُستحبُّ حَمْلُ السَّلاحِ في ) الصَّلاةِ عند الخوف)، ولا يجب، كمـا قـال الإمام الشافعي ومالك رحمهما الله تعالى، عملاً بظاهر الأمر في قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ﴾ الآية [النساء : ۱۰۲] قلنا: هو محمول على الندب، لأن حمله ليس من أعمالها، فلا يجب فيها. (وإنْ لم يَتَنَازَعُوا) أي: القوم (في الصلاة خلف إمام واحد، فالأفضل صلاة كل طائفة مقتديــن (بإمـام) واحــد، فتذهــب الأولى بعد التمام، ثم تصلي الأخرى بإمام آخر (مثل حالة الأمن)، للتوقي عن المشي ونحوه، كذا في « فتـح القدير»، وهو حسبي ونعم النصير.
(۱) المسائل الاثني عشرية هي: ١- رؤية المتيمم الماء. ۲- انقضاء مدة المسح. ٣- نزع الخفين بعمل قليل. ٤- سقوط الجبيرة عن برء. ٥- تعلم أمي قدر فرض القراءة بأن تذكر بعد نسيان أو حفظ بمجرد د السماع، لأن التعلم على خلاف هاتين الصورتين عمل كثير . ٦- وجود عار ما يستر عورته ولو عارية. ٧- قـدرة مـوم عـلـى الركوع والسجود. ۸- تذكر مصل فائتة عليه، أو على إمامه وفي الوقت سعة، ويكون كل صاحب ترتيب. ٩- واستخلاف أمي. ١٠- طلوع الشمس في الفجر. ۱۱- دخول وقت العصر في الجمعة. ١٢- خروج وقت المعذور. فتح باب العناية (۲۹۹/۱). - ٥٦٥ -
Individually, with gestures, to any direction they can, and it is not valid without the presence of an enemy. Carrying weapons in prayer is recommended when fearful. If they do not dispute in prayer behind one imam, then it is better for each group to pray with an imam, like the state of security. It is permissible for him to pray while riding, and if he is being pursued, there is no harm in him praying while walking [sā'ir], because that is actually the action of the mount, and the meaning of walking is attributed to him [through the mount]; when the excuse appears, the attribution is cut off, unlike if he prays while walking on foot, which is not allowed, because walking is his actual action and is contrary to prayer, as in Majma‘ al-Riwāyāt. (Individually with gestures, to any direction they can), because following [the imam] is not valid due to the difference of place while riding, for this reason following is valid if the imam and the follower are on one mount, as if they were on a plank. A drowning person who is swimming is like a walker; his prayer is not valid, because swimming, like walking, is a lot of action. (And) the fear prayer is not valid without the presence of an enemy. If they see a dark mass and think it is an enemy and pray it, then if it becomes clear as they thought, it is valid because the reason for the concession is confirmed; if the opposite appears, the people's prayer is not valid. As for the imam's prayer, it is valid in any case, because there is no source of invalidity concerning him, except if it becomes clear to the first group other than what they thought before they pass the rows; then they may build upon [their prayer] by istihsān, like one who leaves on the suspicion of an event—the invalidity depends, if it appears that he did not have an event, on crossing the rows in the desert. If they begin in the presence of the enemy and then [the enemy] goes away, it is not permissible for them to deviate and leave due to the removal of the reason for the concession. If they begin their prayer and then [the enemy] arrives, deviation is permissible due to the existence of the permissive factor, and this indicates the invalidity of the prayer due to the removal of the permissive factor just before the salām, according to the twelve issues; and it includes the removal of the excuse of the excused one, as in al-Fatḥ. Carrying weapons in prayer when fearful is recommended, not obligatory, as Imām al-Shāfi‘ī and Mālik (may Allah have mercy on them) said, acting on the apparent command in His statement: “And let them take their weapons” [al-Nisā’: 102]. We say: it is carried on recommendation, because carrying it is not part of the actions of prayer, so it is not obligatory therein. (And if they do not dispute) meaning the people (in prayer behind one imam, then better is the prayer of each group following one imam; the first goes after completion, then the other prays with another imam) like the state of security, to avoid walking and the like, as in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. And He is sufficient for me and the best supporter. (1) The twelve issues are: 1- the sight of water by the one performing tayammum; 2- expiration of the period of wiping; 3- removing the khuffs with little action; 4- falling off of the splint upon recovery; 5- an ummī learning the amount of obligatory recitation by remembering after forgetfulness or memorizing by merely hearing, because learning contrary to these two forms is a lot of action; 6- finding something to cover the ‘awrah, even by borrowing; 7- the ability of one who gestures to bow and prostrate; 8- the remembrance of one praying that he or his imam has a missed prayer while there is time and both are people of order; 9- appointing an ummī as imam; 10- sunrise during Fajr; 11- entry of ‘Asr time during Jumu‘ah; 12- exit of the time of the excused one. Fatḥ Bāb al-‘Ināyah (1/299). - 565 -
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) on Nur al-Idah concludes the rulings on Salat al-Khawf (fear prayer). It begins by addressing individual prayer (فُرادى) when facing the enemy—each person prays alone with gestures (إيماء) in any direction they can, as following an imam is not valid due to different positions while riding. The text then states that fear prayer is not valid without the presence of an enemy. If people see a dark mass and think it is the enemy, they may perform fear prayer; if it turns out to be the enemy, the prayer is valid, but if not, the followers' prayer is invalid, though the imam's prayer remains valid. An exception is made for the first group if they realize their mistake before crossing the rows—they may continue by istihsān (juristic preference). If the enemy leaves after they start, they cannot deviate; if the enemy arrives after they start, deviation is allowed but invalidates the prayer, as the concession ends. The text then discusses carrying weapons in prayer when fearful—it is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory, contrary to Shafi‘i and Maliki views. The Hanafi response is that the command in the Quran (take your weapons) is interpreted as recommendation, not obligation, because carrying weapons is not part of the actions of prayer. Finally, if the people do not dispute over a single imam, it is better for each group to pray separately with its own imam, to avoid walking and the like. The footnote lists twelve issues (al-masā'il al-ithnā 'ashariyyah) that share a similar principle: when the excuse (such as tayammum, wiping on khuffs, etc.) ends before completing the prayer, the prayer becomes invalid.

Key Terms
فرادى (furādā): Praying individually, not in congregation, in the fear prayer when following an imam is not possible.
إيماء (īmā'): Gestures with the head for bowing and prostrating, instead of actual movements, permitted in fear prayer when in contact with the enemy, or for the sick.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that allows an exception to qiyas based on a stronger evidence or need, used here to allow the first group to continue their prayer when they realize their mistake before crossing the rows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the fear prayer with gestures become valid for the followers?
A) Whenever they are in a state of fear, even if no enemy is present.
B) Only when the enemy is actually present, and they cannot follow an imam.
C) Only when they follow an imam on the same mount.
D) Only if they face the Qibla.

Key Takeaway
The fear prayer with gestures is a concession valid only when the enemy is present and following an imam is impractical, with specific rules for changes in the enemy's presence.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Carrying Weapons in Fear Prayer: Hanafi vs Shafi'i/Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on carrying weapons in fear prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on carrying weapons in fear prayer and evaluate the evidence for the opposing view.

Core Idea
The command to take weapons in fear prayer is recommendation, not obligation, as carrying weapons is not part of the prayer.

The Quran commands believers to take their weapons during fear prayer. Does this make it obligatory? The Hanafi school says no, because the act of carrying a weapon is external to the prayer itself. Let us examine the proof and the counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that carrying weapons in fear prayer is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory.
The text says 'Yustahabbu' indicating recommendation.
2
Identify the opposing school's view
The Shafi'i and Maliki schools consider it obligatory (wājib) based on the apparent command in the Quran.
They act on the literal meaning of the command 'walya'khudhū aslihatahum'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi argument: the command is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) because carrying weapons is not part of the actions (a'māl) of prayer. Therefore, it cannot be obligatory within the prayer; obligations apply only to acts integral to prayer.
This is a usul principle: commands for acts external to the act of worship are not binding within it.
4
Note the practical consequence
In practice, a person praying in fear is not required to carry a weapon; missing it does not invalidate the prayer or require compensation.
The difference affects whether a sin is incurred for not carrying a weapon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Salah — Prayer

Prayer While Riding, Walking, and the Twelve Issues
Expansion on prayer while riding/walking and the twelve issues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid movements during fear prayer and apply the principle that the end of an excuse invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
Movement attributed to the mount does not break prayer; direct walking does. The twelve issues show that if the excuse ends before the salām, the prayer is invalid.

In fear prayer, a person may pray while riding and even move if the movement is attributed to the mount. But walking on foot invalidates the prayer. Additionally, if the excuse for a concession disappears mid-prayer, the prayer becomes invalid. This lesson explores these nuances.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling on riding
Praying while riding is permissible in fear prayer. If the rider is being pursued, he may pray while walking (sā'ir) because the walking is attributed to the mount, not to him. However, if he walks on foot (māshī), it is not allowed because walking is his own action and contradicts the prayer.
The key distinction is whether the movement is 'his' action or attributed to the mount.
2
Apply the same principle to the drowning person
A drowning person swimming is like a walker; swimming is considered a lot of action (like walking) and invalidates the prayer. Therefore, the prayer of a drowning person swimming is not valid.
The ruling is based on the concept of 'amal kathīr (excessive action).
3
Identify the twelve issues (al-masā'il al-ithnā 'ashariyyah)
The footnote lists twelve cases where the removal of the excuse (e.g., sighting water after tayammum) before completing the prayer invalidates the prayer. This includes the fear prayer scenario: if the enemy arrives after prayer starts, the prayer is invalid because the permissive factor arrived before salām.
These issues illustrate a general principle: if the excuse ends before salām, the prayer is invalid.
4
Connect the principle to the fear prayer case
The text explicitly says: if the enemy arrives after they start, deviation is allowed, and this means the prayer is invalid due to the removal of the permissive factor just before salām, according to the twelve issues.
This shows consistency across different rulings.

فرادى، بالإيماء، إلى أي جهةٍ قَدَرُوا ولم تَجُز بلا حضور عدو. ويُستحبُّ حَمْلُ السلاح في الصَّلاةِ عند الخوف. وإنْ لم يَتَنَازَعُوا في الصَّلاةِ خلف إمام واحد، فالأفضل صلاةُ كلِّ طائفة بإمام، مثل حالة الأمن. تجوز صلاته راكباً، وإن كان مطلوباً فلا بأس بأن يصلي وهو سائر، لأنه فعل الدابة حقيقة، وإنمـا أُضيف إليه معنى التسيير، وإذا جاء العذر انقطعت الإضافة إليه، بخلاف ما لو صلى وهو يمشي، حيث لا يجوز، لأن المشي فعله حقيقة وهو مناف للصلاة، كما في مجمع الروايات»، (فُــرادى بالإيماء، إلى أيّ جهةٍ قَدَرُوا ) إذ لا . يصح الاقتداء؛ لاختلاف المكان حال الركوب، ولذا صح الاقتداء إذا كان الإمام والمقتدي به على دابة واحدة، كما لو كانا على خشبة، والغريق السابح كالماشي لا تجوز صلاته، لأن السباحة كالمشي عمل كثير . ( ولم تَجُزْ) صلاة الخوف بلا حضور عدو، فلو رأوا سواداً ظنـوه عـدواً صلوها، فإن تبين كما ظنوا جازت لتبين سبب الرخصة، وإن ظهر خلافه لم تجز صلاة القوم، وأمـا صـلاة الإمام فصحيحة بكل حال، لعدم المفسد في حقه، إلا إذا تبين للطائفة الأولى غير ما ظنوه قبل أن تتجاوز الصفوف، فإن لهم البناء ،استحساناً، كمن انصرف على ظن الحدث، يتوقف الفساد إذا ظهر أنه لم. يحدث على مجاوزة الصفوف في الصحراء. ولو شرعوا بحضرة العدو فذهب لا يجوز لهم الانحراف والانصراف لزوال سبب الرخصة، ولو شرعوا في صلاتهم ثم حضر ، جاز الانحراف لوجود المبيح، وهذا يفيد بطلان الصلاة، لزوال المبيح قبيل السَّلام على مقتضى المسائل الاثني عشرية)، ويشمله زوال عذر المعذور كذا في «الفتح». ويُستحبُّ حَمْلُ السَّلاحِ في ) الصَّلاةِ عند الخوف)، ولا يجب، كمـا قـال الإمام الشافعي ومالك رحمهما الله تعالى، عملاً بظاهر الأمر في قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ﴾ الآية [النساء : ۱۰۲] قلنا: هو محمول على الندب، لأن حمله ليس من أعمالها، فلا يجب فيها. (وإنْ لم يَتَنَازَعُوا) أي: القوم (في الصلاة خلف إمام واحد، فالأفضل صلاة كل طائفة مقتديــن (بإمـام) واحــد، فتذهــب الأولى بعد التمام، ثم تصلي الأخرى بإمام آخر (مثل حالة الأمن)، للتوقي عن المشي ونحوه، كذا في « فتـح القدير»، وهو حسبي ونعم النصير.
(۱) المسائل الاثني عشرية هي: ١- رؤية المتيمم الماء. ۲- انقضاء مدة المسح. ٣- نزع الخفين بعمل قليل. ٤- سقوط الجبيرة عن برء. ٥- تعلم أمي قدر فرض القراءة بأن تذكر بعد نسيان أو حفظ بمجرد د السماع، لأن التعلم على خلاف هاتين الصورتين عمل كثير . ٦- وجود عار ما يستر عورته ولو عارية. ٧- قـدرة مـوم عـلـى الركوع والسجود. ۸- تذكر مصل فائتة عليه، أو على إمامه وفي الوقت سعة، ويكون كل صاحب ترتيب. ٩- واستخلاف أمي. ١٠- طلوع الشمس في الفجر. ۱۱- دخول وقت العصر في الجمعة. ١٢- خروج وقت المعذور. فتح باب العناية (۲۹۹/۱). - ٥٦٥ -
Individually, with gestures, to any direction they can, and it is not valid without the presence of an enemy. Carrying weapons in prayer is recommended when fearful. If they do not dispute in prayer behind one imam, then it is better for each group to pray with an imam, like the state of security. It is permissible for him to pray while riding, and if he is being pursued, there is no harm in him praying while walking [sā'ir], because that is actually the action of the mount, and the meaning of walking is attributed to him [through the mount]; when the excuse appears, the attribution is cut off, unlike if he prays while walking on foot, which is not allowed, because walking is his actual action and is contrary to prayer, as in Majma‘ al-Riwāyāt. (Individually with gestures, to any direction they can), because following [the imam] is not valid due to the difference of place while riding, for this reason following is valid if the imam and the follower are on one mount, as if they were on a plank. A drowning person who is swimming is like a walker; his prayer is not valid, because swimming, like walking, is a lot of action. (And) the fear prayer is not valid without the presence of an enemy. If they see a dark mass and think it is an enemy and pray it, then if it becomes clear as they thought, it is valid because the reason for the concession is confirmed; if the opposite appears, the people's prayer is not valid. As for the imam's prayer, it is valid in any case, because there is no source of invalidity concerning him, except if it becomes clear to the first group other than what they thought before they pass the rows; then they may build upon [their prayer] by istihsān, like one who leaves on the suspicion of an event—the invalidity depends, if it appears that he did not have an event, on crossing the rows in the desert. If they begin in the presence of the enemy and then [the enemy] goes away, it is not permissible for them to deviate and leave due to the removal of the reason for the concession. If they begin their prayer and then [the enemy] arrives, deviation is permissible due to the existence of the permissive factor, and this indicates the invalidity of the prayer due to the removal of the permissive factor just before the salām, according to the twelve issues; and it includes the removal of the excuse of the excused one, as in al-Fatḥ. Carrying weapons in prayer when fearful is recommended, not obligatory, as Imām al-Shāfi‘ī and Mālik (may Allah have mercy on them) said, acting on the apparent command in His statement: “And let them take their weapons” [al-Nisā’: 102]. We say: it is carried on recommendation, because carrying it is not part of the actions of prayer, so it is not obligatory therein. (And if they do not dispute) meaning the people (in prayer behind one imam, then better is the prayer of each group following one imam; the first goes after completion, then the other prays with another imam) like the state of security, to avoid walking and the like, as in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. And He is sufficient for me and the best supporter. (1) The twelve issues are: 1- the sight of water by the one performing tayammum; 2- expiration of the period of wiping; 3- removing the khuffs with little action; 4- falling off of the splint upon recovery; 5- an ummī learning the amount of obligatory recitation by remembering after forgetfulness or memorizing by merely hearing, because learning contrary to these two forms is a lot of action; 6- finding something to cover the ‘awrah, even by borrowing; 7- the ability of one who gestures to bow and prostrate; 8- the remembrance of one praying that he or his imam has a missed prayer while there is time and both are people of order; 9- appointing an ummī as imam; 10- sunrise during Fajr; 11- entry of ‘Asr time during Jumu‘ah; 12- exit of the time of the excused one. Fatḥ Bāb al-‘Ināyah (1/299). - 565 -
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) on Nur al-Idah concludes the rulings on Salat al-Khawf (fear prayer). It begins by addressing individual prayer (فُرادى) when facing the enemy—each person prays alone with gestures (إيماء) in any direction they can, as following an imam is not valid due to different positions while riding. The text then states that fear prayer is not valid without the presence of an enemy. If people see a dark mass and think it is the enemy, they may perform fear prayer; if it turns out to be the enemy, the prayer is valid, but if not, the followers' prayer is invalid, though the imam's prayer remains valid. An exception is made for the first group if they realize their mistake before crossing the rows—they may continue by istihsān (juristic preference). If the enemy leaves after they start, they cannot deviate; if the enemy arrives after they start, deviation is allowed but invalidates the prayer, as the concession ends. The text then discusses carrying weapons in prayer when fearful—it is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory, contrary to Shafi‘i and Maliki views. The Hanafi response is that the command in the Quran (take your weapons) is interpreted as recommendation, not obligation, because carrying weapons is not part of the actions of prayer. Finally, if the people do not dispute over a single imam, it is better for each group to pray separately with its own imam, to avoid walking and the like. The footnote lists twelve issues (al-masā'il al-ithnā 'ashariyyah) that share a similar principle: when the excuse (such as tayammum, wiping on khuffs, etc.) ends before completing the prayer, the prayer becomes invalid.

Key Terms
سائر (sā'ir): Walking while the mount walks; movement attributed to the mount.
ماشي (māshī): Walking on foot; direct action of the person.
عمل كثير (amal kathīr): Excessive action that invalidates prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person performing fear prayer while swimming (drowning)?
A) Valid, because he is under duress.
B) Invalid, because swimming is like walking and is a lot of action.
C) Valid if he can continue, but invalid if he stops.
D) Valid only if he makes gestures.

Key Takeaway
In fear prayer, movement attributed to the mount is allowed, but direct walking or excessive actions invalidate the prayer; the twelve issues show that the end of an excuse before salām invalidates the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Rulings on the Dying Person: Facing Qibla and Talqin
Describes sunnah actions for the dying person and the ruling of talqin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions for the dying person and apply the Hanafi ruling on talqin, including the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Sunnah at death: face the dying to qibla and gently prompt 'La ilaha illallah' — the Muslim's last words should be the testimony.

In this passage, al-Shurunbulali begins the chapter on funerals by outlining the recommended practices for the one near death. The author explains the sunnah of positioning the dying person towards the qibla and the etiquettes of prompting the shahadah. He also addresses a significant intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab discussion regarding whether both shahadahs should be prompted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling level for the actions
Determine whether the actions described (facing qibla, talqin) are obligatory or recommended. Note the evidence that leads to the classification as sunnah muakkadah.
The imperative 'laqqinū' is interpreted as recommendation due to other evidence.
2
Analyze the positioning of the dying person
Distinguish between the sunnah position (right side facing qibla) and the permissible alternative (lying on back with raised head). Understand the reasoning for each.
The alternative is chosen for ease of treatment.
3
Examine the dalil for talqin
Look at the hadith 'Laqqinū mawtākum...' and 'Man kāna ākhiru kalāmihi...'. Identify how the Hanafi school derives the sunnah ruling from these texts.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
4
Resolve the dispute on one vs two shahadahs
Contrast the Hanafi position (only first shahadah for Muslims) with the Shafi'i position (both shahadahs). Follow the Hanafi response and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.
The dispute hinges on the status of the dying person: Muslim vs non-Muslim.
