Chapter of Rulings of Funerals. It is sunnah to direct the dying person on his right side, and lying on the back is permissible, and his head is raised slightly. And he is prompted with the mention of the testimony at his presence. Chapter of Rulings of Funerals. The plural of janaza - with fatḥ and kasr - from janaztu al-shay'a, I cover it. Al-Aṣmaʿī and Ibn al-Aʿrābī said: with kasr it is the deceased himself, with fatḥ it is the bier. From Thaʿlab: the opposite. Al-Azharī said: it is not called janaza until the deceased is tied on it shrouded. (It is sunnah to direct the muḥtaḍar) i.e. the one close to death, described for the presence of his death or the angels of death. Signs of iḥtiḍār: relaxation of his feet, hollowing of his temples, bending of his nose, elongation of the skin of his testicles because the testicle hangs at death and its skin dangles. Then he is directed toward the qibla on his right side because it is the transmitted sunnah, and because he will be placed in the grave on his right side, so he is given the ruling of what is near to it. (And lying on his back is permissible, chosen by our mashāyikh of mā warā' al-nahr because it is easier for treating him). (And) but (his head is raised slightly) so that his face is toward the qibla and not the sky. (And) it is sunnah that (he is prompted) and that (by the mention of the testimony at his presence) due to his saying: 'Prompt your dying: lā ilāha illallāh, for no Muslim says it at death except that it saves him from the Fire.' And due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whose last words are lā ilāha illallāh enters Paradise' as in al-Burhān, meaning enters Paradise with the successful, otherwise every Muslim, even a sinner, enters Paradise, even if after long punishment. He limited to the mention of the testimony following the authentic hadith, although it is said in al-Mustasfā and others like al-Durar: prompt with the two testimonies lā ilāha illallāh and Muḥammad Rasūlullāh. And his reasoning in al-Durar that the first is not accepted without the second is not absolute because that is regarding the non-believer, and our speech is about prompting the believer. Therefore Shaykh al-Islām Ibn Ḥajar of the Shāfiʿī imams said: The saying of the group that he is prompted 'Muḥammad Rasūlullāh' and also because the intent is his death upon Islam, and he is not called Muslim except with both, is rebutted because he is Muslim, and the intent is only to conclude his speech with lā ilāha illallāh to obtain that reward. As for the disbeliever, he is prompted with both definitely with the word 'ashhadu' because it is obligatory, since he does not become Muslim except with both. End. That is due to the report of the Jewish youth: Bukhārī narrated from Anas that a Jewish youth used to serve the Prophet, then he fell ill, so the Prophet came to visit him and sat at his head and said to him: 'Embrace Islam.' He looked at his father who was with him, and his father said to him: 'Obey Abal-Qāsim,' so he embraced Islam. Then the Prophet, peace be upon him, came out saying: 'Praise be to Allah who saved him from the Fire.' End. And the two testimonies are mentioned (without insistence) because the state is difficult for him. If he says them and does not speak after, they stop, because the purpose is to conclude his speech with them, as we narrated. (And the Muslim is not commanded to say them) so he is not told 'say', because he is in distress, and perhaps he will say 'no' in response to something other than the command, so it will be thought ill of him. They said: if something that necessitates disbelief appears from him, he is not judged as a disbeliever, on the basis that his mind has left him. And some mashāyikh chose that his mind leaves him at death due to this fear. And what should be said to him as a form of repentance seeking forgiveness is: 'I seek forgiveness from Allah the Mighty, the One besides whom there is no god, the Living, the Self-Sustaining, and I repent to Him, seeking intercession through Muḥammad, the Messenger of Allah.' This includes gentle prompting, because he may feel sympathy from mentioning what suggests he is dying. As for the disbeliever, he is commanded with both as we narrated. Hence the Shāfiʿī scholars stated that the prompter should be someone other than the heir, lest he be accused of hastening inheritance if there is another heir, otherwise the most compassionate of the heirs; and likewise anyone who might be accused of enmity or envy. End. (And prompting him) after he is placed (in the grave is prescribed) due to the authenticity of his saying: 'Prompt your dead with the testimony that there is no god but Allah.' It was narrated by all except Bukhārī, and attributed to Ahl al-Sunnah wa'l-Jamāʿah. And it is said: he should not be prompted in the grave, attributed to the Muʿtazila. And it is said: he is not commanded to do it nor forbidden. Its method: it is said: O so-and-so son of so-and-so, remember your religion which you used to follow, and mention death and what follows...
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage from Imdād al-Fattāḥ, a commentary on Nūr al-Īḍāḥ, begins the chapter on funerals (janā'iz). The author first defines the term 'janāzah' and then discusses the sunnah actions for the dying person (muḥtaḍar). The primary ruling is that it is sunnah to turn the dying person on his right side facing the qiblah, as this is the transmitted practice and anticipates his position in the grave. However, it is also permissible to lay him on his back, especially for ease of treatment, as preferred by the scholars of Transoxiana. In that case, his head should be slightly raised so his face faces the qiblah. Next, the text discusses talqīn: prompting the dying person to say the shahādah. This is sunnah and supported by hadiths stating that one who says 'lā ilāha illallāh' at death enters Paradise. A nuanced point arises: should only the first shahādah be prompted, or both? The author clarifies that for a Muslim already having īmān, prompting both is unnecessary; the emphasis is on ending with 'lā ilāha illallāh'. For a non-Muslim, both shahādahs must be recited with 'ashhadu' to enter Islam, based on the incident of the Jewish youth. The passage then explains that prompting should be done gently, without insistence, and the Muslim should not be commanded to say it, to avoid confusion in distress. If the dying person appears to utter disbelief, it is not judged as apostasy due to likely loss of reason. Finally, talqīn after burial is also prescribed according to Ahl al-Sunnah, with a specific method addressing the deceased. The discussion reflects careful Hanafi concern for the dying person's state and the proper means to facilitate a good end.

Key Terms
محتضر (muḥtaḍar): The person who is close to death, showing signs of imminent death.
تلقين (talqīn): Prompting the dying person (or the deceased in the grave) to recite the shahādah.
جنازة (janāzah): The deceased person (with kasr) or the bier on which the deceased is carried (with fatḥ); also the funeral.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How should the dying person be positioned according to the sunnah in the Hanafi school?
A) On his back with face towards the sky
B) On his right side facing the qiblah
C) On his left side facing the qiblah
D) Sitting upright facing the qiblah

Key Takeaway
The sunnah is to face the dying person towards the qibla and gently remind them of 'La ilaha illallah', not to command or insist.

Rulings on Talqeen: Prompting the Dying and the Deceased
Explains talqeen rulings with proofs and scholarly disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqeen for the dying Muslim and non-Muslim and for the deceased in the grave, and explain the evidence from the hadith and the interpretive principle used.

Core Idea
Talqeen of the dying is without insistence; talqeen at the grave is recommended based on the hadith 'Prompt your dying ones.'

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the Hanafi position on talqeen (prompting) in two contexts: at the time of death and after burial. It distinguishes between the Muslim and non-Muslim, and addresses the method, purpose, and evidence. The key proof is the hadith 'Lqinu mawtakum…' which the Hanafis interpret figuratively to refer to those near death, not the deceased. The passage also notes the dispute with the Mu'tazila and the practice of the early Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (talqeen) and the hukm level (mandub / recommended) for each scenario: dying Muslim, dying non-Muslim, and deceased in grave.
The text states talqeen at the grave is 'mashru' (legislated/recommended); for the dying Muslim it is not commanded but done without insistence; for the dying non-Muslim it is commanded.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence cited: the hadith 'Lqinu mawtakum shahadata an la ilaha illallah' (narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, etc.) and the practice of the Salaf.
The hadith is classified as ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its imperative form is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the imperative 'lqinu' indicates recommendation, not obligation, and how the word 'mawtakum' (your dead) is interpreted figuratively as 'those near death' to avoid contradiction with the fact that the deceased do not hear.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-nadb (the imperative gives recommendation) unless there is a qarina indicating wujub. The context of not insisting and the difficulty of the dying confirm nadb.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the conflicting views: the Mu'tazila reject talqeen at the grave; some scholars say it is neither commanded nor prohibited; the Shafi'is also recommend it but advise a non-heir to perform it.
The Hanafi position is attributed to Ahl al-Sunnah; the Mu'tazila objection is recorded in al-Fath.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Determine which position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). The relied-upon view is that talqeen at the grave is recommended (mashru'), supported by Ibn al-Humam and the practice of the Salaf.
The passage also includes a broader discussion on whether the dead hear, reconciling the hadith with Quranic verses.

من غير إلحاح، ولا يُؤمر بها ، وتَلْقِينُهُ في القبر مشروع. وقيل: لا يُلقن، وقيل: لا يُؤمر به، ولا يُنهى عنه، .. عن أنس قال: «كان غلام يهودي يخدم النبي ، فمرض ، فأتاه النبي لا يعوده، فقعد عند رأسه، فقال له: أَسْلِمْ، فَنَظَر إِلَى أَبِيْهِ وَهُوَ عِنْدَهُ فَقَالَ لَهُ: أطِعْ أبا القاسم [ فَأَسْلَمَ ] فَخَرَجَ النَّبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وَهُوَ يَقُولُ: (1) ( الحمد لله الذي أنْقَذَهُ منَ النَّارِ » ) ، انتهى. وتذكر الشهادتين (من غير الحاج)، لأن الحال صعب عليه، فإذا قالها ولم يتكلم بعدها يمسك عنه، لأن المقصود ختم كلامه به، لما رويناه (۳) (ولا يُؤمرُ بها المسلم، فلا يقال له: قل (۳)، لأنه يكون في شدة، فربما يقول لا جواباً لغير الأمر فيظن به خلاف الخير، وقالوا: إذا ظهر منه ما يوجب كفراً لا يحكم بكفره، حملاً على أنه زال عقله، واختار بعض المشايخ: زوال عقله عند موته لهذا الخوف، ومما ينبغي أن يُقال له على جهة الاستتابة: أستغفر الله العظيم الذي لا إله إلا هو الحي القيوم وأتوب إليه، مستشفعاً بمحمد رسول الله، فيشمل التلقين بلطف، لأنه قد يشفق عليه من ذكر ما يشعر بأنه محتضر ، وأما الكافر فيؤمر بهما كما روينا ، ولذا أفاد علماء الشافعية أن يلقنه غير الوارث، لئلا يتهمه باستعجال الإرث إن كان ثَمَّ غيره، وإلا فأشفق الورثة، وكذا كل من يتهمه بعداوة أو حسد، انتهى. (وتَلْقِينُهُ) بعدما وضع (في القبر مشروع) لحقيقة قوله : لَقْنُوا مَوْتَاكُمْ شَهَادَةَ أنْ لا إلَهَ إلا الله : ( أخرجه الجماعة إلا البخاري، ونسب إلى أهل السنة والجماعة، وقيل: لا يُلَقَّنُ) (۱) في القبر، ونُسب إلى المعتزلة، كذا في «الفتح»، وقيل: لا يُؤمر به، ولا يُنهى عنه، وكيفيته أن يقال: يا فلان بن فلان، اذكـــر دينـك الـذي كنت عليه في دار الدنيا بشهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمداً رسول الله، ولاشك أن اللفظ لا يجوز إخراجه عن حقيقته إلا بدليل، فيجب تعيينه فقوله: «موتاكم حقيقة، ونفي صاحب ( الكافي» فائدته مطلقاً فممنوع، نعم الفائدة الأصلية منتفية، ويحتاج إليه ليثبت الجنان للسؤال في القبر، قاله المحقق ابن الهمام»، وقال شيخ مشايخنا العلامة « المقدسي » : قلت ويؤيده ما روی سعید بن منصور، وسمرة بن حبيب وحكيم بن عمير قالوا: إذا سوي على الميت قبره، وانصرف الناس كانوا يستحبون أن يقال للميت عند قبره يا فلان قل لا إله إلا الله ثلاث مرات يا فلان قل ربي الله وديني الإسلام، ونبيي محمد ) انتهى. ثم قال ( الكمال بن الهمام : وعندي أن مبنى ارتكاب هذا المجاز هنا عند أكثر مشايخنا بقول « الهداية » ، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لَقْنُوا مَوْتَاكُمْ» (۳) والمراد الذي قرب من الموت، انتهى هو أن الميت لا يسمع عندهم، وأورد عليهم قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في أهل القليب (۳): « مَا أَنْتُمْ بَأَسْمَعَ لِمَا أقَوْلُ مِنْهُمْ ) وأجابوا تارة بأنه مردود، من عائشة قالت: كيـف يقول عليه الصلاة والسلام ذلك والله تعالى يقول: ﴿وَمَا أَنتَ بِمُسْمِعٍ مَن فِي الْقُبُورِ [قط: ٢٢]، وإِنَّكَ لَا تُسْمِعُ الْمَوْتَى ) [الا: ٨٠]، وتارة بأن ذلك خصوصية له عليه الصلاة والسلام معجزة وزيادة حسرة على الكافرين، وتارة بأنه من ضرب المثل (١) كما قال عليه. ويشكل عليهم ما في مسلم: «إنَّ الميِّتَ لَيَسْمَعُ قَرْعَ نِعَالِهِمْ إِذَا انْصَرَفُوا ، اللهم إلا أن يخصوا ذلك بأول الوضع في القبر، مقدمة للسؤال، جمعاً بينه وبين الآيتين، فإنما يفيدان تحقيق عدم سماعهم، فإنه تعالى شبه الكفار بالموتى لإفادة
Without insistence, and it is not commanded. And talqeen of him in the grave is legislated. And it is said: he should not be prompted, and it is said: it is not commanded nor prohibited. ... From Anas: 'There was a Jewish boy who served the Prophet, and he fell ill. The Prophet came to visit him and sat at his head and said: Accept Islam. He looked at his father who was with him, and his father said: Obey Abu al-Qasim. So he accepted Islam. The Prophet came out saying: Praise be to Allah who saved him from the Fire.' End. And the two testimonies are mentioned (without insistence) because the situation is difficult for him. If he says them and does not speak afterwards, one should stop, because the purpose is that his final words are these, as we have narrated. (And the Muslim is not commanded to say them, so one should not say to him: Say, because he is in distress. Perhaps he will say 'no' in response to other than the command, so it will be thought ill of him. They said: If something that requires kufr appears from him, do not judge him as a disbeliever, interpreting that his mind has left. Some scholars chose that his mind leaves at the time of death due to this fear. And what should be said to him by way of exhortation: 'I seek forgiveness from Allah, the Mighty, besides whom there is no god, the Living, the Sustainer, and I repent to Him, seeking intercession through Muhammad the Messenger of Allah.' This includes gentle prompting, because he may be compassionate about mentioning what indicates that he is dying. As for the disbeliever, he is commanded with both, as we narrated. For this reason, Shafi'i scholars stated that someone other than the heir should prompt him, lest he be accused of hastening inheritance if there are other heirs, otherwise the most compassionate of the heirs (should do it), and likewise anyone who might be accused of enmity or jealousy. End. (And his talqeen) after he is placed (in the grave is legislated) due to the truth of his statement: 'Prompt your dying ones with the testimony that there is no god but Allah' (narrated by all except Bukhari, and attributed to Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah. And it is said: he should not be prompted in the grave, attributed to the Mu'tazila, as in al-Fath. And it is said: it is not commanded nor prohibited. Its manner is that one says: O so-and-so, son of so-and-so, remember your religion which you followed in the world by testifying that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. There is no doubt that the word cannot be taken out of its literal meaning except with evidence, so it is necessary to specify it. So his statement 'your dying ones' is literal, and denying its benefit absolutely is forbidden. Yes, the original benefit is negated, and it is needed to establish firmness for the questioning in the grave, said by al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam. And the teacher of our teachers, al-Maqdisi, said: I say: It is supported by what was narrated by Sa'id ibn Mansur, Samura ibn Habib, and Hakim ibn Umayr: They used to recommend that when the grave is levelled and the people depart, one says to the deceased at his grave: O so-and-so, say 'La ilaha illallah' three times; O so-and-so, say 'My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and my Prophet is Muhammad'. End. Then al-Kamal ibn al-Humam said: In my view, the basis for employing this metaphor here with most of our scholars is the statement of al-Hidayah: His statement 'Prompt your dying ones' and the intended meaning is the one near death. End. He said: The deceased does not hear according to them. They are objected to by his statement about the people of Well (Badr): 'You are not more attentive to what I say than they.' They answered: sometimes by saying it is rejected, as 'Aisha said: How could he say that while Allah says: 'And you cannot make hear those in the graves' and 'Indeed, you cannot make the dead hear'; sometimes by saying it was a special miracle for him and an increase of grief for the disbelievers; sometimes by saying it was a metaphorical similitude as he said. And it poses a problem for them what is in Muslim: 'The deceased hears the sound of their footsteps when they depart.' Unless they specify that for the first placement in the grave as a prelude to the questioning, reconciling between it and the two verses, for they only affirm the non-hearing in general, because Allah likened the disbelievers to the dead to indicate...
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of talqeen (prompting) in two situations: at the time of death and after burial. The author begins by stating that talqeen of the dying person should be done without insistence; the Muslim is not commanded to say the shahada because he is in distress and might say 'no' inadvertently, leading to a misunderstanding. A hadith is cited about the Jewish boy who accepted Islam upon the Prophet's prompting, establishing the permissibility of prompting a non-Muslim at death. For the Muslim, the practice is to mention the shahada without insisting, and if he says it and remains silent, the prompter stops. If the dying person utters words of disbelief, it is not judged as apostasy because his mind may be leaving. The author then addresses talqeen at the grave, stating it is mashru' (legislated) based on the hadith 'Prompt your dying ones' and the practice of the early Muslims, attributed to Ahl al-Sunnah. The Mu'tazila's rejection is noted. The manner of talqeen at the grave is specified. A discussion follows on whether the dead can hear, involving the hadith of the people of Badr and the verse about not hearing, with various reconciliations. The Hanafi position is that talqeen at the grave is beneficial for the deceased's answering of the questions.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqin): Prompting a dying person to say the shahada or prompting the deceased at the grave to remind them of the faith.
موتاكم (mawtākum): Literally 'your dead', interpreted in this context as 'those near death' (dying) to reconcile with the practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on talqeen of a Muslim at the time of death?
A) It is obligatory and must be insisted upon.
B) It is recommended but done without insistence, and the Muslim is not commanded to say the shahada.
C) It is prohibited because it may cause distress.
D) It is only for non-Muslims, not for Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Talqeen of the dying Muslim is not commanded and is done without insistence; talqeen at the grave is recommended (mashru') based on the hadith and the practice of the Salaf.

Talqin and the Hearing of the Dead: The Hanafi Position
Intra-Hanafi dispute on talqin timing and whether the dead hear

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on talqin and explain how the school reconciles the evidence regarding whether the dead hear.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that the dead do not hear, and talqin is recommended after burial.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah presents a detailed intra-Hanafi debate about talqin (prompting the shahada) and whether the dead can hear. The commentator, al-Kamal ibn al-Humam, defends the Hanafi view that the dead do not hear, relying on Quranic verses and reconciling contrary hadith. Understanding this dispute helps clarify the recommended timing of talqin and the usul principles at play.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what most Hanafi scholars hold regarding talqin and the hearing of the dead.
The dead do not hear in general; talqin is recommended after death at the grave.
2
Identify the primary evidence
Examine the Quranic verses and the hadith 'لقنوا موتاكم' and how they are interpreted.
Verses like 'وما أنت بمسمع من في القبور' negate general hearing; the hadith is interpreted figuratively for the near-death.
3
Examine opposing arguments
Understand the counter-evidence: the Prophet's address at Badr and the hadith of hearing sandals.
These are used by those who claim the dead can hear.
4
Analyse the Hanafi reconciliation
How does the school respond to the opposing arguments? Consider the answers: miracle, metaphor, limitation to the first moment in the grave.
The Badr incident is a special case; the sandal hearing is limited to the immediate burial moment as a prelude to questioning.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence of this dispute?
The timing of talqin: Hanafis recommend it after death at the grave; others may restrict it to before death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كنت عليه في دار الدنيا بشهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمداً رسول الله، ولاشك أن اللفظ لا يجوز إخراجه عن حقيقته إلا بدليل، فيجب تعيينه فقوله: «موتاكم حقيقة، ونفي صاحب الكافي فائدته مطلقاً فممنوع، نعم الفائدة الأصلية منتفية، ويحتاج إليه ليثبت الجنان للسؤال في القبر، قاله المحقق ابن الهمام». وقال شيخ مشايخنا العلامة المقدسي: قلت ويؤيده ما روی سعید بن منصور، وسمرة بن حبيب وحكيم بن عمير قالوا: إذا سوي على الميت قبره، وانصرف الناس كانوا يستحبون أن يقال للميت عند قبره يا فلان قل لا إله إلا الله ثلاث مرات يا فلان قل ربي الله وديني الإسلام، ونبيي محمد. ثم قال الكمال بن الهمام: وعندي أن مبنى ارتكاب هذا المجاز هنا عند أكثر مشايخنا بقول الهداية، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لَقْنُوا مَوْتَاكُمْ» والمراد الذي قرب من الموت، انتهى هو أن الميت لا يسمع عندهم، وأورد عليهم قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في أهل القليب: «مَا أَنْتُمْ بِأَسْمَعَ لِمَا أقَوْلُ مِنْهُمْ» وأجابوا تارة بأنه مردود، من عائشة قالت: كيـف يقول عليه الصلاة والسلام ذلك والله تعالى يقول: ﴿وَمَا أَنتَ بِمُسْمِعٍ مَن فِي الْقُبُورِ﴾، ﴿إِنَّكَ لَا تُسْمِعُ الْمَوْتَى﴾، وتارة بأن ذلك خصوصية له عليه الصلاة والسلام معجزة وزيادة حسرة على الكافرين، وتارة بأنه من ضرب المثل كما قال عليه. ويشكل عليهم ما في مسلم: «إنَّ الميِّتَ لَيَسْمَعُ قَرْعَ نِعَالِهِمْ إِذَا انْصَرَفُوا»، اللهم إلا أن يخصوا ذلك بأول الوضع في القبر، مقدمة للسؤال، جمعاً بينه وبين الآيتين، فإنما يفيدان تحقيق عدم سماعهم، فإنه تعالى شبه الكفار بالموتى لإفادة تعذر سماعهم، وهو فرع عدم سماع الموتى، إلا أنه على هذا ينبغي التلقين بعد الموت، لأنه يكون حين إرجاع الروح فيكون حينئذ لفظ «موتاكم» في حقيقته، وهو قول طائفة من المشايخ، إذ هو مجاز باعتبار ما كان نظراً إلى أنه الآن حي، إذ ليس معنى الحي إلا من في بدنه الـــروح، وعلـى كـل حال يحتاج إلى دليل آخر في التلقين حالة الاحتضار، إذ لا يراد الحقيقي والمجازي معاً ولا مجازیان، وليس يظهر معنى يعم الحقيقي والمجازي يعتبر مستعملاً فيه، ليكون من عموم للتضاد، وشرط إعماله فيهما أن لا يتضاد، انتهى قلت يرجح المجازي التعليل في الحديث: «لَقْنُوا مَوْتَاكُمْ لا إله إلا الله فَإِنَّهُ لَيْسَ مُسْلِمٌ يقولها عِنْدَ المَوْتِ إِلا أَنْجَتْهُ مِنَ النَّارِ» انتهى لفظه ودليل المجاز التلقين في القبر بالأثر الذي قدمناه عن الشيخ علي المقدسي. قال الكمال رحمه الله: والعبد الضعيف مؤلف هذه الكلمات، فوض أمره إلى الرب الغني الكريم، متوكلاً عليه، طالباً مـنـه جلت عظمته أن يرحم عظيم فاقتي بالموت على الإيمان والإيقان، ومن يتوكــل عـلـى الله فهو حسبه ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلي العظيم انتهى لفظه وكذلك أقول كما قال: وعلـى الله الكريــم اعتمادي في كل حال. (ويُسْتَحَبُّ لأقرباء المُحْتَضَرِ) وأصدقائه ( وجيرانه الدخولُ عليه) للقيام بحقه والاستئناس بهم، وتذكيرهم إياه ما ينفعه من وصية ونحوها، وبتجريعه الماء، لأن العطش يغلب لشدة النزع حينئذ، ولذلك يأتي الشيطان كما ورد بماء زلال، ويقول : قل لا إله غيري، حتى أسقيك، ويحسنون ظنه بالله تعالى، لخبر مسلم: « لا يموتَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ إِلا وَهُوَ يُحْسِنُ الظَّنَّ بِاللَّهِ » أي: يظن أنه يرحمه ويعفو عنه، وخبر الصحيحين: « قالَ الله تَعَالَى: أَنَا عِنْدَ ظَنِّ عَبْدِي بِي ) (وَيَتْلُونَ عِندَهُ سورة يبين ( لخبر (اقْرَؤُوا عَلَى مَوْتَاكُمْ يبن ) رواه أبو داود وابن حبان وصححه، وقال: المراد بـه من حضره الموت، والحكمة في قراءتها أن أحوال القيامة والبعث مذكورة فيها، فيتجدد له ذكرها،
You were upon it in the abode of the world by the testimony that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, and there is no doubt that the wording cannot be taken out of its literal meaning except by evidence, so it must be specified. So his saying: 'Your dead' is literal, and denying the benefit of al-Kafi is absolutely not accepted. Yes, the original benefit is negated, and it is needed to confirm the heart for the questioning in the grave, said al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam. And the shaykh of our shaykhs, al-Allama al-Maqdisi said: I say, and it is supported by what Sa'id ibn Mansur, Samurah ibn Habib, and Hakim ibn Umayr narrated: they said: When the grave of the deceased is leveled and the people depart, they used to recommend that it be said to the deceased at his grave: O so-and-so, say 'La ilaha illa Allah' three times, O so-and-so, say 'My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and my prophet is Muhammad.' Then al-Kamal ibn al-Humam said: In my view, the basis for adopting this figurative meaning here according to most of our shaykhs is the saying of al-Hidayah, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Prompt your dead,' and what is meant is the one who is near death. He concluded: The deceased does not hear according to them, and there was raised against them his saying, peace be upon him, regarding the people of al-Qalib: 'You are not more hearing of what I say than they are.' And they answered sometimes by saying it is rejected, from Aisha who said: How can he, peace be upon him, say that while Allah says: 'And you cannot make hear those in the graves' and 'Indeed, you cannot make the dead hear,' and sometimes by saying that is a special quality for him, peace be upon him, a miracle and additional regret for the disbelievers, and sometimes by saying it is a metaphorical expression as he said. And there is a difficulty for them from what is in Muslim: 'Indeed, the deceased hears the sound of their sandals when they depart,' unless they limit that to the first placing in the grave as a prelude to the questioning, to reconcile between it and the two verses, for they only indicate the negation of their hearing, because He likened the disbelievers to the dead to indicate the impossibility of their hearing, and that is a branch of the non-hearing of the dead. Except that on this basis, talqin should be after death, because that is when the soul is returned, so then the wording 'your dead' is in its literal meaning, and that is the saying of a group of scholars, because it is metaphorical considering what it was, looking at the fact that he is now alive, for the meaning of 'alive' is only one whose body has the soul. In any case, a different evidence is needed for talqin at the time of death, because the literal and figurative cannot both be intended or two figurative meanings, and there does not appear a meaning that encompasses both the literal and figurative to be considered used in it, to be from generality, because of contradiction, and the condition for applying it to both is that they do not contradict. He concluded: I say, the figurative is given preponderance by the reason in the hadith: 'Prompt your dead with La ilaha illa Allah, for there is no Muslim who says it at the time of death except that it saves him from the Fire.' The wording ends, and the evidence for the figurative is talqin in the grave by the tradition we presented from al-Shaykh Ali al-Maqdisi. Al-Kamal said, may Allah have mercy on him: And the weak slave, the author of these words, entrusts his affair to the Rich, Generous Lord, relying on Him, asking Him, may His greatness be exalted, to have mercy on my great need for death upon faith and certainty, and whoever relies on Allah, He is sufficient for him, and there is no power and no strength except with Allah, the Most High, the Mighty. His words end, and I say as he said: And upon the Generous Allah is my reliance in every situation. (And it is recommended for the relatives of the dying person) and his friends (and his neighbors to enter upon him) to fulfill his right and to find comfort with them, and to remind him of what will benefit him of a will and the like, and to make him drink water, because thirst overwhelms due to the severity of the death throes at that time, and therefore the devil comes, as narrated, with clear water and says: 'Say there is no god but me, so that I may give you to drink,' and they should make him have good opinion of Allah, due to the hadith of Muslim: 'Let none of you die except while he has good opinion of Allah,' i.e., he thinks that He will have mercy on him and pardon him, and the hadith of the two Sahihs: 'Allah says: I am as my servant thinks of Me.' (And they recite at his side Surah Ya-Sin) due to the hadith: 'Recite over your dead Ya-Sin,' narrated by Abu Dawud and Ibn Hibban and authenticated, and he said: What is meant is the one who is at the point of death, and the wisdom in its recitation is that the conditions of the Resurrection and the sending forth are mentioned in it, so its remembrance is renewed for him.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on the issue of talqin (prompting) and whether the dead can hear. The discussion begins with the statement that the literal meaning of a word cannot be abandoned without evidence. The hadith 'Prompt your dead' is interpreted by most Hanafi scholars as referring to the one near death, not the already deceased. The commentator, al-Kamal ibn al-Humam, explains that the dead do not hear according to the school, and addresses objections raised from the Prophet's address to the dead at Badr. Various answers are given: that incident was a miracle, a metaphor, or a special case. The hadith that the dead hear the sound of sandals is reconciled by limiting it to immediately after burial. From this, some scholars conclude that talqin after death is better, because then the word 'your dead' is literal. However, evidence for talqin at the time of death also exists. The author finally recommends talqin in the grave based on the reported practice of the Salaf. The passage ends with a prayer and transitions into recommendations for visiting the dying person.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqin): Prompting a dying or deceased person to recite the shahada.
ميت (mayyit): The deceased person.
حقيقة (haqiqah): Literal meaning of a word.
مجاز (majaz): Figurative meaning of a word.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, when is talqin recommended?
A) Only before death
B) After death and at the grave
C) At the moment of death only
D) Not recommended at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the dead do not hear and that talqin is recommended after burial, supported by the practice of the Salaf and reconciliation of conflicting evidence.

Mustahabb Actions for Relatives of the Dying Person
Lists recommended acts for relatives and neighbors of the dying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two recommended actions for relatives of a dying person and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Reciting Surah Ya-Sin comforts the dying by reminding them of the afterlife.

When a person is in the final moments of life, Islamic teachings recommend specific acts of care and worship. This lesson focuses on two mustahabb actions for relatives and neighbors: being present and reciting Surah Ya-Sin. The proof is a hadith that has been authenticated by scholars such as Ibn Hibban.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts
Read the passage and list the two recommended actions: entering upon the dying person and reciting Surah Ya-Sin.
Both are mustahabb, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith 'Recite over your dead Ya-Sin.' Note that this is transmitted by Abu Dawud and Ibn Hibban and authenticated.
The hadith is ahad, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the imperative 'اقرؤوا' indicates recommendation. Hanafis consider that without evidence of obligation, the imperative yields mustahabb.
The context of comforting the dying reinforces this.
4
Understand the wisdom
The passage explains that Surah Ya-Sin mentions the Resurrection and the afterlife, renewing the dying person's awareness.
This is a hikmah, not a condition for validity.

And it is recommended for the relatives of the dying person and his neighbors to enter upon him, and they recite at his side Surah Ya-Sin due to the hadith: 'Recite over your dead Ya-Sin,' narrated by Abu Dawud and Ibn Hibban and authenticated, and he said: What is meant is the one who is at the point of death, and the wisdom in its recitation is that the conditions of the Resurrection and the sending forth are mentioned in it, so its remembrance is renewed for him.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling indicating recommended actions (mustahabb) for those attending a dying person. It mentions two specific acts: (1) entering upon the dying person by his relatives and neighbors, which includes fulfilling his rights, comforting him, reminding him of beneficial matters like making a will, and giving him water to drink because thirst intensifies during death throes and the devil may tempt him. (2) Reciting Surah Ya-Sin at his side, based on the hadith 'Recite over your dead Ya-Sin.' The commentator clarifies that 'your dead' here means the one who is dying. The wisdom is that Surah Ya-Sin contains descriptions of the Resurrection and the afterlife, which renews the dying person's remembrance of these matters. The passage also mentions making the dying person have good opinion of Allah, based on the hadith 'Let none of you die except while he has good opinion of Allah.'

Key Terms

سورة يس (Surah Ya-Sin): The 36th chapter of the Quran.

Funeral Prayer: Ruling, Pillars, and Number of Takbirs
Defines the funeral prayer as fard kifayah, lists its pillars, and discusses the number of takbirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the funeral prayer as fard kifayah, identify its pillars, and explain why the Hanafi school holds four takbirs as the operative position.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer is fard kifayah, with four takbirs as pillars; the Prophet's final action abrogates earlier practices.

This lesson unpacks the ruling on the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) from Nur al-Idah and its commentary. You will learn why it is a communal obligation, what its pillars are, and how the Hanafi school resolves the dispute over the number of takbirs. The passage also examines whether the first takbir is a condition or a pillar, and the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the consensus of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage defines the funeral prayer as fard kifayah. Confirm the definition: a communal obligation that is fulfilled if some perform it, otherwise all are sinful. Contrast with fard 'ayn.
The proof is the Prophet's command, which indicates obligation per Hanafi usul.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the Prophet's statement: 'Pray over your companion.' In Hanafi usul, the imperative (amr) indicates wujub. Note that if it were fard 'ayn, the Prophet would have prayed over every deceased companion, but he did not.
Dalil type: Sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Determine the pillars and the nature of the first takbir
The text states that the pillars are the takbirs and standing. However, the first takbir is both a condition (shart) for entering the prayer and a pillar (rukn) because it replaces a rak'ah. Al-Kamal's view that supplication is a pillar is rebutted because the masbuq makes up takbirs without supplication.
The masbuq makes up missed takbirs consecutively without du'a to avoid lifting the funeral.
4
Analyze the dispute on the number of takbirs
The Hanafi school holds four takbirs. Ibn Abi Layla and a narration from Abu Yusuf say five. The reports of the Prophet's practice vary, but his last action was four takbirs, which abrogates earlier practices.
'Umar gathered the Companions to resolve the dispute, and they agreed on four.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is four takbirs, based on the Prophet's final action and the consensus of the Companions. The minority view of five is marjuh.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الصلاة على الميت الصَّلاةُ عليه فرضُ كفاية وأركانُها التكبيرات، والقيام. . فصل في الصلاة على الميت سببها الميت [ المسلم ] ، فإنها لقضاء حقه ، وصفة (الصَّلاةُ عليه) ككفنه ودفنه، وتجهيزه. (فرضُ كِفايةٍ) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « صَلُّوا عَلَى صَاحِبِكُمْ (٣) والأمر للوجوب، ولـو كـانـت فـرض عــيـن لصلى عليه النبي . ( وأركانها التكبيرات، والقيام) لكن التكبيرة الأولى شرط باعتبـار الشــروع بها، ركن باعتبار أنها قائمة مقام ركعة كباقي التكبيرات، وقال الكمال وأما أركانها فالذي يفهم من كلامهم أنها الدعاء والقيام والتكبير لقولهم: إن حقيقتها هي الدعاء وهو المقصود منها، انتهى قلت يعارضه قولهم: لو سبق كبر متوالياً خشية رفعها، فلو كان الدعاء ركناً ما جاز تركه بحال من غيـر مـا يقوم مقامه، وقد نص الكمال نفسه عليه بعد هذا بقوله: ثم المسبوق يقضي ما فاته من التكبيرات بعد سلام الإمام نسقاً بغير دعاء، لأنه لو قضاه به ترتفع الجنازة فتبطل الصلاة، لأنها لا تجوز إلا بحضورها، انتهى . ثم قال الكمال أيضاً: وقالوا: كل تكبيرة بمنزلة ركعة، وقالوا: يقدم الثناء، والصلاة على النبي لأنه سنة الدعاء (٣)، ولا يخفى أن التكبيرة الأولى شرط لأنها تكبيرة الإحرام، انتهى. وكأنه لا يقول بركنيتها، لأن الشرط غير المشروط، فيجعلها كتحريمة الصلاة الكاملة خارجة عن الحقيقة، فتكون شرطاً محضاً، والجواب ما قاله في « التاتارخانية ويكبر فيها أربع تكبيرات، وكـــان ابن أبي ليلى رحمه الله يقول: خمس تكبيرات، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف رحمه الله والآثــار واختلفت في فعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فروي الخمس والسبع والتسع وأكثر من ذلك، إلا أن آخر فعله كان أربع تكبيرات)، فكان ناسخاً لما قبله، وروي أن عمر الله جمع الصحابة حين اختلفوا فـي عــدد التكبيرات، وقال لهم: إنكم إذا اختلفتم فمن يأتي بعدكم أشَدُّ اختلافاً، فانظروا إلى آخــر صـلاة
Chapter on the Prayer over the Deceased. The prayer over him is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) and its pillars are the takbirs and standing. Chapter on the Prayer over the Deceased. Its cause is the deceased [Muslim], for it is to fulfill his right, and its description (the prayer over him) is like his shroud, burial, and preparation. (It is a communal obligation) because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Pray over your companion' and the command indicates obligation. If it were an individual obligation, the Prophet would have prayed over him. (And its pillars are the takbirs and standing). However, the first takbir is a condition with regard to commencing with it, and a pillar in that it stands in place of a rak'ah like the other takbirs. Al-Kamal said: As for its pillars, what is understood from their statements is that they are supplication, standing, and takbir, because they said: Its reality is supplication, and that is its purpose. End quote. I say this is contradicted by their saying: If one says takbir consecutively fearing its removal, if supplication were a pillar, it would not be permissible to leave it under any circumstances without something taking its place. Al-Kamal himself stated after this: Then the one who is behind (masbuq) makes up what he missed of the takbirs after the imam's salam consecutively without supplication, because if he made it up with supplication the funeral would be lifted and the prayer invalidated, for it is not permissible except with its presence. End quote. Then al-Kamal also said: They said: Each takbir is like a rak'ah. They said: One begins with praise and salutation upon the Prophet because it is the sunnah of supplication. It is not hidden that the first takbir is a condition because it is the takbir of ihram. End quote. It is as if he does not consider it a pillar, because the condition is other than the conditioned, so he makes it like the tahrimah of the complete prayer, external to the reality, thus it is a pure condition. The response is what is said in 'al-Tatarkhaniyyah': One makes four takbirs. Ibn Abi Layla used to say: five takbirs, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf. The reports differed regarding the action of the Messenger of Allah; five, seven, nine, and more are reported, except that his last action was four takbirs, so it abrogated what came before. It is narrated that 'Umar gathered the Companions when they differed over the number of takbirs and said: If you differ, then those after you will differ more severely. Look at the last prayer
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The author states that the prayer is fard kifayah (communal obligation), meaning if enough people perform it, the obligation is lifted from all. The proof is the Prophet's command 'Pray over your companion,' which is an imperative indicating obligation. If it were fard 'ayn, the Prophet himself would have prayed over every deceased companion, but he did not. The pillars (arkan) of the funeral prayer are the takbirs and standing (qiyam). However, there is a detailed discussion regarding the nature of the first takbir. Some scholars consider it a condition (shart) for entering the prayer, similar to the takbirat al-ihram in regular prayer, while others consider it a pillar (rukn). Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam noted that the essence of the funeral prayer is supplication (du'a), so the pillars are du'a, standing, and takbir. But the author points out a contradiction: if du'a were a pillar, it could not be omitted even in a make-up (qada') situation. Yet, the masbuq (latecomer) makes up missed takbirs without du'a because the funeral would be lifted, invalidating the prayer. Thus, takbirs are the pillars. The first takbir is both a condition (as it initiates the prayer) and a pillar (as it replaces a rak'ah). The disagreement on the number of takbirs is then discussed: the Hanafi school holds four, based on the Prophet's final practice (which is abrogating). Ibn Abi Layla and one narration from Abu Yusuf say five. The passage ends with the story of 'Umar gathering the Companions to settle the dispute.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (farḍ kifāyah): A collective obligation: if performed by some Muslims, the obligation is lifted from the rest.
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbīrat al-iḥrām): The first 'Allahu Akbar' that initiates the prayer; in funeral prayer, it functions as both condition and pillar.
مسبوق (masbūq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late, missing one or more parts; in funeral prayer, one who misses takbirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon number of takbirs in the Hanafi funeral prayer?
A) Five takbirs
B) Four takbirs
C) Seven takbirs
D) Three takbirs

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) with four takbirs and standing as its pillars, and the Prophet's final practice of four takbirs is the abrogating evidence for the Hanafi position.

Salat al-Janazah: Obligation and Pillars
Defines prayer over deceased as fard kifayah and its pillars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Janazah as fard kifayah, identify its pillars (arkan) according to the Hanafi school, and explain the dual status of the first takbir.

Core Idea
Salat al-Janazah is fard kifayah; its pillars are the takbirs and standing, with the first takbir serving both as a condition and a pillar.

In this lesson, we explore the opening of the chapter on Salat al-Janazah from Nur al-Idah. The text establishes the prayer as a communal obligation (fard kifayah) supported by the Prophet's command, then defines its essential pillars. A subtle point of Hanafi fiqh arises: is the first takbir a condition or a pillar? The passage resolves this by affirming its dual role.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its evidence
The text declares prayer over the deceased as fard kifayah and cites the hadith 'Pray over your companion.' Analyze how the command indicates obligation, but the Prophet's practice shows it is not fard 'ayn.
The hadith is ahad, so it gives zanni thubut but qati dalalah per Hanafi usul.
2
List the pillars (arkan)
The pillars are the takbirs (four according to the relied-upon view) and standing (qiyam). Note that the first takbir has a dual role.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf about the first takbir
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Kamal) consider the first takbir a pure condition; others consider it a pillar. The text explains it is both: condition as the takbir al-ihram, pillar because it stands in place of a rak'ah.
Al-Kamal's view is mentioned but the mufta bihi is the dual view.
4
Refute the notion that supplication is a pillar
The passage uses the example of a latecomer making up takbirs without supplication to prove that supplication is not a pillar.
If supplication were a pillar, it could never be omitted.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that the pillars are the takbirs and standing; the first takbir is both a condition and a pillar.
This is the position in al-Tatarkhaniyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الصلاة على الميت
الصَّلاةُ عليه فرضُ كفاية وأركانُها التكبيرات، والقيام. .
فصل في الصلاة على الميت
سببها الميت [ المسلم ] ، فإنها لقضاء حقه ، وصفة (الصَّلاةُ عليه) ككفنه ودفنه، وتجهيزه. (فرضُ كِفايةٍ) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « صَلُّوا عَلَى صَاحِبِكُمْ » والأمر للوجوب، ولـو كـانـت فـرض عــيـن لصلى عليه النبي . ( وأركانها التكبيرات، والقيام) لكن التكبيرة الأولى شرط باعتبـار الشــروع بها، ركن باعتبار أنها قائمة مقام ركعة كباقي التكبيرات، وقال الكمال وأما أركانها فالذي يفهم من كلامهم أنها الدعاء والقيام والتكبير لقولهم: إن حقيقتها هي الدعاء وهو المقصود منها، انتهى قلت يعارضه قولهم: لو سبق كبر متوالياً خشية رفعها، فلو كان الدعاء ركناً ما جاز تركه بحال من غـيـر مـا يقوم مقامه، وقد نص الكمال نفسه عليه بعد هذا بقوله: ثم المسبوق يقضي ما فاته من التكبيرات بعد سلام الإمام نسقاً بغير دعاء، لأنه لو قضاه به ترتفع الجنازة فتبطل الصلاة، لأنها لا تجوز إلا بحضورها، انتهى . ثم قال الكمال أيضاً: وقالوا: كل تكبيرة بمنزلة ركعة، وقالوا: يقدم الثناء، والصلاة على النبي لأنه سنة الدعاء، ولا يخفى أن التكبيرة الأولى شرط لأنها تكبيرة الإحرام، انتهى. وكأنه لا يقول بركنيتها، لأن الشرط غير المشروط، فيجعلها كتحريمة الصلاة الكاملة خارجة عن الحقيقة، فتكون شرطاً محضاً، والجواب ما قاله في « التاتارخانية
Chapter on the prayer over the deceased. Prayer over him is a communal obligation. Its pillars are the takbirs and standing. The prayer over the deceased is a communal obligation due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Pray over your companion.' The command indicates obligation. Had it been an individual obligation, the Prophet would have prayed over him. Its pillars are the takbirs and standing, but the first takbir is a condition with regard to beginning with it, and a pillar with regard to it standing in place of a rak'ah like the other takbirs. Al-Kamal said: As for its pillars, what is understood from their statements is that they are supplication, standing, and takbir, because they said: Its reality is supplication, and that is its purpose. I say: This is contradicted by their statement: If one fears its lifting, he may recite takbirs consecutively. If supplication were a pillar, it would not be permissible to leave it entirely without something substituting for it. Al-Kamal himself stated after this: Then the latecomer makes up what he missed of the takbirs after the imam's salam consecutively without supplication, because if he makes it up with supplication, the bier would be lifted and the prayer invalidated, since it is not permissible except in its presence. Then al-Kamal also said: They said: Every takbir is like a rak'ah. And they said: One begins with praise and salawat upon the Prophet because it is a sunna of supplication. It is clear that the first takbir is a condition because it is the takbir of ihram. It is as if he does not consider it a pillar, because the condition is not the conditioned, so he makes it like the tahrima of the complete prayer, outside the reality, being a pure condition. The answer is what is said in al-Tatarkhaniyya.
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on Salat al-Janazah, stating its ruling and pillars. The author first declares that the prayer over a deceased Muslim is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), supported by the Prophet's command 'Pray over your companion.' The command indicates obligation (wujub), and it is not an individual obligation because the Prophet himself did not pray over every deceased companion, as his prayer would have been required if it were fard 'ayn. The pillars (arkan) of this prayer are the takbirs (four according to the relied-upon view) and standing (qiyam). The commentary then addresses a nuance: there is a discussion whether the first takbir is a condition (shart) or a pillar (rukn). Some, like al-Kamal, argue that the first takbir is a condition because it is the takbir al-ihram, while others hold it is a pillar because it stands in place of a rak'ah. The author reconciles this by noting that the first takbir has both aspects: as the opening it is a condition, and as part of the sequence it is a pillar. The discussion includes refuting the view that supplication (du'a) is a pillar, since in certain cases supplication is omitted (e.g., a latecomer making up missed takbirs without supplication to avoid lifting the bier), proving supplication is not a pillar. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the pillars are the takbirs and standing, not supplication.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation; if some perform it, the obligation drops from the rest.
ركن (rukn): An integral part of the prayer; omission invalidates it.
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbir al-ihram): The first takbir that initiates the prayer; it is a condition (shart) for entering the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of Salat al-Janazah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Fard kifayah
C) Wajib
D) Sunnah mu'akkadah

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Janazah is a communal obligation; its pillars are the takbirs and standing, and the first takbir uniquely serves as both a condition and a pillar.

The Number of Takbirs in Salat al-Janazah
Discusses the differing opinions on the number of takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the number of takbirs in Salat al-Janazah and evaluate the counter-argument based on the first takbir being for opening.

Core Idea
Four takbirs is the relied-upon sunnah; the first takbir counts as one of them.

The number of takbirs in the funeral prayer has been a subject of early disagreement. The Hanafi school, following the final practice of the Prophet and the consensus of the Companions under 'Umar, firmly holds that four takbirs are the sunnah. This lesson explores the proofs and the reasoning behind the Hanafi position, especially the response to the argument that the first takbir should not be counted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the number of takbirs as per the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
The text clearly says four.
2
Examine the opposing view
Understand the argument of Ibn Abi Layla and the narration from Abu Yusuf supporting five takbirs.
Their key point: the first takbir is only for opening.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
See why the Hanafi school counts the first takbir as one of the four, using the concept of naskh and each takbir standing for a rak'ah.
The Prophet's final practice abrogates earlier ones.
4
Note the practical implication (thamarah al-khilaf)
Understand the difference: one extra takbir does not invalidate but is contrary to the sunnah.
The prayer is valid with five, but the preferred is four.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكبر فيها أربع تكبيرات، وكـــان ابن أبي ليلى رحمه الله يقول: خمس تكبيرات، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف رحمه الله والآثــار واختلفت في فعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فروي الخمس والسبع والتسع وأكثر من ذلك، إلا أن آخر فعله كان أربع تكبيرات)، فكان ناسخاً لما قبله، وروي أن عمر الله جمع الصحابة حين اختلفوا فـي عــدد التكبيرات، وقال لهم: إنكم إذا اختلفتم فمن يأتي بعدكم أشَدُّ اختلافاً، فانظروا إلى آخــر صـلاة صلاها رسول الله الله على جنازة فخذوا بذلك، فوجدوه صلى على امرأة وكبر فيها أربعاً، فاتفقوا على ذلك، وروي عن العالي له أنه كبر أربعاً أيضاً، ولأن كل تكبيرة منها قائمة مقــام ركعة، ثـم الصلاة [ المعهودة لا تزيد على أربع تكبيرات، إلا أن ابن ليلي رحمه الله قال: التكبيرة الأولى للافتتاح، فينبغي أن يكون بعدها أربع تكبيرات كل تكبيرة قائمة مقام ركعة، كما في الظهر والعصر والجواب: أن التكبيرة الأولى وإن كانت للافتتاح، ولكن بهذا لا يخرج من أن تكون تكبيراً، أي: قائماً مقام ركعة ، وفي فتاوى الحجة » الأمي، والهنود الذين لا يعلمون الأدعية، يكبر أربــع تكبيرات ويسلم تجوز صلاته، لأن الأركان فيها التكبيرات انتهى. وقد قال الكمال بـعـد هـذا رحمـه الله: قال في « الكافي»: إلا أن أبا يوسف يقول: في التكبيرة الأولى معنيان معنى الافتتاح والـقـيـام مقام ركعة، ومعنى الافتتاح يترجح فيها، ولذا خصت برفع اليدين انتهى. وقال صاحب « البحر » : وفيه أي: كلام الكمال نظر، لأن المصرح به بخلافه، قال في المحيط ) : وأما ركنها فالتكبيرات والقيام، وأما سننها فالتحميد والثناء والدعاء فيها، انتهى. وذكر غير ذلك ، فالذي تلخص هـو الـذي قلناه متناً بحمد الله.
And he makes four takbirs in it. Ibn Abi Layla used to say: five takbirs, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf. The traditions differed regarding the action of the Messenger of Allah; five, seven, nine, and more are reported, except that his final action was four takbirs, so it abrogated what came before. It is narrated that 'Umar gathered the Companions when they differed about the number of takbirs and said to them: 'If you differ, then those after you will differ more severely. Look at the last prayer the Messenger of Allah prayed over a funeral and take that.' They found that he prayed over a woman and made four takbirs, so they agreed upon that. It is also narrated from 'Ali that he made four takbirs. And because each takbir is in place of a rak'ah, then the customary prayer does not exceed four takbirs. However, Ibn Abi Layla said: The first takbir is for opening, so after it there should be four takbirs, each standing in place of a rak'ah, as in Zuhr and 'Asr. The answer: The first takbir, even if for opening, does not exit from being a takbir, i.e., it stands in place of a rak'ah. In Fatawa al-Hujja: The unlettered and Indians who do not know the supplications make four takbirs and say salam; their prayer is valid because the pillars are the takbirs. Al-Kamal said after this: In al-Kafi: Except that Abu Yusuf says: In the first takbir there are two meanings: the meaning of opening and standing in place of a rak'ah; the meaning of opening is preponderant in it, thus it is singled out for raising the hands. The author of al-Bahr said: There is a problem with this speech of al-Kamal, because what is explicitly stated is contrary to it. In al-Muhit: As for its pillars, they are the takbirs and standing; as for its sunan, they are praise, thana', and supplication. And he mentioned other than that. So what is summarized is what we have stated in the matn, by the grace of Allah.
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of takbirs in Salat al-Janazah. The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is four takbirs, as established by the final practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). This is supported by the consensus of the Companions under Caliph 'Umar, who investigated the last janazah prayer of the Prophet and found it to be four takbirs. The passage also discusses a narration from Ibn Abi Layla (a Hanafi scholar) and a narration from Abu Yusuf suggesting five takbirs. The opponents argue that the first takbir is only for opening (ifititah) and not a pillar like a rak'ah, but the Hanafi response is that it still stands in place of a rak'ah and is counted as one of the four. The text also notes that for those who do not know the supplications, making four takbirs and saying salam suffices because the pillars are the takbirs themselves. The discussion concludes by affirming the matn (Nur al-Idah) position of four takbirs, with the view of al-Bahr criticizing al-Kamal's nuance. This shows that the Hanafi school firmly adheres to four takbirs.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation; the later practice of the Prophet (four takbirs) abrogated earlier practices of more takbirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Four
C) Five
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school firmly adopts four takbirs in Salat al-Janazah, based on the Prophet's final practice and the Companions' consensus, with the first takbir counting as one of the four.

Six Conditions of Salat al-Janazah
Lists and explains conditions of janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first four conditions for the validity of Salat al-Janazah and explain the evidence for the condition of Islam.

Core Idea
Salat al-Janazah requires the deceased to be Muslim, pure, present, and placed in front.

This lesson focuses on the conditions that must be met for the funeral prayer to be valid. While the prayer is a collective obligation (fard kifayah), its validity depends on the state of the deceased and the arrangement of the prayer. The text lists four out of six conditions, starting with Islam of the deceased, supported by a clear Quranic prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being conditioned
Recognize that the conditions are for Salat al-Janazah, a fard kifayah prayer. The conditions are external prerequisites (shurut) for validity.
Not to be confused with pillars (arkan) of the prayer.
2
List the known conditions from the passage
From the text, extract the four conditions mentioned: Islam of the deceased, his purity, his placement in front of the congregation, and his presence.
The passage is incomplete; two more conditions are missing.
3
Examine the evidence for the first condition
The text cites Quran 9:84 prohibiting prayer over hypocrites, who are disbelievers. The reasoning is that the prayer is intercession and honor, which a non-Muslim does not deserve.
The dalil block in this lesson explains the wajh al-dalalah.
4
Understand the details and exceptions for purity
The purity condition includes the body, clothing, and place of the deceased. However, there is leniency regarding impurity of the ground if the deceased is on a bier or shrouded.
This shows the Hanafi approach of balancing principle with practicality.
5
Comprehend the condition of presence
The deceased must be physically present; prayer over an absent person is invalid. The Prophet's prayer over the Negus is explained as a case where the bier was raised, making it effectively present.
This condition is unique to the Hanafi school; others may allow prayer over absent deceased.

(وَ) الرابع: (حَضُورُهُ) فلا تصح الصلاة علـى غائب، وأما «صلاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم علـى النجاشي فكانت إما لأنه رفع له سريره حتى رآه عليه الصلاة والسلام بحضرته ، فتكــون صـلاة مـن
And its conditions are six: Islam of the deceased, his purity, his placement in front, and his presence. First: Islam of the deceased, due to His statement: 'And never pray over any of them who dies' [9:84] meaning the hypocrites, who are disbelievers, and because it is intercession for the deceased as an honor and a request for forgiveness, and the disbeliever is not benefited by intercession nor deserving of honor. Second: His purity, because the deceased has the ruling of the imam, and likewise the purity of his place. Al-Qunyah said: Purity from impurity in clothing, body, and place, and covering the 'awrah is a condition for both the imam and the deceased. In al-Fawa'id al-Tajiyyah: If the deceased is on a bier, there is no doubt that it is permissible if the place is impure; without a bier there is no narration, and it should be permissible because the purity of the deceased's place is not a condition, since he is not performing the prayer. It is said: because his shroud is a barrier between him and the ground. Third: His placement in front of the people; so the prayer is not permissible if they place him behind them. He also has the ruling of a follower (mu'tam) because it is permissible to pray over a woman and a boy; thus he is given the ruling of the imam as long as he is not buried, as we will mention. Fourth: His presence; so the prayer over an absent person is not valid. As for the Prophet's prayer over the Negus, it was either because his bier was raised until he saw it in his presence, so it becomes a prayer from
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage enumerates the six conditions for the validity of Salat al-Janazah. The text presents four of them (Islam, purity, placement in front, presence) but the sixth is cut off in the OCR. The first condition is that the deceased must be a Muslim, as proven by the Quranic verse forbidding prayer over hypocrites (who are disbelievers). The second condition is the ritual purity (tahara) of the deceased, similar to the purity required for the imam. This includes purity from najasa on the body, clothing, and place, though there is a leniency regarding the impurity of the ground if the deceased is on a bier or shrouded. The third condition is that the deceased must be placed in front of the congregation; if placed behind, the prayer is invalid. The deceased also has the status of a follower (mu'tam) but with the ruling of an imam in certain respects. The fourth condition is that the deceased must be present physically; prayer over an absent person (gha'ib) is not valid. The text mentions the exceptional case of the Prophet's prayer over the Negus (an-Najashi), which is explained as either the bier being raised so the Prophet saw it, making it effectively a prayer over a present deceased.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition for validity; if missing, the prayer is not valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Quran 9:84 forbidding prayer over hypocrites
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy to zakat

Key Takeaway
The validity of Salat al-Janazah depends on the deceased meeting four conditions: Islam, purity, being present, and being placed in front of the congregation.

Conditions of Janazah Prayer
Lists six conditions for janazah prayer with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions of janazah prayer and apply each condition to determine the validity of the prayer in given scenarios.

Core Idea
Janazah prayer has six conditions; missing any makes the prayer invalid.

The janazah prayer is a collective obligation with specific conditions that must be present for its validity. Building on the foundation of the earlier discussion on takbirs, the author now enumerates six conditions derived from Quran and sunnah. Understanding these conditions helps ensure the prayer is performed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify each condition
List the six conditions named: Islam of the deceased, purity, the deceased in front, presence of the deceased, the one praying not riding (without excuse), and the deceased placed on the ground.
These are prerequisites for validity.
2
Examine the proof for each condition
For each condition, note the dalil cited. For 'Islam of the deceased', the Quranic verse 9:84 is provided. For others, analogical reasoning or general principles are used.
The proof strengthens the ruling.
3
Distinguish conditions from pillars and sunan
Conditions are external prerequisites; pillars (takbirs, standing) are integral parts; sunan are recommended acts. Omitting a condition invalidates the prayer, omitting a pillar invalidates, omitting a sunnah does not.
This classification is key in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
Consider a case where the deceased is placed behind the congregation. According to condition three, the prayer would be invalid because the deceased must be in front.
Practice applying each condition.
5
Note exceptions and details
The text mentions exceptions for presence (most of body or half with head counts) and excuses for riding or lack of ground placement.
These nuances are important for accurate application.

صلاها رسول الله الله على جنازة فخذوا بذلك، فوجدوه صلى على امرأة وكبر فيها أربعاً، فاتفقوا على ذلك ) ، وروي عن العالي له أنه كبر أربعاً(۳) أيضاً، ولأن كل تكبيرة منها قائمة مقــام ركعة، ثـم الصلاة [ المعهودة لا تزيد على أربع تكبيرات، إلا أن ابن ليلي رحمه الله قال: التكبيرة الأولى للافتتاح، فينبغي أن يكون بعدها أربع تكبيرات كل تكبيرة قائمة مقام ركعة، كما في الظهر والعصر والجواب: أن التكبيرة الأولى وإن كانت للافتتاح، ولكن بهذا لا يخرج من أن تكون تكبيراً، أي: قائماً مقام ركعة ، وفي فتاوى الحجة » الأمي، والهنود الذين لا يعلمون الأدعية، يكبر أربــع تكبيرات ويسلم تجوز صلاته، لأن الأركان فيها التكبيرات انتهى. وقد قال الكمال بـعـد هـذا رحمـه الله: قال في « الكافي»: إلا أن أبا يوسف يقول: في التكبيرة الأولى معنيان معنى الافتتاح والـقـيـام مقام ركعة، ومعنى الافتتاح يترجح فيها، ولذا خصت برفع اليدين انتهى. وقال صاحب « البحر » : وفيه أي: كلام الكمال نظر، لأن المصرح به بخلافه، قال في المحيط ) : وأما ركنها فالتكبيرات والقيام، وأما سننها فالتحميد والثناء والدعاء فيها، انتهى. وذكر غير ذلك ، فالذي تلخص هـو الـذي قلناه متناً بحمد الله. وشرائطهَا [ ستة ])، أولها: (إسلام الميت)، لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا تُصَلِّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِّنْهُم مات أبدا [ البوم : ٨٤] يعني المنافقين، وهم الكفرة، ولأنها شفاعة للميت إكراماً له، وطلباً للمغفرة، والكافر لا تنفعه شفاعة، ولا يستحق الإكرام. (وَ) الثاني: (طهارتُهُ) لأن الميـت لـه حـكـم الإمام وكذا طهارة مكانه. قال في « القنية»: الطهارة من النجاسة في الثوب والبدن والمكان، وستر العورة شرط في حق الإمام والميت جميعاً، انتهى. وفي ( الفوائد التاجية»: إن كان الميت على جنازة لاشك أنه يجوز لو كان مكانها نجساً، وبغير جنازة لا رواية فيه، وينبغي أن تجوز لأن طهارة مكان الميت لیست بشرط، لأنه ليس بمؤد، وقيل: لأن كفنه حائل بينه وبين الأرض، لأنه ليس بلابس بل ملبس، انتهى كذا في شرح المقدسي » . (وَ) الثالث: (تقدُّمُهُ) أمام القوم، فلا تجوز الصلاة عليه لو وضعـــوه خلفهم، وله حكم المؤتم أيضاً، لجواز الصلاة على المرأة والصبي، فيعطى حكم الإمـام مـا لـم يدفن كما سنذكره. (وَ) الرابع: (حَضُورُهُ) فلا تصح الصلاة علـى غائب، وأما «صلاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم علـى النجاشي فكانت إما لأنه رفع له سريره حتى رآه عليه الصلاة والسلام بحضرته ، فتكــون صـلاة مـن خلفه على ميت يراه الإمام وبحضرته دون المأمومين، وهذا غير مانع من صحة الاقتداء، وإما أن ذلك خص به النجاشي، فلا يلحق به غيره كما في «الفتح» ، وفيه نزل جبريل عليه السلام [ بتبوك] فقال: يا رسول الله إن معاوية بن المزني مات بالمدينة، أتحب أن أطوي لك الأرض فتصلي عليه، قال: نعم، فضرب بجناحيه على الأرض فرفع له سريره فصلى عليه، وخلفـه صفــان مـن الملائكة عليهم السلام، في كل صف سبعون ألف ملك، ثم رجع، فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام لـجـبـريـل عـلـيـه السلام: «بم أدرك هذا؟ قال: بحبه سورة قُلْ هُوَ اللَّهُ أَحَدٌ﴾ [ الإخلافِن : ۱] وقراءته إياها جائياً وذاهباً وقائماً وقاعداً وعلى كل حال » )، (أو حضور أكثر بَدَنِهِ، أو نصفه مع رأسه) كما تقدم. (وَ) الخامس: (كَوْنُ المُصلِّي عليها غير راكب) وغير قاعد (بلا عذر ، لأن القيام فيها ركن، فلا يترك بـلا عذر. (و) السادس: (كونُ المَيِّتِ موضوعاً (عَلَى الأرض)، لكونه كالإمام من وجه، (فإن كان على دابَّةٍ، أو على أيدي النَّاسِ، لم تجز الصَّلاةُ على المختار، إلا إن كان (من عذر) كذا في « التبيين». ( وسنتها، أربع ) : الأولى (قيام الإمام بحذَاء) صدر (المَيِّتِ، ذَكَرَاً كان الميت (أو أنثى)؛ لأن الصدر موضع القلب، وفيه نور الإيمان فيكون القيام عنده إشارة إلى الشفاعة لإيمانه، وهذا «ظاهر الرواية»، وهو بيان الاستحباب كما سبق، فلو وقف في غيره أجزأه، كذا في «البحر» عن «كافي الحاكم». (و) الثانية : ( الثَّناءُ بعد التكبيرة الأولى فيقول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك إلى آخره، وجازت قراءة الفاتحة بقصد الثناء، كذا نُصَّ عليه عندنا ، وفي ( البخاري» عــن ابـن عبـاس أنـه صلى على جنازة فقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب وقال: لتعلموا أنه من السنة)، وصححه الترمذي. (و) الثالثة: ( الصَّلاةُ على سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعــد) التكبيرة (الثانية) فيقول: اللهم صل على محمد وعلى آل محمد... إلخ، والبداءة بالثناء ثم الصلاة على النبي له سنة الدعاء (۳) لأنه أرجي للقبول.
The Messenger of Allah prayed over a funeral, so take that. They found he prayed over a woman and made four takbirs, so they agreed on that. And it is narrated from al-Ali that he made four takbirs also. And because each takbir stands in place of a rak'ah, then the customary prayer does not exceed four takbirs. Except that Ibn Layla said: The first takbir is for the opening, so there should be four takbirs after it, each standing in place of a rak'ah, as in Zuhr and Asr. The answer: The first takbir, even though it is for the opening, does not exit from being a takbir, i.e., standing in place of a rak'ah. And in the Fatawa al-Hujjah: The illiterate and the Hindus who do not know the supplications, they make four takbirs and say the salam, their prayer is valid, because the pillars are the takbirs. End quote. And al-Kamal said after this: He said in al-Kafi: Except that Abu Yusuf says: In the first takbir there are two meanings: the meaning of opening and standing in place of a rak'ah, and the meaning of opening is preponderant in it, so it is specified with raising the hands. End quote. And the author of al-Bahr said: In it, i.e., the speech of al-Kamal, there is consideration, because what is explicitly stated is contrary to it. He said in al-Muhit: As for its pillars, they are the takbirs and standing. As for its sunan, they are al-hamd, al-thana, and supplication in it. End quote. And he mentioned other than that. So what is summarized is what we stated in the matn, praise be to Allah. And its conditions are six: First: (Islam of the deceased) due to His statement: {And never pray over any of them who dies} [al-Tawbah 84] meaning the hypocrites, and they are disbelievers. And because it is intercession for the deceased as an honor for him and a request for forgiveness, and the disbeliever does not benefit from intercession nor does he deserve honor. Second: (His purity) because the deceased has the ruling of the imam, and likewise purity of his place. He said in al-Qunyah: Purity from impurity in garment, body, and place, and covering the 'awrah are conditions for both the imam and the deceased. End quote. And in al-Fawa'id al-Tajiyyah: If the deceased is on a bier, there is no doubt that it is allowed even if its place is impure. And without a bier there is no narration about it, and it should be allowed because purity of the place of the deceased is not a condition because he is not performing the prayer. And it is said: Because his shroud is a barrier between him and the ground, because he is not a wearer but worn. End quote, as in Sharh al-Maqdisi. Third: (His being in front) of the people, so it is not valid to pray over him if they place him behind them. And he also has the ruling of the follower, because it is allowed to pray over a woman and a boy, so he is given the ruling of the imam as long as he is not buried, as we will mention. Fourth: (His presence) so prayer over an absent person is not valid. As for the Prophet's prayer over al-Najashi, it was either because his bier was raised until he saw it, so it was a prayer of one behind him over a deceased that the imam saw and was present with him but not the followers, and this does not prevent the validity of following. Or that it was specific to al-Najashi, so others are not analogized to him, as in al-Fath. And in it, Jibril descended at Tabuk and said: O Messenger of Allah, Mu'awiyah ibn al-Muzni died in Medina, do you want me to fold the earth for you so you can pray over him? He said: Yes. So he struck his wings on the earth and raised his bier, and he prayed over him, and behind him were two rows of angels, in each row seventy thousand angels. Then he returned. The Prophet said to Jibril: How did he attain this? He said: By his love for Surah Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad and his recitation of it coming and going, standing and sitting, and in every state. (Or presence of most of his body, or half with his head) as mentioned. Fifth: (The one praying not being a rider) nor sitting (without excuse, because standing in it is a pillar, so it is not left without excuse). Sixth: (The deceased being placed on the ground), because he is like the imam in some respects. (If he is on an animal or on people's hands, the prayer is not valid, according to the chosen opinion, except due to an excuse) as in al-Tabyin. And its sunan are four: First: (The imam standing opposite the chest of the deceased, whether male or female) because the chest is the place of the heart, and in it is the light of faith, so standing near it indicates intercession for his faith. This is the apparent narration, and it indicates recommendation as before. So if he stands elsewhere, it suffices him, as in al-Bahr from Kafi al-Hakim. Second: (Al-thana after the first takbir, saying Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika to the end. And it is permissible to recite al-Fatihah with the intention of thana, as is explicitly stated with us. And in al-Bukhari from Ibn Abbas that he prayed over a funeral and recited al-Fatihah and said: So that you know that it is from the Sunnah. Al-Tirmidhi authenticated it. Third: (The salat upon our master the Prophet after the second takbir), saying Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad... etc. And beginning with thana then salat upon the Prophet is the sunnah of supplication because it is more hopeful for acceptance.
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion probe on the rulings of Salat al-Janazah (funeral prayer). It begins with a discussion on the number of takbirs (four according to Hanafis), refuting the view of Ibn Layla who advocated five (one for iftitah plus four). The Hanafi position is that the first takbir serves both as the opening and as one of the four pillars. A subordinate issue: an illiterate person or someone who does not know the supplications may simply perform four takbirs and say the salam; the prayer is valid because the takbirs themselves are the pillars. The author then lists six conditions (shurut) for the prayer's validity: (1) the deceased must be Muslim, citing Quran 9:84; (2) purity of the deceased and the place, with the deceased having the same ruling as the imam regarding purity and covering the 'awrah; (3) the deceased must be in front of the imam and followers; (4) the deceased must be present (not absent), with the case of the Prophet's prayer over al-Najashi explained either as a virtual presence or a special dispensation; (5) the person praying must not be riding without excuse; (6) the deceased must be placed on the ground. After the conditions, the passage presents four sunnan (recommended acts): (1) the imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased for both men and women; (2) reciting al-thana (Subhanaka) after the first takbir, and reciting al-Fatihah is permissible as thana; (3) reciting salat upon the Prophet after the second takbir; (4) the order of thana then salat. The commentary stays within the Hanafi madhhab, noting the 'zahir al-riwayah' for the standing position and citing the relevant hadith sources.

Key Terms
الشرائط (al-shurūṭ): The conditions that must be present for the janazah prayer to be valid; without them the prayer is invalid.
السنن (al-sunan): Recommended acts in the janazah prayer; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but leaves it incomplete in perfection.
طهارة (ṭahārah): Purity from physical impurities (najāsa) in garment, body, and place. For janazah, the deceased must be pure, as well as the place of prayer.
حضور (ḥuḍūr): Physical presence of the deceased; prayer over an absent person is invalid. Exceptions exist for special cases like the Prophet's prayer over al-Najashi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the validity of janazah prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) The deceased must be Muslim.
B) The deceased must be present physically.
C) The imam must be in a state of wudu.
D) The deceased must be placed on the ground.

Key Takeaway
The six conditions for janazah prayer are: Muslim deceased, purity, deceased in front, presence, non-rider/non-sitting without excuse, and deceased on ground.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Sunan of Janazah Prayer and the Ruling on Takbirs
States four sunan and resolves a dispute on the number of takbirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four sunan of janazah prayer and explain the Hanafi ruling on the number of takbirs, including the dispute with Ibn Layla.

Core Idea
The janazah prayer has four takbirs (pillars) and four sunan; the first takbir serves both as opening and as one of the four pillars.

After establishing the conditions for validity, the author turns to the sunan (recommended acts) and also delves into a key dispute about the number of takbirs. The Hanafi position holds that there are four takbirs, each standing in place of a rak'ah. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct performance and for appreciating the school's internal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunan
List the four sunan: 1) imam stands opposite the chest, 2) thana after first takbir, 3) salat after second takbir, 4) order of thana then salat. Note that these are recommended, not obligatory.
Some Hanafi texts consider thana and salat as wajib (obligatory), but this passage classifies them as sunan.
2
Understand the takbir dispute
Ibn Layla argued for five takbirs (one for iftitah plus four). The Hanafi response: the first takbir is both opening and a pillar, so total four. This is based on practice of the Prophet and Companions.
The dispute is cited to reinforce the Hanafi view, not to present ambiguity.
3
Analyze the proof for four takbirs
The text mentions that each takbir stands in place of a rak'ah, and customary prayer does not exceed four takbirs. Also narrations of the Prophet praying four takbirs are referenced.
The proof is a combination of hadith and reasoning.
4
Distinguish between sunan and arkan
The sunan are the recommended recitations and standing position. The arkan are the takbirs and standing. Omitting a sunnah does not invalidate; omitting a takbir invalidates.
This is a key Hanafi point: the recitations are not pillars.
5
Note the subordinate ruling for the illiterate
An illiterate person or someone who does not know the supplications may simply perform four takbirs and say salam; the prayer is valid because the pillars are the takbirs.
This illustrates the principle that the takbirs are the core.
