(وَ) الخامس: (كَوْنُ المُصلِّي عليها غير راكب) وغير قاعد (بلا عذر ، لأن القيام فيها ركن، فلا يترك بـلا عذر. (و) السادس: (كونُ المَيِّتِ موضوعاً (عَلَى الأرض)، لكونه كالإمام من وجه، (فإن كان على دابَّةٍ، أو على أيدي النَّاسِ، لم تجز الصَّلاةُ على المختار، إلا إن كان (من عذر) كذا في « التبيين». ( وسنتها، أربع ) : الأولى (قيام الإمام بحذَاء) صدر (المَيِّتِ، ذَكَرَاً كان الميت (أو أنثى)؛ لأن الصدر موضع القلب، وفيه نور الإيمان فيكون القيام عنده إشارة إلى الشفاعة لإيمانه، وهذا «ظاهر الرواية»، وهو بيان الاستحباب كما سبق، فلو وقف في غيره أجزأه، كذا في «البحر» عن «كافي الحاكم». (و) الثانية : ( الثَّناءُ بعد التكبيرة الأولى فيقول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك إلى آخره، وجازت قراءة الفاتحة بقصد الثناء، كذا نُصَّ عليه عندنا ، وفي ( البخاري» عــن ابـن عبـاس أنـه صلى على جنازة فقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب وقال: لتعلموا أنه من السنة)، وصححه الترمذي. (و) الثالثة: ( الصَّلاةُ على سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعــد) التكبيرة (الثانية) فيقول: اللهم صل على محمد وعلى آل محمد... إلخ، والبداءة بالثناء ثم الصلاة على النبي له سنة الدعاء (۳) لأنه أرجي للقبول.
The Messenger of Allah prayed over a funeral, so take that. They found he prayed over a woman and made four takbirs, so they agreed on that. And it is narrated from al-Ali that he made four takbirs also. And because each takbir stands in place of a rak'ah, then the customary prayer does not exceed four takbirs. Except that Ibn Layla said: The first takbir is for the opening, so there should be four takbirs after it, each standing in place of a rak'ah, as in Zuhr and Asr. The answer: The first takbir, even though it is for the opening, does not exit from being a takbir, i.e., standing in place of a rak'ah. And in the Fatawa al-Hujjah: The illiterate and the Hindus who do not know the supplications, they make four takbirs and say the salam, their prayer is valid, because the pillars are the takbirs. End quote. And al-Kamal said after this: He said in al-Kafi: Except that Abu Yusuf says: In the first takbir there are two meanings: the meaning of opening and standing in place of a rak'ah, and the meaning of opening is preponderant in it, so it is specified with raising the hands. End quote. And the author of al-Bahr said: In it, i.e., the speech of al-Kamal, there is consideration, because what is explicitly stated is contrary to it. He said in al-Muhit: As for its pillars, they are the takbirs and standing. As for its sunan, they are al-hamd, al-thana, and supplication in it. End quote. And he mentioned other than that. So what is summarized is what we stated in the matn, praise be to Allah. And its conditions are six: First: (Islam of the deceased) due to His statement: {And never pray over any of them who dies} [al-Tawbah 84] meaning the hypocrites, and they are disbelievers. And because it is intercession for the deceased as an honor for him and a request for forgiveness, and the disbeliever does not benefit from intercession nor does he deserve honor. Second: (His purity) because the deceased has the ruling of the imam, and likewise purity of his place. He said in al-Qunyah: Purity from impurity in garment, body, and place, and covering the 'awrah are conditions for both the imam and the deceased. End quote. And in al-Fawa'id al-Tajiyyah: If the deceased is on a bier, there is no doubt that it is allowed even if its place is impure. And without a bier there is no narration about it, and it should be allowed because purity of the place of the deceased is not a condition because he is not performing the prayer. And it is said: Because his shroud is a barrier between him and the ground, because he is not a wearer but worn. End quote, as in Sharh al-Maqdisi. Third: (His being in front) of the people, so it is not valid to pray over him if they place him behind them. And he also has the ruling of the follower, because it is allowed to pray over a woman and a boy, so he is given the ruling of the imam as long as he is not buried, as we will mention. Fourth: (His presence) so prayer over an absent person is not valid. As for the Prophet's prayer over al-Najashi, it was either because his bier was raised until he saw it, so it was a prayer of one behind him over a deceased that the imam saw and was present with him but not the followers, and this does not prevent the validity of following. Or that it was specific to al-Najashi, so others are not analogized to him, as in al-Fath. And in it, Jibril descended at Tabuk and said: O Messenger of Allah, Mu'awiyah ibn al-Muzni died in Medina, do you want me to fold the earth for you so you can pray over him? He said: Yes. So he struck his wings on the earth and raised his bier, and he prayed over him, and behind him were two rows of angels, in each row seventy thousand angels. Then he returned. The Prophet said to Jibril: How did he attain this? He said: By his love for Surah Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad and his recitation of it coming and going, standing and sitting, and in every state. (Or presence of most of his body, or half with his head) as mentioned. Fifth: (The one praying not being a rider) nor sitting (without excuse, because standing in it is a pillar, so it is not left without excuse). Sixth: (The deceased being placed on the ground), because he is like the imam in some respects. (If he is on an animal or on people's hands, the prayer is not valid, according to the chosen opinion, except due to an excuse) as in al-Tabyin. And its sunan are four: First: (The imam standing opposite the chest of the deceased, whether male or female) because the chest is the place of the heart, and in it is the light of faith, so standing near it indicates intercession for his faith. This is the apparent narration, and it indicates recommendation as before. So if he stands elsewhere, it suffices him, as in al-Bahr from Kafi al-Hakim. Second: (Al-thana after the first takbir, saying Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika to the end. And it is permissible to recite al-Fatihah with the intention of thana, as is explicitly stated with us. And in al-Bukhari from Ibn Abbas that he prayed over a funeral and recited al-Fatihah and said: So that you know that it is from the Sunnah. Al-Tirmidhi authenticated it. Third: (The salat upon our master the Prophet after the second takbir), saying Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad... etc. And beginning with thana then salat upon the Prophet is the sunnah of supplication because it is more hopeful for acceptance.
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion probe on the rulings of Salat al-Janazah (funeral prayer). It begins with a discussion on the number of takbirs (four according to Hanafis), refuting the view of Ibn Layla who advocated five (one for iftitah plus four). The Hanafi position is that the first takbir serves both as the opening and as one of the four pillars. A subordinate issue: an illiterate person or someone who does not know the supplications may simply perform four takbirs and say the salam; the prayer is valid because the takbirs themselves are the pillars. The author then lists six conditions (shurut) for the prayer's validity: (1) the deceased must be Muslim, citing Quran 9:84; (2) purity of the deceased and the place, with the deceased having the same ruling as the imam regarding purity and covering the 'awrah; (3) the deceased must be in front of the imam and followers; (4) the deceased must be present (not absent), with the case of the Prophet's prayer over al-Najashi explained either as a virtual presence or a special dispensation; (5) the person praying must not be riding without excuse; (6) the deceased must be placed on the ground. After the conditions, the passage presents four sunnan (recommended acts): (1) the imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased for both men and women; (2) reciting al-thana (Subhanaka) after the first takbir, and reciting al-Fatihah is permissible as thana; (3) reciting salat upon the Prophet after the second takbir; (4) the order of thana then salat. The commentary stays within the Hanafi madhhab, noting the 'zahir al-riwayah' for the standing position and citing the relevant hadith sources.

Key Terms
التكبير (al-takbīr): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' in the janazah prayer; the pillars of the prayer are the takbirs themselves according to the Hanafi school.
السنن (al-sunan): Recommended acts in the janazah prayer; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but leaves it incomplete in perfection.
التحميد (al-tahmīd): Praising Allah, usually with 'Alhamdulillah' or similar; in janazah, it is part of the thana.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum requirement for a valid janazah prayer?
A) Four takbirs and recitation of al-Fatihah.
B) Four takbirs and the salam.
C) Four takbirs, thana, salat, and dua.
D) Four takbirs and standing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: four takbirs are the pillars of janazah prayer; the sunan are the imam standing opposite the chest, thana, salat, and dua, but their omission does not invalidate the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Conditions of the Funeral Prayer: Body, Position, and Placement
Stating conditions regarding the deceased's body, prayer leader's posture, and deceased's location

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the validity of the funeral prayer and identify when an excuse permits deviation.

Core Idea
The deceased must be on the ground and the one praying must stand — both are conditions, not mere recommendations.

In the Hanafi school, the funeral prayer has specific conditions that ensure its validity. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies two of them: the posture of the one praying (must not be riding or sitting without excuse) and the placement of the deceased (must be on the ground). It also notes a third condition about the presence of most of the deceased's body. Understanding these conditions prevents common errors in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify each condition
Read the passage and list the three conditions explicitly stated: (1) presence of most of the deceased's body or half with head, (2) the one praying must not be riding or sitting without excuse, (3) the deceased must be placed on the ground.
The first condition is briefly mentioned; the passage elaborates on the second and third.
2
Note the default ruling and exception for each condition
For condition 2: default is that riding/sitting invalidates; exception: with an excuse (udhr). For condition 3: default is that the deceased must be on the ground; if on an animal or carried, invalid; exception: with a valid excuse.
The term 'al-mukhtar' indicates this is the relied-upon position.
3
Understand the legal basis
Why is standing required? The passage says standing is a rukn (pillar) of the funeral prayer, so it cannot be abandoned without excuse. Why must the deceased be on the ground? Because the deceased is like an imam in one respect, requiring a direct connection to the ground.
This reasoning is from the commentary referencing al-Tabyin.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The phrase 'al-mukhtar' shows that there is a difference of opinion within the school: some narrations allow the prayer if the deceased is off the ground, but the chosen (mufta bihi) view is the stricter one requiring ground placement except with excuse.
This nuance is important for fatwa.
5
Apply to a scenario
Take a scenario: the deceased is on a stretcher held by four people, and the imam leads the prayer while standing. Without a valid excuse, the prayer is invalid because the deceased is not on the ground.
Always check for a valid excuse (e.g., extreme crowding, unsafe ground).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو حضور أكثرِ بَدَنِهِ، أَوْ نصفه مع رأسِهِ. وكَوْنُ المصلي عليها غير راكب بلا عذر. وكون الميت على الأرض، فإن كان على دابَّةٍ، أو على أيدي النَّاسِ، لم تجُزِ الصَّلاةُ ، على المختار، إلا من عذر. كذا في « التبيين». (و) الخامس: (كَوْنُ المُصلِّي عليها غير راكب) وغير قاعد (بلا عذر ، لأن القيام فيها ركن، فلا يترك بـلا عذر. (و) السادس: (كونُ المَيِّتِ موضوعاً (عَلَى الأرض)، لكونه كالإمام من وجه، (فإن كان على دابَّةٍ، أو على أيدي النَّاسِ، لم تجز الصَّلاةُ على المختار، إلا إن كان (من عذر) كذا في « التبيين».
Or the presence of most of his body, or half with his head. And that the one praying over it is not riding without excuse. And that the deceased is placed on the ground, for if it is on a riding animal or on the hands of people, the prayer is not valid according to the chosen position, except if there is an excuse. Thus in al-Tabyin. And the fifth: (that the one praying over it is not riding) and not sitting without excuse, because standing in it is a pillar, so it is not abandoned without excuse. And the sixth: (that the deceased is placed on the ground), because it is like the imam in one respect, for if it is on a riding animal or on the hands of people, the prayer is not valid according to the chosen position, except if there is an excuse. Thus in al-Tabyin.
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah states two conditions for the validity of the funeral prayer. The first condition is that the one performing the prayer must not be riding or sitting without a valid excuse, because standing is a pillar (rukn) in the funeral prayer. The second condition is that the deceased must be placed on the ground; if the body is on an animal or carried by people, the prayer is not valid according to the relied-upon position (al-mukhtar), except when there is an excuse such as necessity. The commentary also references the condition regarding the presence of most of the body or half with the head, which was mentioned earlier. These conditions are recorded in al-Tabyin.

Key Terms
حضور أكثر بدنه (hudur akthar badanihi): Presence of most of his body – a condition that the majority of the deceased's body must be present for the prayer to be valid.
راكب (rakib): Riding – one who is on an animal or vehicle. The one praying must not be riding without excuse.
عذر (udhr): Excuse – a valid reason allowing departure from the normal condition, such as illness or necessity.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen position – the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, as opposed to weaker narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person performs the funeral prayer while riding a horse without any excuse, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid.
B) The prayer is invalid.
C) The prayer is makruh.
D) The prayer is valid only if the imam is riding.

Key Takeaway
For the funeral prayer to be valid in the Hanafi school, the deceased must be on the ground and the one praying must be standing, unless a valid excuse exists.

Salah — Prayer

The Four Sunnahs of the Funeral Prayer and Recommended Supplications
Ruling statement enumerating four sunnahs with evidence from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunnahs of the funeral prayer and identify the transmitted supplications recommended after the third takbir.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer has four sunnah acts; the transmitted du'as are best but not obligatory.

The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is a collective obligation with specific recommended acts. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah enumerates the four sunnahs and provides authentic supplications reported from the Prophet. Understanding these sunnahs ensures completeness, while the transmitted du'as enhance spiritual impact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunnah acts
Read the opening sentence: 'Wa sunanuha arba'' and list the four items: imam standing at chest, thana after first takbir, salat upon Prophet after second, du'a after third.
These are sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended) in the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the first sunnah: imam's position
The text states the imam stands at the level of the deceased (bihida' al-mayyit), meaning the chest, for both male and female. This is the relied-upon position.
Some earlier scholars differed but the fatwa is on this, as stated in Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Examine the second and third sunnahs
After the first takbir, recite thana (e.g., Subhanaka). After the second takbir, send salutations upon the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam).
Reciting al-Fatihah with the intention of thana is also permissible in the Hanafi school.
4
Examine the fourth sunnah: du'a
After the third takbir, make supplication for the deceased, oneself, parents, and all Muslims. No specific wording is obligatory, but using transmitted du'as is best.
The du'a should focus on matters of the afterlife.
5
Review the transmitted du'as
The passage provides three major du'as: the du'a of 'Awf ibn Malik (long du'a), the comprehensive du'a (living and dead), and the du'a of Abu Hurairah from the Muwatta.
These have authentic chains from Muslim, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, and Malik.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسُنَنهَا أربع قيام الإمام بحِدَاءِ المَيِّتِ ذَكَرَاً كان أو أنثى. والثَّناءُ بعد التكبيرة الأولى، والصلاة على سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد الثانية... (و) الرابعة من السنن كما صرح به في ( البرهان وغيره ( الدّعاء للميت) ولنفسه ولأبويه ولجماعة المسلمين ( بعد ) التكبيرة ( الثَّالثة، ولا يَتَعَيَّنُ له) أي: الدعاء (شيء) سـوى كـونـه بـأمور الآخرة، (و) لكن ( إن دعا بالمأثور) عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ( فهو أحسنُ وأَبْلَغُ ) لرجاء قبوله، (ومنه مـا حَفِظَ عَـوْفُ من دعاء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ) كما رواه ( الكمال»، من حديث عوف بن مالك أنه صلى مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم علـى جنازة فحفظ من دعائه: ( اللَّهُمَّ اغْفِرْ لَهُ، وَارْحَمْهُ، وَعَافِهِ، وَاعْفُ عَنْهُ، وَأَكْرِمْ نُزُلَهُ، وَوَسِّعْ مَدْخَلَهُ، وَاغْسِلْهُ بِالمَاءِ وَالثَّلْجِ وَالبَرَدِ وَنَقِّهِ مِنَ الخَطَايَا، كَمَا يُنَقَّى الثَّوْبُ الْأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الدَّنَسِ، وَأَبْدِلْهُ دَارًا خيْراً مِنْ دَارِهِ، وَأَهْلاً خَيْراً مِنْ أَهْلِهِ، وَزَوْجَاً خَيْراً مِنْ زَوْجِهِ، وَأَدْخِلْهُ الجَنَّةَ، وَأَعِذْهُ مِنْ عَذَابِ القَبْرِ، وَعَذَابِ النَّارِ » ) قال عوف حتى تمنيت أن أكون أنا ذلك الميت )، رواه مسلم والترمذي، والنسائي، وفي حديث إبراهيم الأشهلي عن أبيه : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا صلـى عـلـى الجنازة قـال: «اللَّهُمَّ اغْفِرْ لِحَيْنَا وَمَيِّتِنَا، وَشَاهِدِنَا وَغَائِبِنَا، وَصَغِيْرِنَا وَكَبِيْرِنَا، وَذَكَرِنَا وأَنْتَانَا ) رواه الترمذي والنسائي عن أبي هريرة، وزاد فيه: «اللَّهُمَّ مَنْ أحْيَيْتَهُ مِنَّا فَأَحْيِهِ عَلَى الْإِسْلَامِ، وَمَنْ تَوَفَّيْتَهُ مِنَّا فَتَوَفَّهُ عَلَى الإِيمَانِ» (۳) وفي رواية: ( وَمَنْ تَوَفَّيْتَهُ مِنَّا فَتَوَفَّهُ عَلَى الإِسْلامِ اللَّهُمَّ لَا تَحْرِمْنَا أَجْرَهُ، وَلَا تُضِلَّنَا بَعْدَه» (1) وفي موطأ ) الإمام مالك عمن سأل أبا هريرة كيف يصلي على الجنازة؟ فقال أبو هريـــرة: أَنَا لَعَمْرُ اللَّهِ أَخْبِرُكَ أتَّبِعُها مِنْ أَهْلِهَا، فَإِذَا وُضِعَتْ كَبَّرْتُ ، وَحَمِدْتُ اللهَ، وَصَلَّيْتُ عَلَى نَبِيِّهِ، ثُمَّ أقُولُ: اللَّهُمَّ [ إِنَّهُ ] عَبْدُكَ وَابْنُ عَبْدِكَ، وَابْنُ أَمَتِكَ، كَانَ يَشْهَدُ أنْ لا إِلَهَ إِلا أَنْتَ، وَأَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللهِ، وَأَنْتَ أَعْلَمُ بِهِ ، اللَّهُمَّ إِنْ كَانَ مُحْسِنًا فَزِدْ فِي إِحْسَانِهِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مُسِيئًا فَتَجَاوَزْ عَنْ سَيِّئَاتِهِ، اللَّهُمَّ لَا تَحْرِمْنَا أَجْرَهُ، وَلا تَفْتِنَا بَعْدَهُ» (٥)
And its sunnahs are four: the imam standing at the level of the deceased, male or female; and glorification (thana) after the first takbir, and salat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) after the second... and the fourth of the sunnahs as stated in al-Burhan and others: supplication for the deceased, for oneself, for one's parents, and for all Muslims after the third takbir. Nothing specific is prescribed for it, meaning for the supplication, other than being about matters of the afterlife. But if one supplicates with the transmitted supplication from the Prophet (peace be upon him), it is best and most effective due to hope of acceptance. Among them is what 'Awf memorized from the Prophet's supplication, as narrated by al-Kamal from the hadith of 'Awf ibn Malik that he prayed with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) over a funeral and memorized from his supplication: 'O Allah, forgive him, have mercy on him, grant him well-being, pardon him, honor his resting place, widen his entry, wash him with water, snow, and hail, and purify him from sins as a white garment is cleansed of filth, and give him a better home than his home, a better family than his family, a better spouse than his spouse, and admit him to Paradise, and protect him from the torment of the grave and the torment of the Fire.' 'Awf said: 'I wished that I were that deceased.' It was narrated by Muslim, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i. And in the hadith of Ibrahim al-Ash'hali from his father: 'When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed over the funeral, he said: O Allah, forgive our living and our dead, our present and our absent, our young and our old, our males and our females.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i from Abu Hurairah, with addition: 'O Allah, whoever You keep alive among us, keep him alive upon Islam, and whoever You take among us, take him upon faith.' In another narration: '...take him upon Islam. O Allah, do not deprive us of his reward, and do not lead us astray after him.' And in the Muwatta of Imam Malik from someone who asked Abu Hurairah how to pray over the funeral, he said: 'By Allah, I will inform you. I follow it from its people. When it is placed, I say takbir, praise Allah, send salutations upon His Prophet, then I say: O Allah, he is Your servant, son of Your servant, son of Your maidservant. He used to bear witness that there is no god but You and that Muhammad is Your Messenger, and You know best about him. O Allah, if he was righteous, increase his righteousness, and if he was sinful, overlook his sins. O Allah, do not deprive us of his reward, and do not test us after him.'
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage presents the four sunnahs of the funeral prayer as explained in Imdad al-Fattah. The first sunnah is that the imam stands at the chest of the deceased, whether male or female, because the chest contains the heart, the seat of faith, and standing there symbolizes intercession for his faith. This is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah. The second sunnah is to recite the thana (Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika) after the first takbir; reciting al-Fatihah with the intention of thana is also permissible according to our school. The third sunnah is to send salutations upon the Prophet after the second takbir. The fourth sunnah is to make supplication (du'a) for the deceased after the third takbir. No specific wording is obligatory, but it is best to use the supplications reported from the Prophet. The passage then provides several authentic supplications, including the well-known du'a of 'Awf ibn Malik, the comprehensive du'a for all believers, and the du'a narrated by Abu Hurairah in the Muwatta. These du'as cover forgiveness, mercy, purification, and entry into Paradise.

Key Terms
ثناء (thana): Glorification of Allah, specifically reciting 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' after the first takbir.
الدعاء المأثور (al-du'a al-ma'thur): The transmitted supplication – du'as that are reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him) for use in the funeral prayer.
تكبيرة (takbirah): The utterance of 'Allahu Akbar' in the funeral prayer, which is repeated four times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should the imam stand relative to the deceased in the funeral prayer?
A) At the head for males and at the middle for females
B) At the feet
C) At the chest for both males and females
D) Anywhere is fine

Key Takeaway
The four sunnahs of the funeral prayer enhance its completeness; the transmitted du'as are the best supplications.

The Fourth Sunnah of Janazah Prayer: Supplication After the Third Takbir
Ruling that supplication after third takbir is sunnah with transmitted supplications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplication after the third takbir in the janazah prayer and distinguish between sunnah and wajib based on the evidence.

Core Idea
Supplication after the third takbir is sunnah, not wajib, and no specific wording is required, though the transmitted supplications are best.

In the janazah prayer, after the third takbir, the imam and congregation make supplication for the deceased. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that this act is sunnah, not wajib, and that while no particular wording is prescribed, using the supplications transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is superior. We will explore the evidence from multiple hadiths and understand why the Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is supplication after the third takbir of the janazah prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunnah, not wajib.
The text states 'wa huwa min al-sunan' (it is among the sunan).
2
Understand the scope of the supplication
The text explicitly says 'la yata'ayyan lahu shay' – nothing is specified for the supplication except that it concern matters of the afterlife. This means flexibility in wording, but the transmitted supplications (al-ma'thur) are better (ahsan wa ablagh).
The commentator explains that the transmitted form is preferred for hope of acceptance.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The passage provides multiple hadiths showing the Prophet's constant practice (fi'l) of supplicating after the third takbir. The key narration is from 'Awf ibn Malik, who memorized a specific supplication. Other narrations from Ibrahim al-Ash'ali, Abu Hurairah, and Wathilah are also cited.
These are ahad hadiths, giving zanni thubut, and the Hanafi usul holds that fi'l al-nabi indicates sunnah, not wujub.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the evidence proves the ruling)
The Prophet's continuous practice without a command (amr) shows that the act is recommended (sunnah) but not obligatory. The Hanafi principle is that the Prophet's action (fi'l) is a proof for sunnah, not fard or wajib, unless there is an accompanying command.
This distinguishes the Hanafi view from some Shafi'i scholars who consider it wajib based on the same actions.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, after the third takbir, the imam may recite any supplication that asks for forgiveness, mercy, and paradise for the deceased and all Muslims. Using the narrated supplications is better but not required.
The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

And supplication for the deceased after the third (takbir). And nothing is specified for him, and if he supplicates with the transmitted (supplication) then it is better and more effective. Among it is what 'Awf memorized from the supplication of the Prophet: 'O Allah, forgive him, have mercy on him, grant him well-being, pardon him, honor his resting place, expand his entrance, wash him with water, snow, and hail, and purify him from sins as a white garment is cleansed from filth, and give him a better house than his house, a better family than his family, a better spouse than his spouse, admit him to Paradise, and protect him from the punishment of the grave and the punishment of the Fire.' (And) the fourth of the sunan as stated in al-Burhan and others: supplication for the deceased, for oneself, for one's parents, and for all Muslims after the third takbir, and nothing is specified for it (the supplication) except that it be concerning matters of the afterlife. But if one supplicates with the transmitted (supplication) from the Prophet, it is better and more effective due to hope of acceptance. Among it is what 'Awf memorized from the supplication of the Prophet as narrated by al-Kamal from the hadith of 'Awf ibn Malik: he prayed with the Messenger of Allah over a funeral and memorized from his supplication: ... 'Awf said: 'I wished that I were that deceased.' Narrated by Muslim, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i. And in the hadith of Ibrahim al-Ash'ali from his father: The Messenger of Allah, when he prayed over a funeral, said: 'O Allah, forgive our living and our dead, our present and our absent, our young and our old, our males and our females' ... al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i narrated from Abu Hurairah, adding: 'O Allah, whoever You keep alive among us, keep him alive upon Islam, and whoever You take among us, take him upon faith.' And in a narration: '... upon Islam. O Allah, do not deprive us of his reward, and do not lead us astray after him.' And in the Muwatta of Imam Malik: Someone asked Abu Hurairah how to pray over a funeral. Abu Hurairah said: 'By Allah, I will inform you: I follow it from its people. When it is placed, I say the takbir, praise Allah, send blessings upon His Prophet, then say: O Allah, he is Your servant, son of Your servant, son of Your maidservant; he used to bear witness that there is no deity except You and that Muhammad is Your Messenger, and You know best about him. O Allah, if he was righteous, increase his righteousness, and if he was a wrongdoer, overlook his wrongdoings. O Allah, do not deprive us of his reward, and do not put us to trial after him.' And Abu Dawud narrated from Wathilah ibn al-Asqa': The Messenger of Allah prayed with us over a man from the Muslims, and I heard him say: 'O Allah, so-and-so son of so-and-so is under Your protection, entered into Your covenant, so protect him from the trial of the grave and the punishment of the Fire; You are the One of fulfillment and truth. O Allah, forgive him and have mercy on him; indeed You are the Oft-Forgiving, the Most Merciful.' And it was narrated from Abu Hurairah, I heard him (meaning the Prophet) say: 'O Allah, You are its Lord, You created it, You guided it to Islam, You took its soul, and You know its secret and its public; we have come as intercessors, so forgive it.'
Source pages p. 584

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the fourth sunnah of the janazah prayer: supplication after the third takbir. The commentator, following the matn of Nur al-Idah, states that supplication is prescribed after the third takbir, but no specific wording is obligatory ('la yata'ayyan lahu shay'). However, using the supplications transmitted from the Prophet (al-ma'thur) is better and more effective (ahsan wa ablagh) due to the hope of acceptance. The passage then provides multiple hadith narrations as proofs, including the famous supplication of 'Awf ibn Malik, where the Prophet asked for forgiveness, mercy, and purification, and 'Awf wished to be that deceased. Other narrations from Ibrahim al-Ash'ali, Abu Hurairah, and Wathilah are cited, showing the variety of permissible supplications. The commentator emphasizes that the supplication may include the deceased, the living, and all Muslims, and that the wording is flexible as long as it concerns afterlife matters. The authority weight of this ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as the matn represents the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
المأثور (al-ma'thur): Supplications transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him) by authentic narrations.
السنن (al-sunan): The recommended actions of the janazah prayer, including the fourth sunnah of supplication after the third takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Supplication after the third takbir is sunnah, not wajib, and any permissible wording is acceptable, but transmitted supplications are preferred.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings of the Salam and Connected Issues in Janazah Prayer
Rulings on concluding the janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the salam, raising hands, following the imam's extra takbirs, and supplication for a child or insane person in the janazah prayer.

Core Idea
Salam after fourth takbir wajib; raise hands only in first; do not follow extra takbirs; no istighfar for child/insane.

This lesson unpacks several rulings that conclude the janazah prayer: the obligatory salam, the proper hand position, the follower's response to an imam's mistake, and the recommended supplication for a child. These rulings are based on the Zahir al-Riwayah, the core transmitted position of the Hanafi school, with some later refinements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The salam after the fourth takbir. What is its hukm level?
The text says 'wajib' (obligatory).
2
Determine the hukm level and post-salam supplication
The salam is wajib. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, no supplication is made after it. Note a later permissive view.
3
Analyze the ruling on raising hands
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, hands are raised only in the first takbir. Some Balkh shaykhs allowed raising in every takbir.
The Hanafi proof: the Prophet raised hands only in the first takbir.
4
Evaluate the scenario of the imam's extra takbir
If the imam says five takbirs, followers should not follow the fifth but wait for his salam. If the imam mistakenly says salam after the third, he performs the fourth and then salam.
This is based on the chosen view (al-mukhtar).
5
Apply the ruling on supplication
One does not seek forgiveness for a child or insane person because they have no sin. Instead, the recommended supplication for a child is: 'Allahumma aj'alhu lana faratan...'.
The word 'farat' means forerunner, one who precedes to the Pond.

Source Text

(ويُسَلِّمُ) وجوباً (بعد ) التكبيرة (الرَّابعة من غير دعاء) بعدها (في ظاهر الرواية)، واستحسن بعض المشايخ أن يقال: رَبَّنَا آتِنَا فِي الدُّنْيَا حَسَنَة، وفي الآخِرَةِ حَسَنَةً، وقنا عذاب النار، أو رَبَّنَا لا تُزِغْ قُلُوبَنَا بَعْدَ إِذْ هَدَيْتَنَا وَهَبْ لَنَا مِنْ لَدُنْكَ رَحْمَةً إِنَّكَ أَنْتَ الْوَهَّابُ وينوي بالتسليمتين الميت مع القوم كما ينوي الإمام، ولا ينبغي للرجل أن يرفع صوته بالتسليم فيها كما يرفع في سائر الصلوات، ويخافت في الدعاء، ويجهر بالتكبير. And he makes the salam after the fourth (takbir), without supplication in the apparent narration, and he does not raise his hands except in the first takbir. And if the imam says five takbirs, he is not followed, but he waits for his salam, in the chosen view. And one does not seek forgiveness for the insane and a child. And he says: O Allah, make him a forerunner for us, and make him a reward and a treasure for us. (And he makes the salam) obligatorily (after the fourth takbir without supplication) after it (in the apparent narration). Some shaykhs considered it good to say: Our Lord, give us in the world good and in the Hereafter good, and protect us from the punishment of the Fire, or: Our Lord, do not cause our hearts to deviate after You have guided us, and grant us from Yourself mercy; indeed You are the Bestower. And he intends with the two salams the deceased along with the congregation, just as the imam intends. And it is not proper for a man to raise his voice in the salam as he raises it in other prayers; he should lower his voice during supplication and raise it during takbir. (And he does not raise his hands except in the first takbir) in the apparent narration. Many shaykhs from Balkh chose raising in every takbir, as Ibn 'Umar used to do. And our proof: He (the Prophet) used to raise his hands in the first takbir when praying over a funeral, then not return. (And if the imam says five takbirs, he is not followed) because it is abrogated as we explained. (But he waits for his salam in the chosen view) so that he may make salam with him in the most correct view. In one narration, the follower makes salam just as his imam said the extra takbir. And if the imam makes salam after the third inadvertently, he says the fourth takbir and makes salam. (And one does not seek forgiveness for the insane and a child) because they have no sin. (And he says) in the supplication: (O Allah, make him a forerunner for us). Al-farat (with two fathas) is one who precedes from his child, i.e., an advance reward. And al-farat and al-farit is one who precedes the arrival to water. In the hadith: 'I am your forerunner at the Pond,' meaning I precede you to it. And this is the most appropriate interpretation of farat, to avoid repetition with his saying after it: (and make him a reward). Reward (thawab) is what is obtained by the fundamentals of the Shari'ah, and what is obtained by complements is called ajr. Because thawab linguistically is payment of substance, and ajr is payment of benefit; the benefit is subsidiary to the substance. Sometimes ajr is used and reward is intended, and with the heart. (And a treasure) with damm on the dhal and sukun on the kha.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage presents multiple rulings concerning the conclusion of the janazah prayer and related issues. First, the salam after the fourth takbir is wajib (obligatory), and according to the Zahir al-Riwayah, no supplication is made after it. However, some later shaykhs (mutakhkhirin) recommended saying certain Qur'anic supplications. Second, the imam and followers should intend the deceased and the congregation with the two salams. The voice should be lowered for the salam and supplication but raised for the takbir. Third, regarding raising hands: in the Zahir al-Riwayah, it is only done at the first takbir, though many Balkh shaykhs preferred raising at every takbir citing Ibn 'Umar's practice; the Hanafi proof is that the Prophet raised hands only in the first takbir. Fourth, if the imam mistakenly says five takbirs, followers should not follow him but wait for his salam; if the imam errs by saying salam after the third, he must say the fourth and then salam. Fifth, one does not seek forgiveness for an insane person or a child because they are not sinful. Finally, the recommended supplication for a child is: 'Allahumma aj'alhu lana faratan...' with an explanation of the word 'farat' meaning a forerunner (one who precedes to the Pond), and 'ajr' (reward) and 'dhukhran' (treasure). The commentary clarifies the distinctions between thawab and ajr. The authority weight is primarily from the Zahir al-Riwayah (apparent narration) with some flexibility for later practice.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from the early Hanafi authorities (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) as recorded in the six major works (Zahir al-Riwayah).
فَرَط (farat): A forerunner, one who precedes to the water (the Pond of Kawthar), used here for a deceased child who precedes the parents to Paradise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, when should the worshipper raise his hands in the janazah prayer?
A) In every takbir.
B) Only in the first takbir.
C) Only in the last takbir.
D) He should not raise his hands at all.

Key Takeaway
The salam after the fourth takbir is wajib; hands are raised only in the first takbir; do not follow the imam's erroneous extra takbirs; and do not seek forgiveness for a child or insane person, but instead make the specific supplication for a child.

Salah — Prayer

Funeral Prayer: Salam, Raising Hands, and Supplication
Commentary on funeral prayer rulings and supplications from Nur al-Idah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for the funeral prayer concerning salam, raising hands, and supplication, and apply the rulings to cases involving a fifth takbir and prayer for a child or insane person.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer salam is wajib after the fourth takbir; no supplication after it, and hands raised only at the first takbir — these are the relied-upon positions.

In this lesson, we examine several key rulings of the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) as presented in the commentary on Nur al-Idah. The passage clarifies the proper procedure for giving salam, raising hands, and making supplication. It also addresses special cases like an imam adding a fifth takbir and the prayer for a child or insane person. Understanding these rulings ensures correctness in a frequently performed prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon (e.g., giving salam, raising hands) and the specific hukm (obligatory, recommended, etc.) as stated in the text.
Salam after fourth takbir is wajib; raising hands in first takbir is sunnah (by implication, since it is not prohibited).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof (hadith) cited for each ruling. For raising hands, the hadith of Ibn Umar; for supplication, the hadith of Abu Hurairah.
The text references the hadith of Ibn Umar raising hands only in the first takbir.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling. For raising hands, the hadith shows that Ibn Umar, a Companion, restricted raising to the first takbir, which becomes the practice.
The Hanafi school uses this as evidence for the first-only view.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify any difference of opinion. Many scholars of Balkh chose raising hands in every takbir, following Ibn Umar's other practice.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the text acknowledges it but upholds the zahir al-riwaya.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Determine which view is mufta bihi (relied upon) and why. The zahir al-riwaya is preferred; the other view is weaker.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah and the later tradition adopt the first-only view.

(ولا يرفع يديهِ في غير التكبيرة الأولى) في ظـاهـر الـروايـة»، وكثير من مشايخ بلخ اختاروا الرفع في كل تكبيرة، كما كان يفعله ابن عمرة ، ولنا أنه كان إذا صلى على جنازة رفع يديه في التكبيرة الأولى، ثم لا يعود ) ، ( ولو كبرَ الإمامُ خَمساً لم يُتْبَعْ) لأنه منسوخ كما بيناه ) ( ولكن ينتَظَرُ سلامه في المختار ليسلم معه في الأصح، وفي رواية يسلم المأموم، كما كبر إمامه الزائدة، ولو سلم الإمام بعد الثالثة ناسياً كبر الرابعة ويسلم، ولا يُسْتَغْفَرُ لمجنون وصبي) إذ لا ذنب لهما، ويقولُ) في الدعاء: (اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْهُ لنا فَرَطَـا) الفَرَط - بفتحتين- الذي يتقدم الإنسان من ولده أي أجراً متقدماً، والفرط والفارط هو الذي يسبق الوارد إلى الماء، وفي الحديث، « أنَا فَرْطُكُمْ عَلَى الحَوْضِ ) أي : أتقدمكم إليه وهذا هو الأنسب لتفسير الفرط، لئلا يلزم التكرار بقوله بعده: (وَاجْعَلْهُ لَنَا أَجْرَاً الثواب هو الحاصل بـأصول الشرع، والحاصل بالمكملات يسمى أجراً، لأن الثواب لغة بذل العين والأجر : بذل المنفعة فالمنفعة تابعة للعين، وقد يطلق الأجر ويراد به الثواب، وبالقلب، (وَذُخراً) بضم الذال المعجمة، وسكون الخـاء المعجمة: الذخيرة، (وَاجْعَلْهُ لَنَا شَافِعَاً مُشَفَعَاً) - بفتح الفاء - مقبول الشفاعة، قال صاحب البحر » : ولم أر من صرح بأنه يدعو لسيد العبد الصغير ) ، وينبغي الدعاء لـه ). انتهى. وفي التاتارخانية » : روي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أن من صلى على صبي، وفي «الولوالجية» أو مجنون، وفي ( المحيط ) يقول: «اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْهُ لَنَا فَرَطَاً، اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْهُ لَنَا ذُخْرَا اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْهُ لَنَا شَافِعَةٌ مُشَفَّعَاً، ولا يَسْتَغْفِرُ لَهُ» انتهى. والله أعلم.
He gives salam after the fourth (takbir), without supplication in the apparent narration, and he does not raise his hands except in the first takbir. If the imam says a fifth takbir, he is not followed, but he waits for his salam in the chosen view. And no forgiveness is sought for an insane person or a child. And he says: O Allah, make him for us a forerunner, and make him for us a reward and a treasure. (1) The trial of the grave and the punishment of the Fire, and You are the Lord of faithfulness and truth. O Allah, forgive him and have mercy on him, indeed You are the Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful. And it is narrated from the hadith of Abu Hurairah: I heard him meaning the Prophet (peace be upon him) saying: O Allah, You are his Lord, and You created him, and You guided him to Islam, and You took his soul, and You know best his secret and public. We have come as intercessors, so forgive him. And he gives salam obligatorily after the fourth takbir without supplication after it in the apparent narration. Some scholars considered it good to say: Our Lord, give us in this world good and in the Hereafter good, and protect us from the punishment of the Fire, or Our Lord, do not let our hearts deviate after You have guided us and grant us from Yourself mercy, indeed You are the Bestower. And he intends with the two salams the deceased along with the people just as the imam intends. And a man should not raise his voice with salam in it as he raises it in other prayers, and he lowers his voice in supplication and raises it in takbir. And he does not raise his hands except in the first takbir in the apparent narration. Many scholars of Balkh chose raising in every takbir as Ibn Umar used to do. And for us it is that he used to raise his hands in the first takbir and then not repeat. And if the imam says a fifth takbir, he is not followed because it is abrogated as we explained, but he awaits his salam in the chosen view to say salam with him in the most correct view. In one narration, the follower says salam as his imam said the extra takbir. If the imam says salam after the third forgetfully, he says the fourth takbir and says salam. And no forgiveness is sought for an insane person or a child because they have no sin. And he says in the supplication: O Allah, make him for us a forerunner. Al-faratu (with two fatah) is one who precedes a person from his children, i.e., a preceding reward. Al-farat and al-farit is one who precedes the one arriving at water. In the hadith: I am your forerunner at the Hawd, i.e., I precede you to it. And this is the most suitable interpretation of 'farat' to avoid redundancy with his saying afterwards: And make him for us a reward. Thawab is what is obtained by the principles of Shariah, and what is obtained by complements is called ajr, because thawab linguistically is payment of an item, and ajr is payment of a benefit. So the benefit is subordinate to the item. Sometimes ajr is used meaning thawab and by heart. And (a treasure) with damm of the dhal and sukun of the kha' means the treasure. And make him for us an intercessor whose intercession is accepted (with fat-h on the fa) meaning accepted intercession. The author of al-Bahr said: I have not seen anyone explicitly stating that he supplicates for the master of a young slave, and it is recommended to supplicate for him. End quote. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: It is narrated from Abu Hanifah (may Allah have mercy on him) that whoever prays over a child, and in al-Walwaljiyyah: or an insane person, and in al-Muhit says: O Allah, make him for us a forerunner, O Allah, make him for us a treasure, O Allah, make him for us an intercessor whose intercession is accepted, and do not seek forgiveness for him. End quote. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on several rulings of the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The matn states: the imam gives salam after the fourth takbir without supplication after it according to the zahir al-riwaya (the most authoritative transmission within the Hanafi school). The commentary explains that salam is wajib (obligatory) after the fourth takbir, and no supplication is made after it in the preferred view, though some scholars considered it good to recite certain Quranic supplications. The imam should not raise his voice with salam as in other prayers, and he lowers his voice in supplication but raises it in takbir. Regarding raising hands, the matn says he does not raise them except in the first takbir. The commentary notes this is the zahir al-riwaya, but many scholars of Balkh chose raising in every takbir following Ibn Umar. The Hanafi proof is a hadith that Ibn Umar raised hands only in the first takbir. If the imam adds a fifth takbir, the follower should not follow, but wait for his salam and then join in salam in the most correct view. No istighfar (seeking forgiveness) is said for a deceased child or insane person because they have no sin. Instead, the recommended supplication is: 'Allahummaj'alhu lana faratan...' The passage explains 'farat' as a forerunner, and 'ajr' as reward, and 'dhukhran' as treasure, and 'shafi' musaffa'an' as an intercessor whose intercession is accepted. It also notes that for a minor slave, one should supplicate for his master, not his parents (who are likely non-Muslim). This is based on a narration from Abu Hanifah.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The most authoritative and widely transmitted position within the Hanafi school, derived from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
فرط (farat): One who precedes; a forerunner (said of a child who dies before parents, acting as a stored reward).
شافع مشفع (shafi' musaffa'): An intercessor whose intercession is accepted (i.e., the deceased intercedes for the living on Judgment Day).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer salam is wajib after the fourth takbir, with no supplication after, and hands raised only at the first takbir — these are the mufta bihi positions per zahir al-riwaya.

Supplication for a Deceased Child or Insane Person
Ruling on the special supplication for child/insane deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi supplication for a deceased child or insane person and explain why forgiveness is not sought.

Core Idea
For a deceased child, do not ask forgiveness; ask Allah to make them a forerunner and treasure.

When praying over a deceased child or insane person, the Hanafi school prescribes a specific supplication that differs from that for an adult. Instead of seeking forgiveness, we ask Allah to make the deceased a forerunner and treasure for the living. This lesson unpacks the transmitted wording and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Recognize that the passage gives the ruling for the du'a in Janazah prayer over a child or insane person. The act is the supplication itself.
The hukm is sunnah—recommended, not obligatory.
2
Extract the exact wording
From the text, note the three phrases: 'Allahumma ij'alhu lana faratan, Allahumma ij'alhu lana dhukhran, Allahumma ij'alhu lana shafi'an mushaffa'an'.
The commentator clarifies the meaning of each term.
3
Understand what is omitted
The passage explicitly states 'wa la yastaghfir lahu'—and he does not ask forgiveness for him. This is the key difference from the adult Janazah supplication.
The reason: the child has no sins, so asking forgiveness is inappropriate.
4
Note the exception for a slave child
The footnotes mention that for a young slave, one supplicates for the master instead of the parents, because the parents are usually non-Muslims.
This shows the school's attention to social circumstances.
5
Locate the authority
The ruling is traced back to Abu Hanifa via quotations from al-Tatarkhaniyyah, al-Walwalijiyyah, and al-Muhit.
This is fatawa mutakhkhirin, not Zahir al-Riwayah, but the commentator endorses it.

Source Text

(1)
المعجمة: الذخيرة، (وَاجْعَلْهُ لَنَا شَافِعَاً مُشَفَعَاً) - بفتح الفاء - مقبول الشفاعة، قال صاحب البحر » : ولم أر من صرح بأنه يدعو لسيد العبد الصغير ) ، وينبغي الدعاء لـه ). انتهى. وفي التاتارخانية » : روي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أن من صلى على صبي، وفي «الولوالجية» أو مجنون، وفي ( المحيط ) يقول: «اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْهُ لَنَا فَرَطَاً، اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْهُ لَنَا ذُحْرَا اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْهُ لَنَا شَافِعَةٌ مُشَفَّعَاً،

(۱) المراد بالعبد في كلامه هنا الصبي. ا.هـ منحة الخالق على البحر الرائق (۱۹۹/۲). (۲) لأن الحر الصغير يدعو لأبويه وأما العبد الصغير فالغالب كون أبويه كافرين فينبغي أن يدعو لـسـيـده بـدل

And make him an intercessor for us whose intercession is accepted. (1) Al-Mu'jamah: al-Dhakhirah, 'and make him for us an accepted intercessor' - with fat-h on the fa - meaning his intercession is accepted. The author of al-Bahr said: I have not seen anyone explicitly stating that he supplicates for the master of a young slave, and it is recommended to supplicate for him. End. And in al-Tatarkhaniyyah: it is narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) that whoever prays over a child, and in al-Walwalijiyyah: or an insane person, and in al-Muhit, he says: 'O Allah, make him for us a forerunner, O Allah, make him for us a treasure, O Allah, make him for us an accepted intercessor,' and he does not ask forgiveness for him. End. And Allah knows best. (1) What is meant by 'abd (slave) in his speech here is the child. End. (2) Because the free minor supplicates for his parents, but for the young slave, his parents are usually disbelievers, so he should supplicate for his master instead of his parents. End. (3) Ibn Hajar mentioned it in Talkhis al-Habir.
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (Imdad al-Fattah) explains the specific supplication to be said over a deceased child or insane person in the Janazah prayer. It first clarifies the phrase 'make him an accepted intercessor' from the supplication. Then it reports from earlier Hanafi works (al-Bahr, al-Tatarkhaniyyah, al-Walwalijiyyah, al-Muhit) that the correct practice, narrated from Abu Hanifa, is to say 'O Allah, make him a forerunner, a treasure, and an accepted intercessor' and not to ask forgiveness for the deceased. The reason is that a child or insane person is not sinful, so asking forgiveness is inappropriate; instead, we ask Allah to make them a source of benefit for the living. The footnotes add that for a free child, one prays for the parents, but for a young slave, one prays for the master because the parents are usually non-Muslims.

Key Terms
فرط (farat): A forerunner, one who goes ahead to prepare the way
ذخر (dhukhr): Treasure, something stored up for future benefit
شفيع مشفع (shafi' mushaffa'): Accepted intercessor, one whose intercession is granted

D) Say the same as for an adult

Key Takeaway
For a deceased child or insane person, the Hanafi school prescribes a supplication that avoids asking forgiveness, focusing instead on making the deceased a forerunner, treasure, and accepted intercessor for the living.

Order of Precedence for Leading the Funeral Prayer (Ruler vs. Guardian)
Legal ruling on precedence for Janazah prayer with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of precedence for leading the Janazah prayer, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and apply the ruling to a scenario involving the ruler and the guardian.

Core Idea
The ruler takes precedence over the guardian for Janazah prayer to preserve public order — a Hanafi exception to the default right of relatives.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains who is most entitled to lead the Janazah prayer when multiple parties are present. While the guardian (wali) is the default right-holder, the ruler (sultan) or his deputy is given precedence to avoid contempt of authority and public corruption. This ruling reveals an important intra-Hanafi disagreement between the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad, who prioritizes the relative based on a Quranic verse. Understanding this hierarchy helps you apply the correct ruling in communal funeral settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary order of precedence
The matn states: ruler, then his deputy, then qadi, then imam of locality, then guardian. List these in order and note that each step applies only if the previous is absent.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf give the ruler precedence over the guardian. Muhammad says the guardian is always first. Cite the evidence each side uses: public interest vs. Quran 33:6.
The disagreement is between Imams within the same madhhab.
3
Understand the basis for the majority view
The majority relies on the story of al-Husayn presenting the governor Sa'id ibn al-'As, and the principle that preventing corruption (fasad) of public order obligates giving precedence to the ruler.
This is a form of istihsan based on public interest.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Suppose a sultan and the deceased's father are present. According to Abu Hanifa, the sultan leads. According to Muhammad, the father leads. The mufta bihi is the sultan. State the thamarah al-khilaf.
The practical consequence is who actually leads the prayer.
5
Distinguish between obligatory and recommended precedence
Giving precedence to the ruler is obligatory (wajib) to avoid corruption. Giving precedence to the imam of locality over the guardian is only recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory.
This distinction affects whether the act is sinful if omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان الأحق بالصلاة على الجنازة ومتعلقاتها السلطانُ أَحقُّ بصلاتِهِ، ثُمَّ نائبه، ثمَّ القاضي، ثمَّ إمام الحي، ثمَّ الوَلِيُّ .
السلطان أحقُّ بصلاته)، نص عليه أبو حنيفة رحمه الله بقوله: الخليفة أولى إن حضر ، فإن لم يحضر فإمام المصر وهو سلطانها، لأنه في معنى الخليفة، وتعظيمه واجب فلا يتقدم عليه أحد، فلذا
قال: (ثم نائبُهُ) عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، لأن الحسن بن علي لما مات خرج الحسين والناس لصلاة الجنازة، فقدم الحسين سعيد بن العاص، وكان سعيد يومئذ والياً بالمدينة أي: متولياً، فأبى أن يتقدم، فقال له الحسين تقدم ولولا السنة ما قدمتك). وقال محمد -وهو رواية عن الإمام: ولي الميت أولى على كل حال، قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَأُولُوا الْأَرْحَامِ بَعْضُهُمْ أَوْلَى بِبَعْضٍ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٦] قلنا : الآية محمولة على الوارث وولاية الإنكاح (ثم القاضي) لأنه صاحب ولاية وبعده صاحب الشرطة، ثم خليفة الوالي، ثم خليفة القاضي، قاله الزيلعي ( ثم) إن لم يحضر هؤلاء يستحب تقديم ( إمام الحي) لأنه رضيه في حال حياته، كذا في ( الهداية ) ، وفي ( التاتارخانية» لا يتقدم إمام الحي إلا بإذن الأب انتهى، وإنما يستحب تقديمه على الولي، إذا كان أفضل من الولي ، كذا في ( البحر » عن «شرح المجمع لمصنفه. وفي « التاتارخانية » عن « الخلاصة ) : إمام الحي أولى من الولي في الصحيح من الرواية، وفي ( التبيين» عن « جوامع الفقه» : إمام المسجد الجامع أولى من إمام الحي انتهى، والصلاة في الأصل حق الأولياء لقربهم إلا أن الإمام والسلطان يقدمان لعارض الإمامة العظمى والسلطنة، فإن التقدم عليهما فيه ازدراء وفساد أمر المسلمين، فيتحاشا عن ذلك الفساد، فيجب تقديم من له حكـم عام، وأما إمام الحي فيستحب تقديمه على طريق الأفضل، وليس بواجب، كذا في « المستصفى»، ثمَّ الوَلِيُّ) الذكر المكلف إذ لا حق للنساء كالصغار، والمعتوه، كذا في « التاتارخانية»، ويقدم الأقرب فالأقرب من ذوي قرابته، كترتيبهم في التعصيب والإنكاح، ولكن يقدم الأب على الابن في قول الكل على الصحيح لفضله، وفي النكاح يقدم الابن لقربه، قال العلامة « المقدسي » : ولتقديم الأب وجه حسن، وهو أن المقصود الدعاء للميت، ودعوته مستجابة روى أبو هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: ثَلاثُ دَعَوَاتٍ مُسْتَجَابَاتٍ: دَعْوَةُ المَظْلُومِ، وَدَعْوَةُ المَسَافِرِ، وَدَعْوَةُ الوَالِدِ» () رواه الطيالسي انتهى.
Section on explaining who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer and its related matters. The ruler is most entitled to lead it, then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the locality, then the guardian. Abu Hanifa stated: the caliph is first if present; if not, then the ruler of the city, who is its sultan, because he is in the meaning of the caliph, and respecting him is obligatory, so no one should precede him. Hence he said: then his deputy – according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because when al-Hasan ibn Ali died, al-Husayn came out with the people for the funeral prayer, and al-Husayn put forward Sa'id ibn al-'As, who was then the governor of Medina, i.e., in charge, but he refused to go forward, so al-Husayn said to him: 'Go forward; were it not for the sunna, I would not have put you forward.' And Muhammad said – and this is a narration from the Imam: the guardian of the deceased is first in every case. Allah Almighty said: 'But those of kinship are more entitled to one another' [Ahzab: 6]. We say: the verse is interpreted regarding inheritance and the guardianship of marriage. Then the qadi, because he is the one with authority, and after him the chief of police, then the deputy of the governor, then the deputy of the qadi – as stated by al-Zayla'i. Then, if these are not present, it is recommended to present the imam of the locality, because he (the deceased) was pleased with him in his life. Similarly in al-Hidayah. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: the imam of the locality does not go forward except with the permission of the father. End. It is recommended to present him over the guardian only if he is better than the guardian. Similarly in al-Bahr from Sharh al-Majma' by its author. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Khulasa: the imam of the locality is more entitled than the guardian in the sound narration. In al-Tabyin from Jami' al-Fiqh: the imam of the congregational mosque is more entitled than the imam of the locality. End. The prayer in origin is the right of the guardians due to their closeness, except that the imam and the ruler are given precedence due to the consideration of the greater imamate and sultanate, because preceding them involves contempt and corruption of the Muslims' affairs, so one avoids that corruption, so it is obligatory to present one who has general authority. As for the imam of the locality, it is recommended to present him as a matter of preference, not obligatory. Similarly in al-Mustasfa. Then the guardian: the male who is legally responsible, because there is no right for women, like minors and the insane. Similarly in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. The closest in relation is given precedence, like their order in 'asaba and marriage guardianship, but the father is given precedence over the son in the opinion of everyone in the correct view due to his virtue. In marriage, the son is given precedence due to closeness. Al-Maqdisi said: There is a good justification for giving precedence to the father: the purpose is supplication for the deceased, and his supplication is answered. Abu Hurairah narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Three supplications are answered: the supplication of the oppressed, the supplication of the traveler, and the supplication of a parent.' Narrated by al-Tayalisi. End.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage is a section from Imdad al-Fattah explaining the order of precedence for who is most entitled to lead the Janazah prayer. The matn (Nur al-Idah) states the order: ruler (sultan), his deputy, qadi, imam of the locality, then wali (guardian). The commentary expands on each. The key intra-Hanafi dispute is between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: the majority hold that the ruler takes precedence over the wali to avoid corruption of public order, citing the incident of al-Husayn putting forward the governor. Muhammad holds that the wali is always first, based on the Quranic verse 33:6 which he interprets generally as giving relatives priority. The commentator refutes this by restricting the verse to inheritance and marriage. Further details include: the qadi comes after the deputy; after them, the imam of the locality is recommended (not obligatory) if more virtuous than the wali; there is also an opinion from al-Khulasa that the imam of the locality is more entitled than the wali. Among guardians, the father is preferred over the son for leading the prayer due to virtue and answered supplication, unlike in marriage where the son is preferred.

Key Terms
سلطان (sultan): The ruler or sultan of the land, who has general authority
ولي (wali): The guardian of the deceased, typically a male relative
إمام الحي (imam al-hayy): The imam of the local neighborhood mosque

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is most entitled to lead the Janazah prayer if the ruler (sultan) is present?
A) The wali (guardian)
B) The ruler (sultan)
C) The qadi
D) The imam of the locality

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the ruler (or his deputy) takes precedence over the guardian for Janazah prayer to preserve public order, and this ruling is wajib, not merely recommended.

Salah — Prayer

The Primary Hierarchy for Leading the Funeral Prayer
Establishes the primary hierarchy and its rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of those entitled to lead the funeral prayer and explain why the sultan is given precedence over the guardian.

Core Idea
Giving precedence to the ruler avoids fitna – public order overrides the guardian's original right.

This passage establishes the order of priority for who should lead the funeral prayer. It begins with the sultan (ruler) and proceeds through his deputy, the qadi, the imam of the neighborhood, and finally the guardian. The ruling balances the original right of the guardian with the need to honor public authority and prevent discord.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy
Read the first sentence: 'The sultan has the most right to his prayer, then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the neighborhood, then the guardian.' This is the primary order.
2
Understand the reasoning for the sultan's precedence
The author explains that the caliph or sultan must be honored; it is wajib to give him precedence to avoid fitna (discord). The guardian's original right is overridden by public interest.
The ruling is based on the principle of 'sadd al-dhari'ah' (blocking the means to harm) and 'maslahah' (public good).
3
Distinguish between wajib and mustahab in the hierarchy
Note that giving precedence to the sultan and his deputy is wajib, while giving precedence to the imam of the neighborhood is mustahab (recommended) and not obligatory. This distinction is made explicitly in the text.
The imam of the neighborhood is only preferred if he is more virtuous than the guardian.
4
Locate the proof from practice
The text cites the practice of al-Husayn, who gave precedence to the governor over his own family, indicating the principle of honoring authority.
This is a form of 'amal al-sahabah' (practice of the Companions).
