فصل في بيان الأحق بالصلاة على الجنازة ومتعلقاتها السلطانُ أَحقُّ بصلاتِهِ، ثُمَّ نائبه، ثمَّ القاضي، ثمَّ إمام الحي، ثمَّ الوَلِيُّ .
فصل في بيان الأحق بالصلاة على الجنازة ومتعلقاتها
السلطان أحقُّ بصلاته)، نص عليه أبو حنيفة رحمه الله بقوله: الخليفة أولى إن حضر ، فإن لم يحضر فإمام المصر وهو سلطانها، لأنه في معنى الخليفة، وتعظيمه واجب فلا يتقدم عليه أحد، فلذا
قال: (ثم نائبُهُ) عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، لأن الحسن بن علي لما مات خرج الحسين والناس لصلاة الجنازة، فقدم الحسين سعيد بن العاص، وكان سعيد يومئذ والياً بالمدينة أي: متولياً، فأبى أن يتقدم، فقال له الحسين تقدم ولولا السنة ما قدمتك). وقال محمد -وهو رواية عن الإمام: ولي الميت أولى على كل حال، قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَأُولُوا الْأَرْحَامِ بَعْضُهُمْ أَوْلَى بِبَعْضٍ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٦] قلنا : الآية محمولة على الوارث وولاية الإنكاح (ثم القاضي) لأنه صاحب ولاية وبعده صاحب الشرطة، ثم خليفة الوالي، ثم خليفة القاضي، قاله الزيلعي ( ثم) إن لم يحضر هؤلاء يستحب تقديم ( إمام الحي) لأنه رضيه في حال حياته، كذا في ( الهداية ) ، وفي ( التاتارخانية» لا يتقدم إمام الحي إلا بإذن الأب انتهى، وإنما يستحب تقديمه على الولي، إذا كان أفضل من الولي ، كذا في ( البحر » عن «شرح المجمع لمصنفه. وفي « التاتارخانية » عن « الخلاصة ) : إمام الحي أولى من الولي في الصحيح من الرواية، وفي ( التبيين» عن « جوامع الفقه» : إمام المسجد الجامع أولى من إمام الحي انتهى، والصلاة في الأصل حق الأولياء لقربهم إلا أن الإمام والسلطان يقدمان لعارض الإمامة العظمى والسلطنة، فإن التقدم عليهما فيه ازدراء وفساد أمر المسلمين، فيتحاشا عن ذلك الفساد، فيجب تقديم من له حكـم عام، وأما إمام الحي فيستحب تقديمه على طريق الأفضل، وليس بواجب، كذا في « المستصفى»، ثمَّ الوَلِيُّ) الذكر المكلف إذ لا حق للنساء كالصغار، والمعتوه، كذا في « التاتارخانية»، ويقدم الأقرب فالأقرب من ذوي قرابته، كترتيبهم في التعصيب والإنكاح، ولكن يقدم الأب على الابن في قول الكل على الصحيح لفضله، وفي النكاح يقدم الابن لقربه، قال العلامة « المقدسي » : ولتقديم الأب وجه حسن، وهو أن المقصود الدعاء للميت، ودعوته مستجابة روى أبو هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: ثَلاثُ دَعَوَاتٍ مُسْتَجَابَاتٍ: دَعْوَةُ المَظْلُومِ، وَدَعْوَةُ المَسَافِرِ، وَدَعْوَةُ الوَالِدِ» ()
ولِمَنْ له حقُّ التَّقَدَّم أنْ يأْذَنَ لغيرِهِ، فإن صلى غيره أعادها، إن شاء. ولا يُعِيدُ معه من صلَّى مع غيرِهِ، وَمَنْ له ولايةُ التَّقَدَّم فيها، أحقُّ مِمَّنْ أوصى له الميتُ بالصَّلاةِ عليه على المفتى به. وإِنْ دُفِنَ بلا صلاةٍ صُلِّيَ على قبره، وإن لم يُغَسَلْ، ما لم يَتَفَسَّخ.
وقال الزيلعي والسيد أولى من قريب عبده على الصحيح والقريب أولى من السيد المعتق، فإن لم يكن ولي فالزوج، ثم الجيران. ( ولِمَنْ له حقُّ التَّقَدَّم أنْ يأْذَنَ لغيره، لأن التقدم حقه فيملك إبطاله، وإذا كان لــه وليان فأذن أحدهما لأجنبي فللآخر منعه، وإن قدم كل منهما رجلاً فالذي قدمه الأكبر أولى، لأنهما رضـيـا بسقوط حقهما، وأكبرهما سناً أولى بالصلاة عليه، فيكون أولى بالتقديم، كذا في « التاتارخانية»، (فإن صلى غيره)، أي: غير من له حق التقدم بلا إذنه ولم يعتد به (أعادها) هو (إنْ شاءَ) لعدم سقوط حقه، وإن تأدى الفرض بها، ولا يُعِيدُ مَعهُ) أي: مع من له حق التقدم (من صلـى مـع غـيـره) لعدم مشروعية التنفل بها، كما لا يصلي أحد عليها بعده، وإن صلى وحده، وصلاة النبي الله علـى مـن دفـن بـعـد الصـلاة عليه ) لحق تقدمه بقوله تعالى: ﴿ النَّبِيُّ أَوْلَى بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْ أَنفُسِهِمْ ﴾ [الأخْزَاب : ٦] وللولي حق الإعــادة، وصلاة الصحابة على النبي الله أفواجا ) كانت من الخواص، وإلا لصلي على قبره الشريف إلـى يــوم القيامة لبقائه كما وضع طرياً، بل حياً يُرزق ويتنعم بسائر الملاذ والعبادات. (ومـن لـه ولاية التقدم فيـهـا أحقُّ) بالصلاة عليها مِمَّنْ أوصى له الميّتُ بالصَّلاةِ عليه) قال في «العيون»: إن الوصية باطلة (على المُفْتَى بِهِ)، قال الصدر الشهيد: وفي نوادر ) ابن رستم الوصية جائزة، ويؤمــر فـلان بالصلاة عـلـيـه، كذا في «البرهان». (وإنْ دُفِنَ) وأهيل عليه التراب بلا صلاة لأمر اقتضـى ذلـك (صلي على قبره، وإن لم يُغسل) لسقوط شرط طهارته، ولحرمة ،نبشه فيصلى عليه بلا غسل للضرورة، وتعاد لـو صـلـى عـليـه قبل الدفن بلا غسل لفساد الأولى بالقدرة على تغسيله قبل الدفن، وقيل: تنقلب الأولى صحيحة عند تحقق العجز، فلا تعاد، ولو لم يهل التراب يخرج فيغسل ويصلى عليه ( ا لم يَتَفَسَّخ)، والمعتبر في ذلك أكبر الرأي على الصحيح، وهو احتراز عما روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يصلى عليه إلى ثلاثة أيام، وجـه الصحيح أنه يختلف باختلاف الزمان والمكان والأشخاص.
تنبيه: قال في « التاتارخانية ) عن ( العتابية ) : إذا كان القوم سبعة قاموا ثلاثة صفوف يتقدم واحد، وثلاثة بعده، واثنان بعدهم وواحد بعدهما، لأن في الحديث: «مَنْ صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ ثَلَاثَةُ صُفُوفِ غُفِرَ لَهُ ) (۳) وفي ( البزازية ) : خير صفوف الرجال فيها آخرها، وفي سائر الصلوات أولها، لأن القيام
Chapter on explaining who has the most right to lead the funeral prayer and its related matters. The sultan has the most right to his prayer, then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the neighborhood, then the guardian (wali). Chapter on explaining who has the most right to lead the funeral prayer and its related matters. The sultan has the most right to his prayer – Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) stated this saying: The caliph is most entitled if he is present; if he is not present, then the imam of the city who is its sultan, because he is similar to the caliph, and it is obligatory to honor him, so no one should precede him. Therefore he said: (then his deputy) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because when al-Hasan ibn Ali died, al-Husayn went out with the people for the funeral prayer, and al-Husayn presented Sa'id ibn al-As, and Sa'id was at that time the governor of Medina, i.e., in charge, but he refused to step forward, so al-Husayn said to him: 'Step forward; were it not for the sunna, I would not have put you forward.' And Muhammad said – and it is a narration from the Imam: The guardian of the deceased is most entitled in all circumstances. Allah the Exalted said: {But those of kinship are more entitled to each other} [Quran 33:6]. We said: The verse is interpreted regarding inheritance and the authority of marriage. (Then the qadi) because he is the possessor of authority, and after him the chief of police, then the deputy of the governor, then the deputy of the qadi – al-Zayla'i said that. (Then) if these are not present, it is recommended to present (the imam of the neighborhood) because the deceased chose him during his lifetime. Thus in al-Hidaya. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: The imam of the neighborhood may not advance except with the permission of the father – end quote. He is recommended over the guardian only if he is better than the guardian – thus in al-Bahr from Sharh al-Majma' by its author. In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Khulasa: The imam of the neighborhood is more entitled than the guardian in the correct narration. In al-Tabyin from Jami' al-Fiqh: The imam of the congregational mosque is more entitled than the imam of the neighborhood – end quote. The prayer is originally the right of the guardians because of their closeness, but the imam and the sultan are given precedence due to the reason of the greater imamate and sovereignty, because preceding them involves disrespect and corruption of the Muslims' affairs, so one avoids that corruption, thus it is obligatory to give precedence to one with general authority. As for the imam of the neighborhood, it is recommended to present him as a matter of preference, not obligatory – thus in al-Mustasfa. (Then the guardian) – the male who is legally responsible, for women have no right, like minors and the insane – thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And the closest is presented, then the next closest from among his relatives, like their order in inheritance by ta'sib (residuary) and marriage. However, the father is presented over the son in the opinion of all, based on what is correct, due to his virtue. In marriage, the son is presented because of his closeness. The scholar al-Maqdisi said: For presenting the father there is a good aspect: the purpose is supplication for the deceased, and his supplication is answered. Abu Hurayra narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Three supplications are answered: the supplication of the oppressed, the supplication of the traveler, and the supplication of a parent.' And for the one who has the right of precedence to permit others, if another leads the prayer, he may repeat it if he wishes. And he does not repeat it with him who prayed with another. And one who has authority to lead in it is more entitled than one whom the deceased appointed by will to lead the prayer over him, according to the fatwa. If the deceased is buried without prayer, prayer is performed over his grave, even if he was not washed, as long as he has not decomposed. Al-Zayla'i said: The master is more entitled than the relative of his slave, according to the correct view; and the relative is more entitled than the manumitting master. If there is no guardian, then the husband, then the neighbors. (And for the one who has the right of precedence to permit others) because precedence is his right, so he can nullify it. If there are two guardians and one of them permits a stranger, the other may prevent him. If each puts forward a man, the one put forward by the older one is more entitled, because they both consented to waive their right, and the older one in age is more entitled to lead the prayer over him, so his chosen one is more entitled to be given precedence – thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. (If another leads the prayer), i.e., other than the one entitled to precedence without his permission and he does not count it, (he may repeat it) if he wishes, because his right has not lapsed, even if the obligation is fulfilled by it. And he does not repeat it with him (i.e., the one entitled to precedence) who prayed with another, because there is no basis for performing a supererogatory funeral prayer, just as no one should lead another funeral prayer after it, even if he prays alone. And the Prophet's prayer over one who was buried after the prayer over him was due to his right of precedence by the saying of the Exalted: {The Prophet is more entitled to the believers than themselves} [Quran 33:6]. And the guardian has the right of repetition. The prayer of the Companions over the Prophet in groups was from the elite; otherwise, prayer would have been performed at his noble grave until the Day of Resurrection due to his staying fresh as if just placed, rather he is alive, provided for, and enjoying all pleasures and acts of worship. (And one who has authority of precedence in it is more entitled) to lead the prayer over him than one whom the deceased appointed by will to lead the prayer over him. In al-Uyun: The will is invalid – according to the fatwa. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: In the Nawadir of Ibn Rustam, the will is valid, and so-and-so is ordered to lead the prayer over him – thus in al-Burhan. (If the deceased is buried) and soil poured over him without prayer due to a necessitating reason, (prayer is performed over his grave, even if he was not washed) because the condition of his purity is waived, and because it is forbidden to exhume him, so prayer is performed without washing out of necessity. And it would be repeated if prayer was performed before burial without washing because the first is invalid due to the ability to wash him before burial. And it is said: The first becomes valid when inability is confirmed, so it is not repeated. If the soil has not been poured, he is taken out, washed, and prayed over. (As long as he has not decomposed). What is considered in that is the majority opinion, on the correct view. This is a caveat to what was narrated from Abu Hanifa that prayer can be performed over him up to three days. The correct view is that it varies according to time, place, and persons. Alert: In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Atabiyya: If the people are seven, they stand in three rows: one goes forward, three behind him, two behind them, and one behind them, because in the hadith: 'Whoever is prayed over by three rows will be forgiven.' In al-Bazzaziyya: The best of rows for men in it is the last, whereas in other prayers it is the first, because standing...
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the hierarchy of those entitled to lead the funeral prayer. The author begins by stating the order: the sultan (ruler), then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the neighborhood, then the guardian (wali). He then provides proofs and explanations for each level. The basis for the sultan's precedence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said the caliph is most entitled, and it is obligatory to honor the ruler and avoid any disrespect that could cause public discord. This is a matter of public order. The deputy (na'ib) comes next according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, citing the practice of al-Husayn who gave precedence to the governor Sa'id ibn al-As. Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, holds that the deceased's guardian is always most entitled, based on the Quranic verse about close relatives being more entitled. The author explains that the verse refers to inheritance and marriage, not funeral prayer. The qadi is next because he has general authority. If none of these are present, the imam of the neighborhood is recommended, not obligatory, and only if he is more virtuous than the guardian. Some scholars hold that the imam of the neighborhood is more entitled than the guardian, while others give priority to the imam of the congregational mosque. The reason for prioritizing public officials over guardians is to avoid fitna (discord). The guardian's right is original, but it is overridden by the ruler due to the greater good. Among guardians, the closest male relative is given precedence, with the father preferred over the son due to the virtue of his supplication. The text then discusses several related rulings: (1) The one with the right of precedence may delegate another to lead; if someone else leads without permission, the one entitled may repeat the prayer at his discretion, but those who prayed with the unauthorized imam do not repeat. (2) A person appointed by the deceased's will to lead the prayer is not given priority over the rightful guardian; the will in this matter is invalid according to the fatwa, though there is a dissenting narration. (3) If a person is buried without prayer, one may pray over the grave, even if he was not washed, as long as the body has not decomposed. This is due to necessity and the prohibition of exhuming. However, if prayer was performed before burial without washing, it is invalid and must be repeated because washing was possible. (4) An additional note on the arrangement of rows: for funeral prayer, the best row is the last, opposite to other prayers. The text includes several intra-Hanafi disputes, such as the position of Muhammad al-Shaybani on the guardian's priority, and the different views on the validity of the deceased's will regarding who should lead. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the will is invalid. The commentary as a whole provides a comprehensive treatment of who is entitled to lead the funeral prayer, integrating proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, practice of the Companions, and the principles of public interest and avoidance of discord.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruler or highest political authority of the land.
الولي (al-wali): The closest male relative of the deceased who is legally responsible.
حق التقدم (haqq al-taqaddum): The right to lead the funeral prayer as the imam.

Key Takeaway
The sultan has wajib priority in leading the funeral prayer to preserve public order, overriding the guardian's original right.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Proofs and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Guardian's Right
Presents the intra-Hanafi dispute and its proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the proof of Muhammad al-Shaybani for the guardian's precedence and the Hanafi majority's refutation, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Muhammad's reliance on Quran 33:6 is refuted by restricting the verse to inheritance and marriage.

This passage presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani argues that the deceased's guardian is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer in all cases, citing a Quranic verse. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) respond by limiting the verse's scope and by invoking the practice of al-Husayn and the principle of avoiding fitna. Understanding this dispute clarifies the hierarchy's foundation.

Guided Path
1
Identify Muhammad's position and his dalil
Muhammad says: 'The guardian of the deceased is most entitled in all circumstances.' He cites Quran 33:6: 'But those of kinship are more entitled to each other.'
The verse literally says 'أولى ببعض' which is used for priority.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response
The majority respond: 'The verse is interpreted regarding inheritance and the authority of marriage, not funeral prayer.' They limit (takhsis) the generality of the verse.
This is a classic usul argument: a general text may be restricted by context or other evidence.
3
Examine the practical proof from al-Husayn
The author cites the incident where al-Husayn presented the governor Sa'id over himself for his brother's funeral, showing that public authority takes precedence even over a close relative.
This is a practice of a Companion, which is a source of law in Hanafi usul, but not as strong as Quran.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the sultan is present, Muhammad's view would allow the guardian to lead, while the majority would require the sultan to lead.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

ولِمَنْ له حقُّ التَّقَدَّم أنْ يأْذَنَ لغيرِهِ، فإن صلى غيره أعادها، إن شاء. ولا يُعِيدُ معه من صلَّى مع غيرِهِ، وَمَنْ له ولايةُ التَّقَدَّم فيها، أحقُّ مِمَّنْ أوصى له الميتُ بالصَّلاةِ عليه على المفتى به. وإِنْ دُفِنَ بلا صلاةٍ صُلِّيَ على قبره، وإن لم يُغَسَلْ، ما لم يَتَفَسَّخ.

Chapter on explaining who has the most right to lead the funeral prayer and its related matters. The sultan has the most right to his prayer, then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the neighborhood, then the guardian (wali). Chapter on explaining who has the most right to lead the funeral prayer and its related matters. The sultan has the most right to his prayer – Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) stated this saying: The caliph is most entitled if he is present; if he is not present, then the imam of the city who is its sultan, because he is similar to the caliph, and it is obligatory to honor him, so no one should precede him. Therefore he said: (then his deputy) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because when al-Hasan ibn Ali died, al-Husayn went out with the people for the funeral prayer, and al-Husayn presented Sa'id ibn al-As, and Sa'id was at that time the governor of Medina, i.e., in charge, but he refused to step forward, so al-Husayn said to him: 'Step forward; were it not for the sunna, I would not have put you forward.' And Muhammad said – and it is a narration from the Imam: The guardian of the deceased is most entitled in all circumstances. Allah the Exalted said: {But those of kinship are more entitled to each other} [Quran 33:6]. We said: The verse is interpreted regarding inheritance and the authority of marriage. (Then the qadi) because he is the possessor of authority, and after him the chief of police, then the deputy of the governor, then the deputy of the qadi – al-Zayla'i said that. (Then) if these are not present, it is recommended to present (the imam of the neighborhood) because the deceased chose him during his lifetime. Thus in al-Hidaya. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: The imam of the neighborhood may not advance except with the permission of the father – end quote. He is recommended over the guardian only if he is better than the guardian – thus in al-Bahr from Sharh al-Majma' by its author. In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Khulasa: The imam of the neighborhood is more entitled than the guardian in the correct narration. In al-Tabyin from Jami' al-Fiqh: The imam of the congregational mosque is more entitled than the imam of the neighborhood – end quote. The prayer is originally the right of the guardians because of their closeness, but the imam and the sultan are given precedence due to the reason of the greater imamate and sovereignty, because preceding them involves disrespect and corruption of the Muslims' affairs, so one avoids that corruption, thus it is obligatory to give precedence to one with general authority. As for the imam of the neighborhood, it is recommended to present him as a matter of preference, not obligatory – thus in al-Mustasfa. (Then the guardian) – the male who is legally responsible, for women have no right, like minors and the insane – thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And the closest is presented, then the next closest from among his relatives, like their order in inheritance by ta'sib (residuary) and marriage. However, the father is presented over the son in the opinion of all, based on what is correct, due to his virtue. In marriage, the son is presented because of his closeness. The scholar al-Maqdisi said: For presenting the father there is a good aspect: the purpose is supplication for the deceased, and his supplication is answered. Abu Hurayra narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Three supplications are answered: the supplication of the oppressed, the supplication of the traveler, and the supplication of a parent.' And for the one who has the right of precedence to permit others, if another leads the prayer, he may repeat it if he wishes. And he does not repeat it with him who prayed with another. And one who has authority to lead in it is more entitled than one whom the deceased appointed by will to lead the prayer over him, according to the fatwa. If the deceased is buried without prayer, prayer is performed over his grave, even if he was not washed, as long as he has not decomposed. Al-Zayla'i said: The master is more entitled than the relative of his slave, according to the correct view; and the relative is more entitled than the manumitting master. If there is no guardian, then the husband, then the neighbors. (And for the one who has the right of precedence to permit others) because precedence is his right, so he can nullify it. If there are two guardians and one of them permits a stranger, the other may prevent him. If each puts forward a man, the one put forward by the older one is more entitled, because they both consented to waive their right, and the older one in age is more entitled to lead the prayer over him, so his chosen one is more entitled to be given precedence – thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. (If another leads the prayer), i.e., other than the one entitled to precedence without his permission and he does not count it, (he may repeat it) if he wishes, because his right has not lapsed, even if the obligation is fulfilled by it. And he does not repeat it with him (i.e., the one entitled to precedence) who prayed with another, because there is no basis for performing a supererogatory funeral prayer, just as no one should lead another funeral prayer after it, even if he prays alone. And the Prophet's prayer over one who was buried after the prayer over him was due to his right of precedence by the saying of the Exalted: {The Prophet is more entitled to the believers than themselves} [Quran 33:6]. And the guardian has the right of repetition. The prayer of the Companions over the Prophet in groups was from the elite; otherwise, prayer would have been performed at his noble grave until the Day of Resurrection due to his staying fresh as if just placed, rather he is alive, provided for, and enjoying all pleasures and acts of worship. (And one who has authority of precedence in it is more entitled) to lead the prayer over him than one whom the deceased appointed by will to lead the prayer over him. In al-Uyun: The will is invalid – according to the fatwa. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: In the Nawadir of Ibn Rustam, the will is valid, and so-and-so is ordered to lead the prayer over him – thus in al-Burhan. (If the deceased is buried) and soil poured over him without prayer due to a necessitating reason, (prayer is performed over his grave, even if he was not washed) because the condition of his purity is waived, and because it is forbidden to exhume him, so prayer is performed without washing out of necessity. And it would be repeated if prayer was performed before burial without washing because the first is invalid due to the ability to wash him before burial. And it is said: The first becomes valid when inability is confirmed, so it is not repeated. If the soil has not been poured, he is taken out, washed, and prayed over. (As long as he has not decomposed). What is considered in that is the majority opinion, on the correct view. This is a caveat to what was narrated from Abu Hanifa that prayer can be performed over him up to three days. The correct view is that it varies according to time, place, and persons. Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the hierarchy of those entitled to lead the funeral prayer. The author begins by stating the order: the sultan (ruler), then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the neighborhood, then the guardian (wali). He then provides proofs and explanations for each level. The basis for the sultan's precedence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said the caliph is most entitled, and it is obligatory to honor the ruler and avoid any disrespect that could cause public discord. This is a matter of public order. The deputy (na'ib) comes next according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, citing the practice of al-Husayn who gave precedence to the governor Sa'id ibn al-As. Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, holds that the deceased's guardian is always most entitled, based on the Quranic verse about close relatives being more entitled. The author explains that the verse refers to inheritance and marriage, not funeral prayer. The qadi is next because he has general authority. If none of these are present, the imam of the neighborhood is recommended, not obligatory, and only if he is more virtuous than the guardian. Some scholars hold that the imam of the neighborhood is more entitled than the guardian, while others give priority to the imam of the congregational mosque. The reason for prioritizing public officials over guardians is to avoid fitna (discord). The guardian's right is original, but it is overridden by the ruler due to the greater good. Among guardians, the closest male relative is given precedence, with the father preferred over the son due to the virtue of his supplication. The text then discusses several related rulings: (1) The one with the right of precedence may delegate another to lead; if someone else leads without permission, the one entitled may repeat the prayer at his discretion, but those who prayed with the unauthorized imam do not repeat. (2) A person appointed by the deceased's will to lead the prayer is not given priority over the rightful guardian; the will in this matter is invalid according to the fatwa, though there is a dissenting narration. (3) If a person is buried without prayer, one may pray over the grave, even if he was not washed, as long as the body has not decomposed. This is due to necessity and the prohibition of exhuming. However, if prayer was performed before burial without washing, it is invalid and must be repeated because washing was possible. (4) An additional note on the arrangement of rows: for funeral prayer, the best row is the last, opposite to other prayers. The text includes several intra-Hanafi disputes, such as the position of Muhammad al-Shaybani on the guardian's priority, and the different views on the validity of the deceased's will regarding who should lead. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the will is invalid. The commentary as a whole provides a comprehensive treatment of who is entitled to lead the funeral prayer, integrating proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, practice of the Companions, and the principles of public interest and avoidance of discord.

Key Terms
الأولى (al-awla): More entitled or worthy.
الوارث (al-warith): Heir who inherits property.
الإنكاح (al-inkah): Authority to give in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Quran 4:11
B) Quran 33:6
C) Quran 2:180
D) Quran 24:61

Key Takeaway
Muhammad's proof from Quran 33:6 is refuted by restricting the verse to inheritance and marriage; the majority's evidence from practice and maslahah prevails.

Salah — Prayer

Delegation, Repetition, and the Invalidity of the Deceased's Will
Rulings on delegation, repetition, and the deceased's will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on delegation of the right to lead, the consequences of leading without permission, and the status of the deceased's will regarding who leads.

Core Idea
The entitled person may delegate, and if another leads without permission, the entitled can repeat; the deceased's will to appoint an imam is invalid.

This passage addresses three practical issues: can the person entitled to lead delegate? What happens if someone else leads without permission? And can a deceased person appoint someone by will to lead his own funeral? The Hanafi rulings here clarify the limits of the right of precedence (haqq al-taqaddum) and the scope of testamentary disposition.

Guided Path
1
Understand delegation
The one with the right of precedence may permit another to lead. This is because it is his right, and he can waive it.
Permission can be explicit or implicit.
2
Analyze the case of leading without permission
If another leads without permission, the entitled person may repeat the funeral prayer (if he wishes) because his right has not lapsed. However, those who prayed with the unauthorized imam do not repeat.
The prayer performed is valid as a fulfillment of the obligation, but the entitled person retains the right to repeat out of respect for his right.
3
Examine the deceased's will
The deceased cannot appoint by will someone to lead his own funeral. The right belongs to the living guardian. The will is invalid according to the fatwa.
There is a dissenting narration (nawadir) that the will is valid, but it is not acted upon.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi conflict on the will
Al-Sadr al-Shahid reports from Nawadir Ibn Rustam that the will is valid and the appointed person should lead. But the fatwa (mufta bihi) is that it is invalid.
The principle: the right of precedence cannot be transferred by the deceased; it is a right of the living guardian.

( ولِمَنْ له حقُّ التَّقَدَّم أنْ يأْذَنَ لغيره، لأن التقدم حقه فيملك إبطاله، وإذا كان لــه وليان فأذن أحدهما لأجنبي فللآخر منعه، وإن قدم كل منهما رجلاً فالذي قدمه الأكبر أولى، لأنهما رضـيـا بسقوط حقهما، وأكبرهما سناً أولى بالصلاة عليه، فيكون أولى بالتقديم، كذا في « التاتارخانية»، (فإن صلى غيره)، أي: غير من له حق التقدم بلا إذنه ولم يعتد به (أعادها) هو (إنْ شاءَ) لعدم سقوط حقه، وإن تأدى الفرض بها، ولا يُعِيدُ مَعهُ) أي: مع من له حق التقدم (من صلـى مـع غـيـره) لعدم مشروعية التنفل بها، كما لا يصلي أحد عليها بعده، وإن صلى وحده، وصلاة النبي الله علـى مـن دفـن بـعـد الصـلاة عليه ) لحق تقدمه بقوله تعالى: ﴿ النَّبِيُّ أَوْلَى بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْ أَنفُسِهِمْ ﴾ [الأخْزَاب : ٦] وللولي حق الإعــادة، وصلاة الصحابة على النبي الله أفواجا ) كانت من الخواص، وإلا لصلي على قبره الشريف إلـى يــوم القيامة لبقائه كما وضع طرياً، بل حياً يُرزق ويتنعم بسائر الملاذ والعبادات. Chapter on explaining who has the most right to lead the funeral prayer and its related matters. The sultan has the most right to his prayer, then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the neighborhood, then the guardian (wali). Chapter on explaining who has the most right to lead the funeral prayer and its related matters. The sultan has the most right to his prayer – Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) stated this saying: The caliph is most entitled if he is present; if he is not present, then the imam of the city who is its sultan, because he is similar to the caliph, and it is obligatory to honor him, so no one should precede him. Therefore he said: (then his deputy) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because when al-Hasan ibn Ali died, al-Husayn went out with the people for the funeral prayer, and al-Husayn presented Sa'id ibn al-As, and Sa'id was at that time the governor of Medina, i.e., in charge, but he refused to step forward, so al-Husayn said to him: 'Step forward; were it not for the sunna, I would not have put you forward.' And Muhammad said – and it is a narration from the Imam: The guardian of the deceased is most entitled in all circumstances. Allah the Exalted said: {But those of kinship are more entitled to each other} [Quran 33:6]. We said: The verse is interpreted regarding inheritance and the authority of marriage. (Then the qadi) because he is the possessor of authority, and after him the chief of police, then the deputy of the governor, then the deputy of the qadi – al-Zayla'i said that. (Then) if these are not present, it is recommended to present (the imam of the neighborhood) because the deceased chose him during his lifetime. Thus in al-Hidaya. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: The imam of the neighborhood may not advance except with the permission of the father – end quote. He is recommended over the guardian only if he is better than the guardian – thus in al-Bahr from Sharh al-Majma' by its author. In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Khulasa: The imam of the neighborhood is more entitled than the guardian in the correct narration. In al-Tabyin from Jami' al-Fiqh: The imam of the congregational mosque is more entitled than the imam of the neighborhood – end quote. The prayer is originally the right of the guardians because of their closeness, but the imam and the sultan are given precedence due to the reason of the greater imamate and sovereignty, because preceding them involves disrespect and corruption of the Muslims' affairs, so one avoids that corruption, thus it is obligatory to give precedence to one with general authority. As for the imam of the neighborhood, it is recommended to present him as a matter of preference, not obligatory – thus in al-Mustasfa. (Then the guardian) – the male who is legally responsible, for women have no right, like minors and the insane – thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And the closest is presented, then the next closest from among his relatives, like their order in inheritance by ta'sib (residuary) and marriage. However, the father is presented over the son in the opinion of all, based on what is correct, due to his virtue. In marriage, the son is presented because of his closeness. The scholar al-Maqdisi said: For presenting the father there is a good aspect: the purpose is supplication for the deceased, and his supplication is answered. Abu Hurayra narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Three supplications are answered: the supplication of the oppressed, the supplication of the traveler, and the supplication of a parent.' And for the one who has the right of precedence to permit others, if another leads the prayer, he may repeat it if he wishes. And he does not repeat it with him who prayed with another. And one who has authority to lead in it is more entitled than one whom the deceased appointed by will to lead the prayer over him, according to the fatwa. If the deceased is buried without prayer, prayer is performed over his grave, even if he was not washed, as long as he has not decomposed. Al-Zayla'i said: The master is more entitled than the relative of his slave, according to the correct view; and the relative is more entitled than the manumitting master. If there is no guardian, then the husband, then the neighbors. (And for the one who has the right of precedence to permit others) because precedence is his right, so he can nullify it. If there are two guardians and one of them permits a stranger, the other may prevent him. If each puts forward a man, the one put forward by the older one is more entitled, because they both consented to waive their right, and the older one in age is more entitled to lead the prayer over him, so his chosen one is more entitled to be given precedence – thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. (If another leads the prayer), i.e., other than the one entitled to precedence without his permission and he does not count it, (he may repeat it) if he wishes, because his right has not lapsed, even if the obligation is fulfilled by it. And he does not repeat it with him (i.e., the one entitled to precedence) who prayed with another, because there is no basis for performing a supererogatory funeral prayer, just as no one should lead another funeral prayer after it, even if he prays alone. And the Prophet's prayer over one who was buried after the prayer over him was due to his right of precedence by the saying of the Exalted: {The Prophet is more entitled to the believers than themselves} [Quran 33:6]. And the guardian has the right of repetition. The prayer of the Companions over the Prophet in groups was from the elite; otherwise, prayer would have been performed at his noble grave until the Day of Resurrection due to his staying fresh as if just placed, rather he is alive, provided for, and enjoying all pleasures and acts of worship. (And one who has authority of precedence in it is more entitled) to lead the prayer over him than one whom the deceased appointed by will to lead the prayer over him. In al-Uyun: The will is invalid – according to the fatwa. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: In the Nawadir of Ibn Rustam, the will is valid, and so-and-so is ordered to lead the prayer over him – thus in al-Burhan. (If the deceased is buried) and soil poured over him without prayer due to a necessitating reason, (prayer is performed over his grave, even if he was not washed) because the condition of his purity is waived, and because it is forbidden to exhume him, so prayer is performed without washing out of necessity. And it would be repeated if prayer was performed before burial without washing because the first is invalid due to the ability to wash him before burial. And it is said: The first becomes valid when inability is confirmed, so it is not repeated. If the soil has not been poured, he is taken out, washed, and prayed over. (As long as he has not decomposed). What is considered in that is the majority opinion, on the correct view. This is a caveat to what was narrated from Abu Hanifa that prayer can be performed over him up to three days. The correct view is that it varies according to time, place, and persons. Alert: In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Atabiyya: If the people are seven, they stand in three rows: one goes forward, three behind him, two behind them, and one behind them, because in the hadith: 'Whoever is prayed over by three rows will be forgiven.' In al-Bazzaziyya: The best of rows for men in it is the last, whereas in other prayers it is the first, because standing...
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the hierarchy of those entitled to lead the funeral prayer. The author begins by stating the order: the sultan (ruler), then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the neighborhood, then the guardian (wali). He then provides proofs and explanations for each level. The basis for the sultan's precedence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said the caliph is most entitled, and it is obligatory to honor the ruler and avoid any disrespect that could cause public discord. This is a matter of public order. The deputy (na'ib) comes next according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, citing the practice of al-Husayn who gave precedence to the governor Sa'id ibn al-As. Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, holds that the deceased's guardian is always most entitled, based on the Quranic verse about close relatives being more entitled. The author explains that the verse refers to inheritance and marriage, not funeral prayer. The qadi is next because he has general authority. If none of these are present, the imam of the neighborhood is recommended, not obligatory, and only if he is more virtuous than the guardian. Some scholars hold that the imam of the neighborhood is more entitled than the guardian, while others give priority to the imam of the congregational mosque. The reason for prioritizing public officials over guardians is to avoid fitna (discord). The guardian's right is original, but it is overridden by the ruler due to the greater good. Among guardians, the closest male relative is given precedence, with the father preferred over the son due to the virtue of his supplication. The text then discusses several related rulings: (1) The one with the right of precedence may delegate another to lead; if someone else leads without permission, the one entitled may repeat the prayer at his discretion, but those who prayed with the unauthorized imam do not repeat. (2) A person appointed by the deceased's will to lead the prayer is not given priority over the rightful guardian; the will in this matter is invalid according to the fatwa, though there is a dissenting narration. (3) If a person is buried without prayer, one may pray over the grave, even if he was not washed, as long as the body has not decomposed. This is due to necessity and the prohibition of exhuming. However, if prayer was performed before burial without washing, it is invalid and must be repeated because washing was possible. (4) An additional note on the arrangement of rows: for funeral prayer, the best row is the last, opposite to other prayers. The text includes several intra-Hanafi disputes, such as the position of Muhammad al-Shaybani on the guardian's priority, and the different views on the validity of the deceased's will regarding who should lead. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the will is invalid. The commentary as a whole provides a comprehensive treatment of who is entitled to lead the funeral prayer, integrating proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, practice of the Companions, and the principles of public interest and avoidance of discord.

Key Terms
الإذن (al-idhn): Permission or authorization.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): Will or testament.
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The position relied upon for giving fatwas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi fatwa regarding a deceased person's will to appoint a specific imam for his funeral?
A) The will is valid and must be followed
B) The will is invalid; the living guardian has the right
C) The will is valid but only if the appointee is a relative
D) The will is valid only if the sultan approves

Key Takeaway
The right to lead the funeral prayer belongs to the living guardian; the deceased cannot override it by will.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Praying Over the Grave Without Washing
Ruling on praying over the grave without washing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the funeral prayer may be performed over a grave and explain the ruling when the body was not washed before burial.

Core Idea
If buried without prayer, the prayer is performed over the grave without washing, as long as the body has not decomposed.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a person is buried without the funeral prayer being performed, perhaps due to an emergency. The Hanafi ruling allows the prayer to be performed over the grave even if the body was not washed, provided the body has not decomposed. This is an expression of the Shari'ah's flexibility in the face of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
The case is when a deceased person has been buried without the funeral prayer, and now the prayer is desired.
This may happen due to urgency or oversight.
2
Apply the ruling on washing
If the body was not washed before burial, the prayer is still performed over the grave without washing, because exhuming for washing is not allowed.
Washing is a condition of the prayer, but it is waived here due to necessity (haraj).
3
Note the time limit
The prayer is valid as long as the body has not decomposed. The correct view is that this varies by time, place, and condition, not a fixed three days.
Abu Hanifa reportedly said up to three days, but the author says the correct view is flexible.
4
Contrast with the case where prayer was done before burial without washing
If the prayer was performed before burial without washing, it is invalid and must be repeated because washing was possible at that time.
The ruling is based on the ability to fulfill the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان الأحق بالصلاة على الجنازة ومتعلقاتها السلطانُ أَحقُّ بصلاتِهِ، ثُمَّ نائبه، ثمَّ القاضي، ثمَّ إمام الحي، ثمَّ الوَلِيُّ .
فصل في بيان الأحق بالصلاة على الجنازة ومتعلقاتها
السلطان أحقُّ بصلاته)، نص عليه أبو حنيفة رحمه الله بقوله: الخليفة أولى إن حضر ، فإن لم يحضر فإمام المصر وهو سلطانها، لأنه في معنى الخليفة، وتعظيمه واجب فلا يتقدم عليه أحد، فلذا
قال: (ثم نائبُهُ) عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، لأن الحسن بن علي لما مات خرج الحسين والناس لصلاة الجنازة، فقدم الحسين سعيد بن العاص، وكان سعيد يومئذ والياً بالمدينة أي: متولياً، فأبى أن يتقدم، فقال له الحسين تقدم ولولا السنة ما قدمتك). وقال محمد -وهو رواية عن الإمام: ولي الميت أولى على كل حال، قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَأُولُوا الْأَرْحَامِ بَعْضُهُمْ أَوْلَى بِبَعْضٍ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٦] قلنا : الآية محمولة على الوارث وولاية الإنكاح (ثم القاضي) لأنه صاحب ولاية وبعده صاحب الشرطة، ثم خليفة الوالي، ثم خليفة القاضي، قاله الزيلعي ( ثم) إن لم يحضر هؤلاء يستحب تقديم ( إمام الحي) لأنه رضيه في حال حياته، كذا في ( الهداية ) ، وفي ( التاتارخانية» لا يتقدم إمام الحي إلا بإذن الأب انتهى، وإنما يستحب تقديمه على الولي، إذا كان أفضل من الولي ، كذا في ( البحر » عن «شرح المجمع لمصنفه. وفي « التاتارخانية » عن « الخلاصة ) : إمام الحي أولى من الولي في الصحيح من الرواية، وفي ( التبيين» عن « جوامع الفقه» : إمام المسجد الجامع أولى من إمام الحي انتهى، والصلاة في الأصل حق الأولياء لقربهم إلا أن الإمام والسلطان يقدمان لعارض الإمامة العظمى والسلطنة، فإن التقدم عليهما فيه ازدراء وفساد أمر المسلمين، فيتحاشا عن ذلك الفساد، فيجب تقديم من له حكـم عام، وأما إمام الحي فيستحب تقديمه على طريق الأفضل، وليس بواجب، كذا في « المستصفى»، ثمَّ الوَلِيُّ) الذكر المكلف إذ لا حق للنساء كالصغار، والمعتوه، كذا في « التاتارخانية»، ويقدم الأقرب فالأقرب من ذوي قرابته، كترتيبهم في التعصيب والإنكاح، ولكن يقدم الأب على الابن في قول الكل على الصحيح لفضله، وفي النكاح يقدم الابن لقربه، قال العلامة « المقدسي » : ولتقديم الأب وجه حسن، وهو أن المقصود الدعاء للميت، ودعوته مستجابة روى أبو هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: ثَلاثُ دَعَوَاتٍ مُسْتَجَابَاتٍ: دَعْوَةُ المَظْلُومِ، وَدَعْوَةُ المَسَافِرِ، وَدَعْوَةُ الوَالِدِ» ()
ولِمَنْ له حقُّ التَّقَدَّم أنْ يأْذَنَ لغيرِهِ، فإن صلى غيره أعادها، إن شاء. ولا يُعِيدُ معه من صلَّى مع غيرِهِ، وَمَنْ له ولايةُ التَّقَدَّم فيها، أحقُّ مِمَّنْ أوصى له الميتُ بالصَّلاةِ عليه على المفتى به. وإِنْ دُفِنَ بلا صلاةٍ صُلِّيَ على قبره، وإن لم يُغَسَلْ، ما لم يَتَفَسَّخ.
وقال الزيلعي والسيد أولى من قريب عبده على الصحيح والقريب أولى من السيد المعتق، فإن لم يكن ولي فالزوج، ثم الجيران. ( ولِمَنْ له حقُّ التَّقَدَّم أنْ يأْذَنَ لغيره، لأن التقدم حقه فيملك إبطاله، وإذا كان لــه وليان فأذن أحدهما لأجنبي فللآخر منعه، وإن قدم كل منهما رجلاً فالذي قدمه الأكبر أولى، لأنهما رضـيـا بسقوط حقهما، وأكبرهما سناً أولى بالصلاة عليه، فيكون أولى بالتقديم، كذا في « التاتارخانية»، (فإن صلى غيره)، أي: غير من له حق التقدم بلا إذنه ولم يعتد به (أعادها) هو (إنْ شاءَ) لعدم سقوط حقه، وإن تأدى الفرض بها، ولا يُعِيدُ مَعهُ) أي: مع من له حق التقدم (من صلـى مـع غـيـره) لعدم مشروعية التنفل بها، كما لا يصلي أحد عليها بعده، وإن صلى وحده، وصلاة النبي الله علـى مـن دفـن بـعـد الصـلاة عليه ) لحق تقدمه بقوله تعالى: ﴿ النَّبِيُّ أَوْلَى بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْ أَنفُسِهِمْ ﴾ [الأخْزَاب : ٦] وللولي حق الإعــادة، وصلاة الصحابة على النبي الله أفواجا ) كانت من الخواص، وإلا لصلي على قبره الشريف إلـى يــوم القيامة لبقائه كما وضع طرياً، بل حياً يُرزق ويتنعم بسائر الملاذ والعبادات. (ومـن لـه ولاية التقدم فيـهـا أحقُّ) بالصلاة عليها مِمَّنْ أوصى له الميّتُ بالصَّلاةِ عليه) قال في «العيون»: إن الوصية باطلة (على المُفْتَى بِهِ)، قال الصدر الشهيد: وفي نوادر ) ابن رستم الوصية جائزة، ويؤمــر فـلان بالصلاة عـلـيـه، كذا في «البرهان». (وإنْ دُفِنَ) وأهيل عليه التراب بلا صلاة لأمر اقتضـى ذلـك (صلي على قبره، وإن لم يُغسل) لسقوط شرط طهارته، ولحرمة ،نبشه فيصلى عليه بلا غسل للضرورة، وتعاد لـو صـلـى عـليـه قبل الدفن بلا غسل لفساد الأولى بالقدرة على تغسيله قبل الدفن، وقيل: تنقلب الأولى صحيحة عند تحقق العجز، فلا تعاد، ولو لم يهل التراب يخرج فيغسل ويصلى عليه ( ا لم يَتَفَسَّخ)، والمعتبر في ذلك أكبر الرأي على الصحيح، وهو احتراز عما روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يصلى عليه إلى ثلاثة أيام، وجـه الصحيح أنه يختلف باختلاف الزمان والمكان والأشخاص.
تنبيه: قال في « التاتارخانية ) عن ( العتابية ) : إذا كان القوم سبعة قاموا ثلاثة صفوف يتقدم واحد، وثلاثة بعده، واثنان بعدهم وواحد بعدهما، لأن في الحديث: «مَنْ صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ ثَلَاثَةُ صُفُوفِ غُفِرَ لَهُ ) (۳) وفي ( البزازية ) : خير صفوف الرجال فيها آخرها، وفي سائر الصلوات أولها، لأن القيام
Chapter on explaining who has the most right to lead the funeral prayer and its related matters. The sultan has the most right to his prayer, then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the neighborhood, then the guardian (wali). Chapter on explaining who has the most right to lead the funeral prayer and its related matters. The sultan has the most right to his prayer – Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) stated this saying: The caliph is most entitled if he is present; if he is not present, then the imam of the city who is its sultan, because he is similar to the caliph, and it is obligatory to honor him, so no one should precede him. Therefore he said: (then his deputy) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because when al-Hasan ibn Ali died, al-Husayn went out with the people for the funeral prayer, and al-Husayn presented Sa'id ibn al-As, and Sa'id was at that time the governor of Medina, i.e., in charge, but he refused to step forward, so al-Husayn said to him: 'Step forward; were it not for the sunna, I would not have put you forward.' And Muhammad said – and it is a narration from the Imam: The guardian of the deceased is most entitled in all circumstances. Allah the Exalted said: {But those of kinship are more entitled to each other} [Quran 33:6]. We said: The verse is interpreted regarding inheritance and the authority of marriage. (Then the qadi) because he is the possessor of authority, and after him the chief of police, then the deputy of the governor, then the deputy of the qadi – al-Zayla'i said that. (Then) if these are not present, it is recommended to present (the imam of the neighborhood) because the deceased chose him during his lifetime. Thus in al-Hidaya. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: The imam of the neighborhood may not advance except with the permission of the father – end quote. He is recommended over the guardian only if he is better than the guardian – thus in al-Bahr from Sharh al-Majma' by its author. In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Khulasa: The imam of the neighborhood is more entitled than the guardian in the correct narration. In al-Tabyin from Jami' al-Fiqh: The imam of the congregational mosque is more entitled than the imam of the neighborhood – end quote. The prayer is originally the right of the guardians because of their closeness, but the imam and the sultan are given precedence due to the reason of the greater imamate and sovereignty, because preceding them involves disrespect and corruption of the Muslims' affairs, so one avoids that corruption, thus it is obligatory to give precedence to one with general authority. As for the imam of the neighborhood, it is recommended to present him as a matter of preference, not obligatory – thus in al-Mustasfa. (Then the guardian) – the male who is legally responsible, for women have no right, like minors and the insane – thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And the closest is presented, then the next closest from among his relatives, like their order in inheritance by ta'sib (residuary) and marriage. However, the father is presented over the son in the opinion of all, based on what is correct, due to his virtue. In marriage, the son is presented because of his closeness. The scholar al-Maqdisi said: For presenting the father there is a good aspect: the purpose is supplication for the deceased, and his supplication is answered. Abu Hurayra narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Three supplications are answered: the supplication of the oppressed, the supplication of the traveler, and the supplication of a parent.' And for the one who has the right of precedence to permit others, if another leads the prayer, he may repeat it if he wishes. And he does not repeat it with him who prayed with another. And one who has authority to lead in it is more entitled than one whom the deceased appointed by will to lead the prayer over him, according to the fatwa. If the deceased is buried without prayer, prayer is performed over his grave, even if he was not washed, as long as he has not decomposed. Al-Zayla'i said: The master is more entitled than the relative of his slave, according to the correct view; and the relative is more entitled than the manumitting master. If there is no guardian, then the husband, then the neighbors. (And for the one who has the right of precedence to permit others) because precedence is his right, so he can nullify it. If there are two guardians and one of them permits a stranger, the other may prevent him. If each puts forward a man, the one put forward by the older one is more entitled, because they both consented to waive their right, and the older one in age is more entitled to lead the prayer over him, so his chosen one is more entitled to be given precedence – thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. (If another leads the prayer), i.e., other than the one entitled to precedence without his permission and he does not count it, (he may repeat it) if he wishes, because his right has not lapsed, even if the obligation is fulfilled by it. And he does not repeat it with him (i.e., the one entitled to precedence) who prayed with another, because there is no basis for performing a supererogatory funeral prayer, just as no one should lead another funeral prayer after it, even if he prays alone. And the Prophet's prayer over one who was buried after the prayer over him was due to his right of precedence by the saying of the Exalted: {The Prophet is more entitled to the believers than themselves} [Quran 33:6]. And the guardian has the right of repetition. The prayer of the Companions over the Prophet in groups was from the elite; otherwise, prayer would have been performed at his noble grave until the Day of Resurrection due to his staying fresh as if just placed, rather he is alive, provided for, and enjoying all pleasures and acts of worship. (And one who has authority of precedence in it is more entitled) to lead the prayer over him than one whom the deceased appointed by will to lead the prayer over him. In al-Uyun: The will is invalid – according to the fatwa. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: In the Nawadir of Ibn Rustam, the will is valid, and so-and-so is ordered to lead the prayer over him – thus in al-Burhan. (If the deceased is buried) and soil poured over him without prayer due to a necessitating reason, (prayer is performed over his grave, even if he was not washed) because the condition of his purity is waived, and because it is forbidden to exhume him, so prayer is performed without washing out of necessity. And it would be repeated if prayer was performed before burial without washing because the first is invalid due to the ability to wash him before burial. And it is said: The first becomes valid when inability is confirmed, so it is not repeated. If the soil has not been poured, he is taken out, washed, and prayed over. (As long as he has not decomposed). What is considered in that is the majority opinion, on the correct view. This is a caveat to what was narrated from Abu Hanifa that prayer can be performed over him up to three days. The correct view is that it varies according to time, place, and persons. Alert: In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Atabiyya: If the people are seven, they stand in three rows: one goes forward, three behind him, two behind them, and one behind them, because in the hadith: 'Whoever is prayed over by three rows will be forgiven.' In al-Bazzaziyya: The best of rows for men in it is the last, whereas in other prayers it is the first, because standing...
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the hierarchy of those entitled to lead the funeral prayer. The author begins by stating the order: the sultan (ruler), then his deputy, then the qadi, then the imam of the neighborhood, then the guardian (wali). He then provides proofs and explanations for each level. The basis for the sultan's precedence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said the caliph is most entitled, and it is obligatory to honor the ruler and avoid any disrespect that could cause public discord. This is a matter of public order. The deputy (na'ib) comes next according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, citing the practice of al-Husayn who gave precedence to the governor Sa'id ibn al-As. Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, holds that the deceased's guardian is always most entitled, based on the Quranic verse about close relatives being more entitled. The author explains that the verse refers to inheritance and marriage, not funeral prayer. The qadi is next because he has general authority. If none of these are present, the imam of the neighborhood is recommended, not obligatory, and only if he is more virtuous than the guardian. Some scholars hold that the imam of the neighborhood is more entitled than the guardian, while others give priority to the imam of the congregational mosque. The reason for prioritizing public officials over guardians is to avoid fitna (discord). The guardian's right is original, but it is overridden by the ruler due to the greater good. Among guardians, the closest male relative is given precedence, with the father preferred over the son due to the virtue of his supplication. The text then discusses several related rulings: (1) The one with the right of precedence may delegate another to lead; if someone else leads without permission, the one entitled may repeat the prayer at his discretion, but those who prayed with the unauthorized imam do not repeat. (2) A person appointed by the deceased's will to lead the prayer is not given priority over the rightful guardian; the will in this matter is invalid according to the fatwa, though there is a dissenting narration. (3) If a person is buried without prayer, one may pray over the grave, even if he was not washed, as long as the body has not decomposed. This is due to necessity and the prohibition of exhuming. However, if prayer was performed before burial without washing, it is invalid and must be repeated because washing was possible. (4) An additional note on the arrangement of rows: for funeral prayer, the best row is the last, opposite to other prayers. The text includes several intra-Hanafi disputes, such as the position of Muhammad al-Shaybani on the guardian's priority, and the different views on the validity of the deceased's will regarding who should lead. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the will is invalid. The commentary as a whole provides a comprehensive treatment of who is entitled to lead the funeral prayer, integrating proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, practice of the Companions, and the principles of public interest and avoidance of discord.

Key Terms
التفسخ (al-tafassukh): Decomposition of the body.
الصلاة على القبر (al-salat ala al-qabr): Funeral prayer performed at the grave after burial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition may the funeral prayer be performed over a grave without washing the deceased?
A) The deceased was a martyr
B) The body has not decomposed
C) The family requests it
D) The sultan permits it

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer over the grave is valid without washing if the body has not decomposed, reflecting a leniency due to necessity.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Right of Precedence in Leading the Funeral Prayer
Rulings on who leads the funeral prayer and delegation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of who has the right to lead the funeral prayer and explain why a deceased's will appointing an imam is invalid according to the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The wali's right to lead the funeral prayer cannot be overridden by the deceased's will; delegation is permitted but not obligation.

This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah clarifies the rules of precedence in leading the janazah prayer. It establishes that the wali (guardian) holds the primary right, which he may delegate, but a will appointing someone else is invalid. The text also outlines a hierarchy of walis and cites the Quranic verse supporting the Prophet's ultimate precedence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
The one with wilayat al-taqaddum (wali) is more entitled than any appointee of the deceased. This is the mufta bihi.
The ruling is based on the authority of the wali being established by Sharia.
2
Understand the hierarchy
The order: master > relative of slave > manumitting master > husband > neighbors. This determines who is the wali in absence of closer relatives.
The hierarchy is derived from the text's explicit statements.
3
Recognize the delegation rule
The wali may authorize another to lead. If someone leads without permission, the wali may repeat the prayer if he wishes.
Delegation does not forfeit the right; it merely permits another to act.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
The mufta bihi holds that a deceased's will appointing an imam is invalid. A rare transmission (Nawadir of Ibn Rustam) validates it, but the fatwa is on the invalidity.
The practical difference: who leads when a will exists.
5
Connect the proof
Quran 33:6 states the Prophet is 'awlā' (more entitled) to the believers. By analogy, the wali is more entitled to lead the funeral prayer.
The dalāla is zanni; the analogy is drawn via the concept of priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولِمَنْ له حقُّ التَّقَدُّم أنْ يأْذَنَ لغيرِهِ، فإن صلى غيره أعادها، إن شاء. ولا يُعِيدُ معه من صلَّى مع غيرِهِ، وَمَنْ له ولايةُ التَّقَدَّم فيها، أحقُّ مِمَّنْ أوصى له الميتُ بالصَّلاةِ عليه على المفتى به. وقال الزيلعي والسيد أولى من قريب عبده على الصحيح والقريب أولى من السيد المعتق، فإن لم يكن ولي فالزوج، ثم الجيران. ولِمَنْ له حقُّ التَّقَدُّم أنْ يأْذَنَ لغيره، لأن التقدم حقه فيملك إبطاله، وإذا كان له وليان فأذن أحدهما لأجنبي فللآخر منعه، وإن قدم كل منهما رجلاً فالذي قدمه الأكبر أولى، لأنهما رضيا بسقوط حقهما، وأكبرهما سناً أولى بالصلاة عليه، فيكون أولى بالتقديم، كذا في التاتارخانية. فإن صلى غيره، أي: غير من له حق التقدم بلا إذنه ولم يعتد به أعادها هو إن شاء لعدم سقوط حقه، وإن تأدى الفرض بها، ولا يُعِيدُ معه، أي: مع من له حق التقدم، من صلى مع غيره لعدم مشروعية التنفل بها، كما لا يصلي أحد عليها بعده، وإن صلى وحده. وصلاة النبي ﷺ على من دفن بعد الصلاة عليه لحق تقدمه بقوله تعالى: ﴿ النَّبِيُّ أَوْلَى بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْ أَنفُسِهِمْ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٦] وللولي حق الإعادة. وصلاة الصحابة على النبي ﷺ أفواجاً كانت من الخواص، وإلا لصلي على قبره الشريف إلى يوم القيامة لبقائه كما وضع طرياً، بل حياً يُرزق ويتنعم بسائر الملاذ والعبادات. ومن له ولاية التقدم فيها أحق بالصلاة عليها ممن أوصى له الميت بالصلاة عليه. قال في العيون: إن الوصية باطلة على المفتى به. قال الصدر الشهيد: وفي نوادر ابن رستم الوصية جائزة، ويؤمر فلان بالصلاة عليه، كذا في البرهان.
Whoever has the right of precedence may authorize someone else. If another leads (without permission), he may repeat (the prayer) if he wishes. Those who prayed with the unauthorized imam do not repeat with the rightful one. And the one who has the authority of precedence in it is more entitled than the one whom the deceased appointed in his will, according to the mufta bihi. Al-Zayla'i said: The master is more entitled than the relative of his slave, according to the correct view, and the relative is more entitled than the manumitting master. If there is no wali, then the husband, then the neighbors. The one with the right of precedence may authorize another because the right is his, so he can nullify it. If there are two walis, and one authorizes a stranger, the other may prevent him. If each appoints a man, the one appointed by the elder takes precedence, because they both consented to relinquish their rights, and the elder in age is more entitled to lead, so his appointment is preferred, as in al-Tatarakhaniyya. If another leads, i.e., other than the one with right, without his permission and he does not consider it valid, the one with right may repeat it, if he wishes, because his right is not dropped, even if the obligation is fulfilled. Those who prayed with the unauthorized imam do not repeat with the one with right, because the supererogatory prayer over her is not legislated, just as no one prays over her after that, even if he prays alone. The prayer of the Prophet (peace be upon him) over him who was buried after the prayer over him was due to his precedence by His statement: 'The Prophet is more entitled to the believers than themselves' (33:6). The wali has the right to repeat. The prayer of the Companions over the Prophet (peace be upon him) in groups was from the elite, otherwise prayer would have been over his noble grave until the Day of Resurrection due to its preservation as fresh, but he is alive and provided for. And the one with authority of precedence in it is more entitled to lead than the one whom the deceased appointed in his will. He said in al-Uyun: The will is invalid according to the mufta bihi. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: In the Nawadir of Ibn Rustam, the will is valid, and so-and-so is ordered to pray over him, as in al-Burhan.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah addresses the rules of precedence in leading the funeral prayer. The key point is that the person with the 'right of precedence' – the wali (guardian) – has primary authority. He may delegate to another, but if someone leads without his permission, he retains the right to repeat the prayer for the deceased. The wali is more entitled than anyone the deceased may have appointed in a will; such a will is considered invalid according to the mufta bihi (the relied-upon position), though a rare transmission (Nawadir) allows it. The passage also outlines a hierarchy of entitlement: the master of a slave is more entitled than the slave's relative, but the relative is more entitled than the manumitting master. If no wali exists, the husband leads, then the neighbors. If there are two walis, they may each appoint someone; if they disagree, the appointment of the elder (in age) takes precedence. The proof for the Prophet's ultimate precedence is the verse from Surah al-Ahzab, which analogically applies to the wali.

Key Terms
حق التقدم (haqq al-taqaddum): The right to lead the funeral prayer, held by the wali (guardian) or other qualified person.
ولاية التقدم (wilayat al-taqaddum): The authority or guardianship that gives precedence in leading the funeral prayer.
ولي (wali): A guardian or person with the right to lead the funeral prayer, typically a relative or master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi, who is more entitled to lead the funeral prayer: the wali (guardian) or a person appointed by the deceased in their will?
A) The appointed person
B) The wali
C) The husband
D) The eldest son

Key Takeaway
The wali's right to lead the funeral prayer is paramount; a deceased's will appointing another is invalid according to the mufta bihi.

Prayer at the Grave: Conditions and Validity
Ruling on praying at the grave after burial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying at the grave after burial and explain the condition of non-decomposition as the standard, resolving the apparent dispute about the three-day limit.

Core Idea
The permissibility of prayer at the grave depends on the body not having decomposed, assessed by the most knowledgeable person present.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: a deceased Muslim is buried without the funeral prayer due to an exigency. The Hanafi school permits praying at the grave, provided the body has not yet decomposed. But how is 'decomposition' determined? And what about a narration that sets a three-day limit? The passage clarifies the correct view and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
Read the passage to determine when prayer at the grave is valid. Note that the condition for validity is that the body has not decomposed (lam yatafassakh), and that ghusl is waived due to necessity and prohibition of exhumation.
The ruling applies when burial occurred without prayer for a legitimate reason.
2
Understand the waiver of ghusl
Recognise that if the body was not washed before burial, washing is not required because exhumation is prohibited. The prayer is performed directly at the grave.
This is based on the legal maxim of necessity overriding conditions.
3
Resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute on time limit
Note the difference: one view attributed to Abu Hanifa sets a three-day limit; the correct view (al-sahih) states that it depends on actual decomposition, assessed by akbar al-ra'y (the judgment of the most knowledgeable person present).
The dispute is resolved by referencing varying conditions of time, place, and persons.
4
Apply the standard of akbar al-ra'y
Understand that decomposition varies; thus the assessment must be made by an expert. In practice, a local scholar or imam evaluates the state of the body.
This avoids rigidity and accommodates different climates and burial conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن دُفِنَ وأهيل عليه التراب بلا صلاة لأمر اقتضى ذلك صلي على قبره، وإن لم يُغسل لسقوط شرط طهارته، ولحرمة نبشه فيصلى عليه بلا غسل للضرورة، وتعاد لو صلى عليه قبل الدفن بلا غسل لفساد الأولى بالقدرة على تغسيله قبل الدفن، وقيل: تنقلب الأولى صحيحة عند تحقق العجز، فلا تعاد، ولو لم يهل التراب يخرج فيغسل ويصلى عليه لم يَتَفَسَّخ، والمعتبر في ذلك أكبر الرأي على الصحيح، وهو احتراز عما روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يصلى عليه إلى ثلاثة أيام، وجه الصحيح أنه يختلف باختلاف الزمان والمكان والأشخاص.
And if he is buried and soil is poured over him without prayer for a reason that necessitated that, prayer is performed over his grave, even if he was not washed, because the condition of his purity is dropped, and due to the prohibition of exhuming him; so prayer is performed over him without washing due to necessity. If prayer was performed over him before burial without washing, it is repeated because the first becomes invalid due to the ability to wash him before burial. And it is said: The first becomes valid when incapacity is realized, so it is not repeated. If soil has not been poured over him, he is taken out, washed, and prayed over, as long as he has not decomposed. The criterion in that is the greatest opinion (akbar al-ra'y) according to the correct view, and this is a caution against what was narrated from Abu Hanifa that prayer is performed over him up to three days. The basis of the correct view is that it varies by time, place, and persons.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where a deceased Muslim is buried without the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) due to some exigency. The ruling is that it is permissible to pray at the grave, even without washing the body, because exhumation is prohibited (to avoid disrespect) and the condition of ritual purity (ghusl) is waived due to necessity. If the prayer was performed before burial but without washing, it is invalid because washing was still possible; however, a minority view (qīl) holds that if capacity was already absent, the prayer becomes valid retroactively. If the body has not yet been fully buried (soil not poured), it should be exhumed, washed, and prayed over normally. The key condition for prayer at the grave is that the body has not decomposed. The standard for decomposition is 'akbar al-ra'y' (the judgment of the person with the best opinion), which varies by climate and case – a refinement of an earlier view attributed to Abu Hanifa that set a fixed three-day limit.

Key Terms
أكبر الرأي (akbar al-ra'y): The judgment of the most knowledgeable person present regarding whether the body has decomposed.
لم يَتَفَسَّخ (lam yatafassakh): The body has not yet decomposed or disintegrated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key condition for performing the funeral prayer at a grave after burial?
A) Within three days of burial
B) The body must have been washed
C) The body has not decomposed
D) The grave must be at least one month old

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of prayer at the grave hinges on the body not having decomposed, assessed by the most knowledgeable person present, not a fixed number of days.
