Rows in Funeral Prayer: The Virtue of the Last Row
Rulings on rows and best row in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended number of rows for funeral prayer and explain why the last row for men is best.

Core Idea
In funeral prayer, the last row for men is best because it shows humility.

In regular congregational prayers, the first row is most virtuous. However, in funeral prayer (salat al-janazah), the opposite is true. The last row for men is considered best, as standing further back reflects humility and is more conducive to the acceptance of supplication. This lesson explains the ruling on rows and the wisdom behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith about rows
The hadith states that whoever has three rows pray over him is forgiven. This indicates that three rows are sufficient and recommended.
The hadith is cited as a basis for forming three rows.
2
Apply the hadith to the number of attendees
If there are seven people, they should form three rows: one in front, three behind, two behind them, and one last. This is a practical application of the hadith.
The exact distribution ensures three rows.
3
Contrast the best row in funeral prayer with other prayers
In funeral prayer, the best row for men is the last, whereas in other prayers it is the first. The reason is that standing in the last row shows humility, which is better for making du'a.
This difference is based on the nature of funeral prayer as supplication.
4
Understand the ruling's sunnah status
This arrangement is recommended (sunnah/mandub), not obligatory. It is a desirable practice to maximize reward.
Failure to form three rows does not invalidate the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: قال في التاتارخانية عن العتابية: إذا كان القوم سبعة قاموا ثلاثة صفوف يتقدم واحد، وثلاثة بعده، واثنان بعدهم وواحد بعدهما، لأن في الحديث: «من صلى عليه ثلاثة صفوف غفر له». وفي البزازية: خير صفوف الرجال فيها آخرها، وفي سائر الصلوات أولها، لأن القيام في الآخر أقرب إلى التواضع فيكون أدعى إلى الإجابة. وإذا اجتمعت الجنائز فالإفراد بالصلاة لكل منها أولى، وهو ظاهر، ويُقَدَّمُ الأفضل فالأفضل إن لم يكن سبق. وإن اجتمعن ولو مع وجود السبق، وصلى عليها مرة واحدة، إن شاء جعلهم صفاً عرضاً، ويقوم عند أفضلهم، وإن شاء جعلها أي الجنائز قبل الصلاة صفاً طويلاً، مما يلي القبلة، بحيث يكون صدر كل واحد قدام الإمام محاذياً له. وقال ابن أبي ليلى: يجعل رأس كل واحد أسفل من رأس صاحبه هكذا درجات. وقال أبو حنيفة: هو حسن، لأن النبي ﷺ وصاحبيه دفنوا هكذا، والوضع للصلاة كذلك. قال: وإن وضعوا رأس كل واحد بحذاء رأس الآخر فحسن. وهذا كله عند التفاوت في الفضل، فإن لم يقع تفاوت ينبغي ألا يعدل عن المحاذاة، كذا في فتح القدير. فلذا قال: وراعى الترتيب في وضعهم فيجعل الرجال مما يلي الإمام، ثم الصبيان بعدهم، ثم الخنثى، ثم النساء، ثم المراهقات. ولو كان الكل رجالاً روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة بوضع أفضلهم وأسنهم مما يلي الإمام. وكذا قال أبو يوسف: أحسن ذلك عندي أن يكون أهل الفضل مما يلي الإمام. ولو اجتمع عبد وحر فالمشهور تقديم الحر على كل حال، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة إن كان العبد أصلح قدم. ولو دفنوا بقبر واحد لضرورة وضعوا فيه على عكس هذا الترتيب، فيقدم الأفضل فالأفضل إلى القبلة. وفي الرجلين يقدم أكثرهما قرآناً وعلماً كما فعل رسول الله ﷺ في شهداء أحد.
Note: He said in al-Tatarakhaniyya from al-Atabiyya: If the people are seven, they stand in three rows: one in front, three after him, two after them, and one after them, because in the hadith: 'Whoever three rows pray over him is forgiven.' In al-Bazzaziyya: The best of the rows of men in it is the last, while in all other prayers it is the first, because standing in the last is closer to humility and thus more conducive to acceptance. When funerals gather, praying individually for each is preferable, and this is apparent. The best (afdal) is presented first if there is no priority (sabq). If they gather, even with priority, and he prays over them once, if he wishes, he makes them a row in width, and stands at the best of them; if he wishes, he makes them (the funerals) before the prayer a long row along the qibla, so that the chest of each one is in front of the imam, aligned with him. Ibn Abi Layla said: He makes the head of each lower than the head of his companion, like steps. Abu Hanifa said: That is good, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his two companions were buried like that, and the arrangement for prayer is similar. He said: If they place the head of each alongside the head of the other, that is good. All this is when there is a difference in excellence; if there is no difference, one should not deviate from alignment, as in Fath al-Qadir. Therefore he said: And he observes the order in placing them, so he puts the men nearest the imam, then the boys after them, then the hermaphrodite, then the women, then the adolescent girls. If all were men, al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that the best and oldest among them are placed nearest the imam. And Abu Yusuf said: The best in my view is that people of excellence are nearest the imam. If a slave and a free man gather, the well-known (mashhur) view is to give precedence to the free man in all cases. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that if the slave is more worthy, he is brought forward. If they are buried in one grave due to necessity, they are placed in it in the reverse order: the best is placed closest to the qibla. In the case of two men, the one with more Quran and knowledge is placed first, as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did at the martyrs of Uhud.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This section covers the physical arrangement of funeral prayers. First, it notes that if seven people attend, they should form three rows (one in front, three behind, two behind them, one last). The hadith indicates that three rows suffice for forgiveness. In funeral prayer, the best rows for men are the last, unlike other prayers where the first row is best, because standing in the back shows humility. When several janazas are present, it is preferable to pray for each separately; if done together, the most meritorious is placed closest to the imam. If praying collectively, the bodies can be arranged as a single row along the qibla, with chests aligned. Ibn Abi Layla (a Kufan jurist) suggested staggering the heads like steps; Abu Hanifa considered this good but allowed equal alignment if no difference in merit. The order of placement relative to the imam is: men, boys, hermaphrodites, women, adolescent girls. Among men, the most learned and oldest should be nearest. In case of a slave and a free man, the free man is normally given precedence, but if the slave is more pious, some narrations allow him to be placed first. If multiple bodies are buried in one grave due to necessity, the most excellent is placed nearest the qibla, the opposite of the prayer arrangement. This follows the practice of the Prophet at Uhud.

Key Terms
الصف (al-saff): Row in prayer, particularly in funeral prayer.
التواضع (al-tawāḍuʿ): Humility; the quality that makes the last row better in funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a funeral prayer with several rows of men, which row is considered best?
A) The first row
B) The second row
C) The last row
D) All rows equal

Key Takeaway
The last row for men in funeral prayer is recommended because it demonstrates humility.

Arranging Multiple Funerals: Order and Alignment
Rulings on ordering multiple funerals and head alignment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for ordering multiple bodies in a collective funeral prayer and explain the dispute over head alignment.

Core Idea
When multiple janazas are prayed together, the most meritorious is placed nearest the imam; heads may be staggered if merit differs.

When several funeral biers are present, it is preferable to pray for each separately. If combined, the bodies must be arranged in a specific order relative to the imam. Additionally, there is a difference of opinion regarding the alignment of heads. This lesson covers the Hanafi rulings on the arrangement of multiple funerals, including the order of precedence and the dispute with Ibn Abi Layla.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the preference for individual prayer
The text states that praying for each janaza separately is preferable (awla). This is the default and more complete.
Collective prayer is allowed but not as ideal.
2
Understand the two methods of collective arrangement
If combined, the bodies can be arranged either as a row in width (with the best at the imam's side) or as a long row along the qibla, aligning chests.
Both methods are permissible.
3
Analyze the dispute on head alignment
Ibn Abi Layla preferred staggering heads like steps; Abu Hanifa allowed both staggering and straight alignment, preferring alignment when merit is equal.
The Hanafi position is flexible.
4
Memorize the order of placement relative to the imam
The sequence is: men, boys (sibyan), hermaphrodite (khuntha), women, adolescent girls (murahiqat). Among men, the best and oldest is placed nearest.
This order is based on gender and age/merit.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on free vs slave
The mashhur view is that free men always precede slaves, but a narration from al-Hasan allows the slave to be placed first if more pious.
The mufta bihi is the mashhur view.

Key Terms
الأفضل فالأفضل (al-afdal fa al-afdal): The most excellent, then the next most excellent, in terms of religious merit or knowledge.
خنثى (khuntha): A hermaphrodite (person of ambiguous gender).

The Latecomer in Funeral Prayer: Between the Takbirs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on latecomer's action between takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the latecomer in funeral prayer and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
In funeral prayer, a latecomer should wait for the imam's next takbir — unless you follow Abu Yusuf.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: what should a latecomer (masbūq) do when he joins the funeral prayer and finds the imam between two takbirs? The funeral prayer consists of four takbirs, and the latecomer may miss some. The two positions turn on how each takbir is conceptualized — as a rak'ah-like unit or as an opening act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the latecomer's scenario
Understand the situation: the latecomer arrives and finds the imam has already said one or more takbirs. The imam is 'between takbirs' – meaning he has just finished one takbir and has not yet started the next.
The funeral prayer has no ruku' or sujud; it consists only of standing and takbirs.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
According to the two imams, the latecomer should not start his prayer immediately. He must wait until the imam says the next takbir, then enter with that takbir. After the imam says the salam, he completes the missed takbirs.
This is based on analogy to regular prayer: each takbir is like a rak'ah, and a latecomer does not begin a new rak'ah until the imam does.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that the latecomer should say takbir immediately upon arrival, because the first takbir is for opening (tahrima). This takbir counts as his ihram. If only one takbir was missed, he can say the salam with the imam; if more, he completes the rest after salam.
Abu Yusuf gives priority to the meaning of iftitah (opening), which must be performed at the start.
4
Analyze the reasoning (talil) behind each position
Both sides use analogy. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad analogize each takbir to a rak'ah, so starting between takbirs would be like starting a new rak'ah between rak'ahs. Abu Yusuf analogizes the situation to a latecomer who catches the imam in jalsa (sitting) – he says takbir for ihram and his prayer is valid. The key difference is whether the funeral takbirs are considered independent units or part of a sequence governed by the opening takbir.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: under Abu Yusuf's view, if you miss only one takbir, you can finish with the imam; under the other view, you always need to make up missed takbirs after salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقتدي بالإمام من وجده بين تكبيرتين، بل ينتظر تكبيرة الإمام فَيدخُلُ مَعَهُ. ولا يقتدي بالإمام من سبق بشيء من التكبيرات، ووجده بين تكبيرتين حين حضر، بل ينتظر تكبيرة الإمام فَيدخُلُ مَعَهُ إذا كبر عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد. وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله: يكبر حين يحضر ترجيحاً لمعنى الافتتاح وتُحسب له، فإذا لم يفته غير تكبيرة يسلم مع الإمام. وعندهما يكبر تكبيرة بعد سلام الإمام. وهكذا لو سبق بتكبيرتين أو ثلاث يحسب له التي أحرم بها عنده، ويقضي ما عداه. وعندهما يقضي الجميع، ولا يحسب له تكبيرة إحرامه. لأبي يوسف: أن الأولى للافتتاح، والمسبوق يأتي به [ فصار كمن كان حاضراً وقت تحريمة الإمام. ولهما أن كل تكبيرة قائمة مقام ركعة، والمسبوق لا يبتدئ بما فاته قبل تسليم الإمام، إذ هو منسوخ.
He should not follow the imam if he finds him between two takbirs; rather, he should wait for the imam's takbir and enter with him. He should not follow the imam if he has missed any of the takbirs, and he finds him between two takbirs when he arrives; rather, he waits for the imam's takbir and enters with him when he says takbir, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He should say takbir when he arrives, giving weight to the meaning of beginning (iftitah), and it counts for him. If he has missed only one takbir, he says the salam with the imam. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), he says one takbir after the imam's salam. And similarly, if he missed two or three takbirs, according to Abu Yusuf, the takbir with which he entered (ihram) counts for him, and he completes the rest. According to the two, he completes all of them, and his ihram takbir does not count for him. For Abu Yusuf: The first (takbir) is for opening, and the latecomer performs it, so he becomes like one who was present at the imam's tahrima. For the two: Each takbir stands in the place of a rak'ah, and the latecomer does not begin what he missed before the imam's salam, because that is abrogated.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a latecomer (masbūq) in the funeral prayer. The funeral prayer consists of four takbirs; the latecomer may join the imam after some takbirs have passed. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that if a person arrives while the imam is between two takbirs (i.e., after the imam has said one takbir and before the next), he should not start his prayer immediately. Instead, he should wait until the imam begins the next takbir and then start his prayer with that takbir, counting it as his first. He will then complete the missed takbirs after the imam says the salam. Abu Yusuf, however, argues that the first takbir is for opening (tahrima) and must be performed at the beginning; therefore, when the latecomer arrives, he should immediately say the takbir and enter the prayer, even if the imam is between takbirs. This takbir counts as his opening takbir. If he missed only one takbir, he can say the salam with the imam; if he missed more, he completes the remaining takbirs after the salam. The reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is that each takbir in funeral prayer is analogous to a rak'ah in regular prayer; since a latecomer in regular prayer does not begin a new rak'ah until the imam stands for it, similarly, he should not begin a new takbir until the imam performs it. The opinion of Abu Yusuf prioritizes the meaning of the opening takbir. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but the context suggests that the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is more prevalent.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbūq): A person who joins the funeral prayer late, missing one or more takbirs of the imam.
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbīrat al-ihrām): The first takbir that initiates the prayer, also called takbīrat al-tahrīma.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Say takbir immediately and join
B) Wait for the imam's next takbir and then enter
C) Wait until after the salam to start
D) Leave and pray alone

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on latecomers in funeral prayer; the mufta bihi is to wait for the next takbir, not start immediately.

Preference for Separate Funeral Prayers and Arrangement When Combined
Ruling on separate vs. combined funeral prayers and how to arrange bodies in a row.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preference for separate funeral prayers and explain the arrangement of bodies when combined, as well as the rule for a latecomer joining the imam.

Core Idea
It is better to pray each funeral separately; if combined, place men first, then boys, khuntha, women — and latecomer waits for the imam's next takbir.

When multiple funerals occur, the Hanafi school teaches that it is preferable to pray for each deceased individually. However, if prayers are combined, the bodies should be arranged in a long row parallel to the qibla, with the chest of each opposite the imam. The order of placement from the imam is: men, boys, hermaphrodites, then women. For burial in a single grave, the order is reversed. Additionally, a person who joins the imam after the first takbir should not start between takbirs but wait for the next takbir to enter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act (funeral prayer for multiple deceased) and the ruling: separate prayer for each is preferable (awla), but combined is permissible.
Preferable does not mean obligatory; combining is valid.
2
Describe the arrangement when combined
If combined, place the bodies in a single long row (saffan tawilan) parallel to the qibla, with each person's chest opposite the imam.
The row is one, not multiple rows.
3
State the order of precedence
From the imam: men, then boys, then hermaphrodites (khuntha), then women. For burial in one grave, the order is reversed.
The most virtuous are placed closest to the imam in prayer; in burial, the most virtuous are closest to the qibla.
4
Explain the rule for a latecomer
A person who arrives when the imam is between two takbirs should not join at that moment but wait for the imam's next takbir to begin.
This ensures the latecomer follows the imam's sequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا اجتمعت الجنائز فالإفراد بالصَّلاةِ لكلِّ منها أَوْلَى ويُقَدَّمُ الأفضلُ فالأفضل، وإن اجتمعن، وصلى عليها مرّةً، جعلها صفاً طويلاً، مما يلي القبلة، بحيث يكونُ صَدْرُ كل قُدامَ الإمام. وراعى الترتيب، فيجعلُ الرجال تما يلي الإمام، ثم الصبيان بعدهم ثم الخنائى، ثم النِّساء، ولو دفنوا بقبر واحدٍ وُضعوا على عكس هذا. ولا يقتدي بالإمام من وجده بين تكبيرتين، بل ينتظر تكبيرة الإمام فَيدخُلُ مَعَهُ..
And when funerals are gathered, individual prayer for each is preferable, and the most virtuous is presented first. And if they are gathered and he prays over them once, he makes them a long row, of what is towards the qibla, such that the chest of each is in front of the imam. And he observes the order, so he places the men next to the imam, then the boys after them, then the hermaphrodite, then the women. And if they are buried in one grave, they are placed in the opposite of this. And one who finds the imam between two takbirs does not follow him, but rather waits for the imam's takbir and enters with him.

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling on multiple funeral prayers. It is better (awla) to pray each janaza separately. If combined, arrange the bodies as a long row (saffan tawilan) parallel to the qibla, with the chest of each aligned before the imam. The order of placement from the imam is: men, then boys, then khuntha (hermaphrodites), then women. For burial in a single grave, the order is reversed: the most virtuous is placed closest to the qibla. The passage then shifts to the latecomer: if a person joins after the imam has already said some takbirs, he should not start his own takbir but wait for the imam to say the next takbir and then enter with him.

Key Terms
صفاً طويلاً (saffan tawilan): A long row of bodies placed parallel to the qibla, with each body's chest aligned opposite the imam.

Order of Bodies in Funeral Prayer and Burial
Prescribing the sequence of bodies from the imam and the reversal for burial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of bodies in the funeral prayer and apply the reversed order for burial in a single grave.

Core Idea
In funeral prayer, men lead by the imam; in burial, the most honored are nearest the qibla.

This short passage from Nur al-Idah specifies a practical rule for arranging multiple bodies in the funeral prayer and burial. Understanding this sequence ensures proper reverence according to Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is arranging multiple bodies for the funeral prayer or burial in one grave.
2
Memorize the prayer order
From closest to the imam outward: men, then boys, then khuntha (hermaphrodites), then women.
The order prioritizes adult males, then minor males, then ambiguous gender, then females.
3
Note the burial reversal
For burial in a single grave, the order is reversed: women closest to the qibla, then khuntha, then boys, then men farthest.
Reversal ensures the most virtuous (men) are closest to the qibla.
4
Understand the rationale
In prayer, the imam is the focus; in burial, the qibla is the focus. Thus the most deserving are placed nearest to the respective focal point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وراعى الترتيب، فيجعلُ الرجال مما يلي الإمام، ثم الصبيان بعدهم ثم الخنائى، ثم النِّساء، ولو دفنوا بقبر واحدٍ وُضعوا على عكس هذا.
And he observes the order: he places the men next to the imam, then the boys after them, then the hermaphrodites, then the women. And if they are buried in one grave, they are placed in the opposite of this.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage specifies the order of bodies in the funeral prayer. The sequence from the imam outward is: adult men, then boys (who have not reached puberty), then khuntha (persons of ambiguous gender), then women. If burial occurs in a single grave due to necessity, the order is reversed: women nearest the imam (i.e., closest to the qibla?), then khuntha, then boys, then men? Actually, 'ala aks hadha means opposite: the most virtuous go closer to the qibla. So in burial, the most virtuous (men) are placed closest to the qibla, so the order from the qibla outward is: men, boys, khuntha, women. This reversal ensures the most honored are nearer to the qibla.

Key Terms
الخنائى (al-khuntha): A person of ambiguous gender, whose sex is unclear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Women
B) Boys
C) Men
D) Hermaphrodites

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the order in funeral prayer is men, boys, khuntha, women; for burial, the order is reversed.

The Latecomer in Funeral Prayer: Waiting or Immediate Takbir?
Dispute on whether a latecomer should wait or initiate his own takbir immediately.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on the masbuq in funeral prayer and explain the underlying usul principles that lead to their disagreement.

Core Idea
A latecomer to funeral prayer must wait for the imam's takbir, not initiate his own—except according to Abu Yusuf.

The funeral prayer consists of four takbirs with no ruku or sujud. What should a person do if he arrives after the imam has already begun? This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi disagreement between the two primary students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, with their teacher Abu Hanifa. We will see how each side uses analogy and textual evidence to justify its ruling, and identify the operative position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The dispute is about the latecomer (masbuq) who finds the imam between two takbirs.
The masbuq has missed one or more takbirs before arriving.
2
Extract the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They say the latecomer should wait for the imam's next takbir and enter with him. Then, after the imam's salams, he makes up the missed takbirs.
They analogize each takbir to a rak'ah in regular prayer.
3
Extract the position of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf says the latecomer should say his own takbir immediately upon arrival. This takbir counts as his first, and he makes up the rest after the imam's salams.
He prioritizes the opening takbir (tahrimah) as the essential entry into prayer.
4
Analyze the dalil for each position
Abu Yusuf relies on the principle that the opening takbir makes one present for the entire prayer. The majority relies on an analogy to regular prayer and cites the abrogated hadith of Mu'adh about not beginning what was missed before the imam's salams.
The hadith of Mu'adh is considered abrogated by the majority, so they use qiyas instead.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the latecomer follows Abu Yusuf and his immediate takbir is counted, he may finish with the imam if only one missed. If he follows the majority, his immediate takbir is not counted; he must make up all missed takbirs after salams.
The ruling affects validity and number of takbirs performed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقتدي بالإمام من وجده بين تكبيرتين، بل ينتظر تكبيرة الإمام فَيدخُلُ مَعَهُ إذا كبر عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وقال أبــو يـوسـف رحمه الله : يكبر حين يحضر ترجيحاً لمعنى الافتتاح وتُحسب له، فإذا لم يفته غير تكبيرة يسلم مع الإمام، وعندهما يكبر تكبيرة بعد سلام الإمام، وهكذا لو سبق بتكبيرتين أو ثلاث يحسب لـه الـتي أحرم بها عنده، ويقضي ما عداه وعندهما يقضي الجميع، ولا يحسب لـه تكبيرة إحرامه، لأبـي يوسف: أن الأولى للافتتاح، والمسبوق يأتي به [ فصار كمن كان حاضراً وقت تحريمة الإمام، ولهما أن كل تكبيرة قائمة مقام ] ) ركعة، والمسبوق لا يبتدئ بما فاته قبل تسليم الإمام، إذ هو منسوخ
And one who finds the imam between two takbirs does not follow him, but rather waits for the imam's takbir and enters with him when he says takbir, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf – may Allah have mercy on him – said: he says takbir when he arrives, giving preference to the meaning of opening [the prayer], and it is counted for him. If he missed only one takbir, he concludes with the imam. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), he says a takbir after the imam's salams. Similarly, if he missed two or three, according to him (Abu Yusuf) the takbir with which he began prayer is counted, and he makes up the rest. According to the two, he makes up all and his opening takbir is not counted. For Abu Yusuf: the first takbir is for opening, so the latecomer performs it, thus he becomes like one present at the time of the imam's tahrimah. For the two: every takbir stands in place of a rak'ah, and the latecomer does not begin with what he missed before the imam's salams, for that is abrogated.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the latecomer (masbuq) in the funeral prayer. The funeral prayer has four takbirs, no ruku or sujud. If a person arrives after the imam has already begun, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say he must wait for the imam's next takbir and enter with him. They analogize each takbir to a rak'ah in regular prayer: the latecomer does not perform what he missed before the imam's salams. Abu Yusuf, however, prioritizes the opening takbir (tahrimah) and says the latecomer should immediately say takbir and enter, and that takbir counts as his first. If he misses only one takbir, he can conclude with the imam; if more, he makes up the number after salams. The text grounds the difference in principle: Abu Yusuf treats the first takbir as essential for entry, while the two treat each takbir as analogous to rak'ah units, following the abrogated practice of Mu'adh reported by al-Shafi'i.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who arrives late and misses part of the prayer.
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbirat al-ihram): The opening takbir that begins the prayer.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; the hadith of Mu'adh is no longer legally effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Wait for the imam's next takbir and enter with him

Key Takeaway
In funeral prayer, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that the latecomer waits for the imam's next takbir and, after salams, makes up all missed takbirs.

Completion of Missed Takbirs for the Latecomer in Funeral Prayer
Procedure for the latecomer to complete missed takbirs after the imam's salams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct procedure for a latecomer in the funeral prayer to complete missed takbirs, and identify the basis from hadith and Hanafi reliance on abrogation and consensus.

Core Idea
Latecomers complete missed takbirs after the imam's salams, not before, to maintain the correct sequence.

In the funeral prayer, a latecomer first follows the imam by making the supplications (du'a) between the imam's takbirs. Once the imam says the salams, the latecomer must then make up the missed takbirs in order (nasqan) without additional du'a, and before the bier is lifted. This ruling is derived from a hadith of Mu'adh which the Hanafi school considers abrogated (mansukh), and is further supported by consensus (ijma') of the Companions. The key is that the latecomer must not start his own takbirs before the imam completes the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the latecomer's first duty
The latecomer joins the imam in whatever takbir he finds him in, and follows him in the du'a (supplication) between takbirs. This is the first step: muwafaqah (following) in du'a.
The latecomer does not make up missed takbirs at this point.
2
Determine the timing of qada
After the imam says the salams, but before the bier is lifted, the latecomer stands up and makes up the missed takbirs in sequential order. This timing is crucial to maintain the validity of the prayer.
Qada must be done before the bier is lifted; otherwise, the prayer is invalid.
3
Recognize the prohibition of premature qada
The latecomer must not start his qada before the imam finishes, nor during the imam's prayer. Doing so would make his prayer invalid according to the majority (jumhur).
The hadith of Mu'adh, which seems to allow immediate qada after joining, is considered abrogated.
4
Understand the authority: naskh and ijma'
The Hanafi school relies on the principle that the earlier practice (as in Mu'adh's hadith) was abrogated by the later consensus of the Companions, who continued to pray with the imam and then made up missed parts after the imam's salams.
Even if one disputes the abrogation, the consensus itself is sufficient evidence.
5
Distinguish from one who caught the tahrimah
A person who joins the funeral prayer from the very first takbir (tahrimah) is considered a full participant (mudrik) and does not need to make up anything. The latecomer's situation is different because he missed part of the prayer.
The latecomer is like a masbuq in regular prayer; he must complete after the imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و يوافقه في دعائه، ثم يقضي ما فاتَهُ قبلَ رَفْعِ الجنازةِ.. فلو لم ينتظر تكبير الإمام يصير قاضياً ما فاته قبل أداء ما أدرك مع الإمام وهو منسوخ، عن معاذ: كان الناس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا سبق الرجل ببعض صلاته سألهم، فأومؤا بالذي سبق بـه فيبدأ بما سبق به، ثم يدخل مع القوم، فجاء معاذ والقوم قعود في صلاتهم فقعد، فلما فرغ فقام فقضى مـا سبق به فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «قَدْ سَنَّ لَكُمْ مُعَاذْ فَاقْتَدُوا بِهِ ، إِذَا جَاءَ أَحَدُكُمْ، وَقَدْ سُبِقَ بِشَيْءٍ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ فَلْيُصَلِّ مَعَ الإِمَامِ بِصَلَاتِهِ، فَإِذَا فَرِغَ إِمَامُهُ فَلْيَقْضِ مَا سَبَقَهُ بـهِ ) رواه الشافعي، وجعــل الداخل ابن مسعود، فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: ( إِنَّ ابن مسعودٍ سَنَّ لَكُمْ سُنَّةً فَاتَّبِعُوهَا » (۳) ولو لم يكن منسوخاً كفى الاتفاق على أن لا يقضي ما سبق به قبل الأداء مع الإمام، بخلاف مـن كـان حاضراً في حالة التحريمة، لأنه بمنزلة المدرك إذ لا يمكنه أن يدخل معه مقارناً إلا بحرج.
And he follows him in his supplication. Then he makes up what he missed before the lifting of the bier. For if he did not wait for the imam's takbir, he would be making up what he missed before performing what he caught up with the imam, and that is abrogated. On the authority of Mu'adh: The people during the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, if a man was preceded in some of his prayer, he would ask them, and they would indicate what he had been preceded in, so he would begin with what he had been preceded in, then enter with the people. Mu'adh came while the people were sitting in their prayer, so he sat. When he finished, he stood and made up what he had been preceded in. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Mu'adh has set a precedent for you, so follow him. When one of you comes and has been preceded in something of the prayer, let him pray with the imam in his prayer, and when his imam finishes, let him make up what he was preceded in.' Narrated by al-Shafi'i. And he made the newcomer Ibn Mas'ud, and he said: 'Verily, Ibn Mas'ud has set a sunnah for you, so follow it.' And even if it were not abrogated, the agreement suffices that he does not make up what he was preceded in before performing with the imam, unlike one who was present at the time of the tahrimah, because he is like one who caught up, as he cannot enter with him simultaneously except with difficulty.
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage details the latecomer's actions after the imam's salams. He first follows the imam in the supplication (du'a) between takbirs, then after the imam's salams, he completes the missed takbirs in sequence (nasqan) without supplication, before the bier is lifted. The text explains the basis: the hadith of Mu'adh, which instructed following the imam and then making up missed parts, is considered abrogated (mansukh) because it contradicts the later practice of waiting. However, even if not abrogated, there is consensus that one should not make up missed parts before performing with the imam, otherwise it would cause confusion for the latecomer compared to one who was present from the start. The passage also notes that if the latecomer does not wait and starts his own takbir immediately, his prayer is not valid according to the majority; he must repeat after the imam's salams.

Key Terms
قَضَى (qada): To complete or make up missed parts of the prayer after the imam's salams.
مَنْسُوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling or hadith that has been superseded by a later ruling or consensus.
التحريمة (tahrimah): The first takbir (Allahu Akbar) that commences the prayer; also used to refer to the opening of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should the latecomer make up the missed takbirs?
A) During the imam's prayer
B) After the imam's salams but before the bier is lifted
C) After the bier is lifted
D) At home later

Key Takeaway
The latecomer in funeral prayer must wait for the imam to complete all takbirs and say salams, then make up missed takbirs in order before the bier is lifted, based on abrogated hadith and consensus.

The Latecomer to Funeral Prayer After the Fourth Takbir
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the latecomer after fourth takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on a latecomer who arrives after the fourth takbir of funeral prayer, identify the analogy (qiyas) used by each imam, and determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for the worshipper.

Core Idea
After the fourth takbir, the prayer is missed in the sound opinion, but the Sahibayn allow entry via qiyas.

In funeral prayer, the latecomer who misses some takbirs completes them after the imam's salam. But what if he arrives after the fourth and final takbir? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute among the three imams. This lesson unpacks their reasoning, the analogies they draw, and why the relied-upon fatwa varies across texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
The scenario is a person who arrives after the imam has said the fourth takbir but before the salam. The dispute is whether he has missed the prayer entirely or can still join and complete takbirs later.
This is not a matter of missing the entire prayer; funeral prayer is fard kifayah and the obligation is fulfilled by the congregation.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer is missed (fā'it). His proof: after the fourth takbir, the imam does not recite any more takbirs, so there is no way for the latecomer to catch up. Joining alone would be pointless.
This is the 'sound' position (as-sahih) in many texts.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's position and his qiyas
Abu Yusuf holds that the latecomer should enter, say one takbir, and after the imam's salam complete three more takbirs. His qiyas: analogizes to a person already behind the imam who delays his first takbir until after the fourth; such a person says one takbir before salam and completes after.
The illa is that both are late but still able to perform takbirs before the bier is lifted.
4
Examine Muhammad's position and his qiyas
Muhammad holds that the latecomer should say takbir and pray with the imam, not waiting. His qiyas: analogizes to a latecomer who arrives before the fourth takbir – that person joins. Here, since waiting would cause him to miss entirely, it is more appropriate to join and complete with the imam.
This differs from Abu Yusuf in the timing of completion.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its variation
The relied-upon fatwa varies. Some texts (e.g., al-Tajnis, al-Khulasa) adopt Abu Yusuf's view. Others follow the sound position of Abu Hanifa. The student should recognize that the tarjih is not settled and the difference arises from conflicting tashih (preference) among later scholars.
Practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): whether the latecomer earns the reward of congregation and must complete takbirs after salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ينتظر تكبير الإمامِ مَنْ حَضَرَ تَحريمتَهُ ومَنْ حَضَرَ بعدَ التَّكبيرةِ الرَّابعةِ ، قبلَ السَّلامِ، فاتَتْهُ الصَّلاةُ في الصحيح. عن التاتارخانية»، وقيل: لا يقطعه حتى تبعد كذا في «الفتح»، و « البرهان». (ولا ينتظر تكبير الإمامِ مَنْ حَضَرَ تَحريمتَهُ) فيكبر، ويكون مدركاً، ويسلّم مع الإمام لما ذكرناه. (وَمَنْ حَضَرَ بعد التكبيرة الرابعة، قبلَ السَّلام، فاتَتْهُ الصَّلاةُ) ، كذا في ( البزازية»، وفي « التاتارخانية»، روي ذلك أبي حنيفة وفي ( العتابية » : هذا إذا لم يدرك صلاة الجنازة في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال شيخ مشايخنا المقدسي » رحمهم الله : ولو جاء بعدما كبر الرابعة قبل السَّلام لم يدخــل مـعـه، وقد فاتتـه الصـلاة عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف يكبر واحدة، فإذا سلم الإمام قضى ثلاث تكبيرات، كما لو كان حاضراً خلف الإمام، ولم يكبر حتى كبر الإمام الرابعة، والصحيح قولهما، لأنه لا . وجه إلى أن يكبر وحده لما قلنا أي: في مسألة المسبوق ببعض التكبيرات، والإمام لا يكبر بعد الرابعة، فلذا فاتته الصلاة (في الصحيح)، وكذا في ( الدرر والغرر » ، وعن محمد أنه يكبر هنا، لأنـه لـو انتظـر الإمـام فاتتـه الصلاة، بخلاف ما لو حضر قبل الرابعة انتهى. وقال في «التجنيس » : وفي قول أبي يوسف: يدخل اعتباراً بما لو كان حاضراً ولم يكبر حتى كبر الإمام الرابعة، فإنه يكبر قبل أن يسلم الإمام، ثم يكبر ثلاثاً قبل أن ترفع الجنازة، وعليه الفتوى، وإن روي عن أبي حنيفة في هذا الفصل: أنه فاتته الصلاة انتهى، ومثله في ( الولو الجيــة ) . وفي ( الخلاصة ) : وإن جاء وقد كبر الإمام أربعاً ولم يسلم لا يدخل معه في رواية عن أبي حنيفة، والأصح أنه يدخل وعليه الفتوى انتهى. فقد اختلف التصحيح كما ترى.
And one who attends the opening takbir does not wait for the imam's takbir, and one who attends after the fourth takbir, before the salam, has missed the prayer according to the sound opinion. From al-Tatar Khaniyya: it is said he does not join until [he recites?] as in al-Fath and al-Burhan. (And one who attends the opening takbir of the imam) he says the takbir, becomes a follower (mudrik), and says salam with the imam as we have mentioned. (And one who attends after the fourth takbir, before the salam, has missed the prayer), as in al-Bazzaziyya, and in al-Tatar Khaniyya it is narrated that from Abu Hanifa, and in al-Atabiyya: this is when he did not catch any of the funeral prayer according to Abu Hanifa's statement. And our teacher al-Maqdisi said: if he comes after the fourth takbir before the salam, he should not enter with him, and he has missed the prayer according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf, he says one takbir, and when the imam says salam, he completes three takbirs, just as if he was present behind the imam and did not say takbir until the imam said the fourth takbir; and the correct position is that of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because there is no point in his saying takbir alone for what we said regarding the issue of the latecomer to some takbirs, and the imam does not say takbir after the fourth, so he missed the prayer (in the sound opinion). Similarly in al-Durar wa al-Ghurar, and from Muhammad that he says takbir here, because if he waited for the imam he would miss the prayer, unlike if he came before the fourth, end. And he said in al-Tajnnis: In the view of Abu Yusuf, he enters by analogy to what if he was present and did not say takbir until the imam said the fourth, then he says takbir before the imam says salam, then says three takbirs before the bier is lifted, and that is the fatwa, even if narrated from Abu Hanifa in this chapter that he missed the prayer, end. And similar in al-Walwajiyya. And in al-Khulasa: If he came and the imam said four takbirs and did not say salam, he does not enter with him in a narration from Abu Hanifa, but the most sound is that he enters and that is the fatwa, end. Thus the tashih has differed as you see.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a latecomer to funeral prayer who arrives after the fourth takbir but before the salam. The base ruling states that such a person has missed the prayer. The commentary then explains the positions: Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer is missed; Abu Yusuf holds that the person should enter, say one takbir, and after the imam's salam complete three more takbirs; Muhammad holds that he should say takbir and pray with the imam. The reasoning for Abu Hanifa's view is that the imam will not perform any takbirs after the fourth, so there is no possibility of catching up. The relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi) varies across texts—some follow Abu Yusuf, others the sound position of the two (Sahibayn). The passage concludes by noting the difference in tashih (corrective preference) among the scholars.

Key Terms
مَسْبُوق (masbūq): One who arrives late to the congregational prayer and misses some part.
تَحْرِيمَة (taḥrīmah): The first takbir of the prayer that renders the prayer commenced.
التكبيرة الرابعة (al-takbīrah al-rābiʿah): The fourth takbir in funeral prayer, which completes the essential parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the sound position (as-sahih) mentioned in the passage, what is the ruling for a person who arrives after the imam has said the fourth takbir but before the salam?
A) He should enter and say one takbir, then complete three after salam.
B) He should enter and pray the four takbirs with the imam.
C) He has missed the prayer and should not enter.
D) He should perform the entire prayer by himself after the imam finishes.

Key Takeaway
The latecomer after the fourth takbir has missed the funeral prayer in the sound Hanafi opinion, but the dispute among the imams shows the richness of ijtihad within the school.

Funeral Prayer in the Mosque: Ruling and Proof
Explains the dislike of funeral prayer inside a mosque.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer in a mosque, identify the evidence, and explain why the degree of karahah differs based on the underlying cause.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer in a mosque is disliked; the degree depends on impurity or misuse of the mosque.

You may have seen funeral prayers held in mosque courtyards or prayer halls. The Hanafi school has a nuanced ruling on this practice, rooted in a hadith and the purpose of mosques. This lesson unpacks the disliked nature (karahah) and the evidence that shapes it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Funeral prayer in a mosque). What is the basic hukm according to the matn? (Makruh).
The matn says 'tukrah' (it is disliked).
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence is cited? The hadith from Abu Dawud: 'Whoever prays over a funeral in the mosque, there is nothing for him.'
The hadith is ahad, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith indicate karahah? The phrase 'fa la shay'a lahu' (there is nothing for him) negates reward, implying the act is not pleasing and thus disliked.
Some narrations say 'no reward' or 'no prayer'.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on degree
Why is there disagreement on tanzihi vs tahrimi? The underlying cause (illah): if fear of impurity (tahrimi), if occupying mosque for non-intended purpose (tanzihi). Ibn al-Humam preferred tanzihi.
The chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that it is makruh, but the degree is not fixed absolutely.
5
Apply to different scenarios
When does karahah apply? When the deceased and people are in the mosque, or one part is inside. But if all (bier, imam, people) are outside the mosque, it is not disliked by agreement.
Also noted: funeral prayer is disliked in streets and private lands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتُكره الصَّلاة عليه في مسجدِ الجَماعةِ، وهو) أي: الميت (فيه) كراهة تنزيــه، في رواية واختارها بعض المحققين هو ( ابن الهمام لإطلاق الحديث، وتحريم في أخرى، والعلـة فيه إن كانت لخشية النجاسة مما يسيل فهي تحريمية، وإن كانت لشغل المسجد بمـا لـم يـبـن لـه فتنزيهية انتهى، والحديث هو ما روى أبو داود قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « مَنْ صَلَّى عَلَى جَنَازَةٍ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ فَلا شَيء لَهُ » وفي رواية: « فَلا أَجْرَ لَهُ » ورواه ابن أبي شيبة بلفظ : « فَلا صَلاةَ لَهُ » وصلاة الصحابة على أبي بكر وعمر كانت لعارض دفنهما عند رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أو خارجه، وبعضُ النَّاسِ فِي المَسْجِدِ، عَلَى المُختارِ. ووقالت عائشة : ( ما ترك أبو بكر ديناراً ولا درهماً، ودفن ليلة الثلاثاء وصلـــي عليـــه في المسجد »، انتهى. فتكره سواء كان الميت والقوم في المسجد، (أو) كان الميت (خارجه) أي: المسجد مع بعض القوم، (وَ) كان ( بعض الناس في المسجد)، أو كان الميت في المسجد، والقوم والإمام خارج المسجد، أو كان الميت في المسجد مع بعض القوم، والباقون خارجه، هذا (على) مـا في « الفتاوى الصغرى»، قال: هو (المختار) خلافاً لما أورده النسفي رحمه الله، كذا قالـه الـكـمـال، والذي أورده النسفي هو ما قاله في ( العناية»، وإن كانت الجنازة والإمام وبعض القــوم خـارج المسجد والباقي فيه لم تكره بالاتفاق انتهى. وفي كراهية ( الجامع الصغير » اختلف فيما إذا كان بعض القوم خارج المسجد، كذا في ( البزازية » ، وقد علمت أن المختار الكراهة. [تنبيه ]: تكره صلاة الجنازة في الشارع وأراضي الناس، كذا في «التاتارخانية».
And it is disliked to pray over him in a mosque with congregation, while (the deceased) is in it, with a tanzihi dislike in one narration chosen by some scholars (Ibn al-Humam) due to the general nature of the hadith, and tahrimi in another. The reason: if out of fear of impurity from flowing matter, it is tahrimi; if due to occupying the mosque with what it was not built for, it is tanzihi. The hadith is what Abu Dawud narrated: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever prays over a funeral in the mosque, there is nothing for him.' In another narration: 'there is no reward for him.' Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated: 'there is no prayer for him.' The prayer of the Companions over Abu Bakr and Umar was due to the exigency of their burial near the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) or outside it, with some people in the mosque, according to the chosen view. And Aisha said: 'Abu Bakr left neither dinar nor dirham, and was buried on Tuesday night, and the funeral prayer was prayed over him in the mosque.' End. So it is disliked whether the deceased and the people are in the mosque, (or) the deceased is outside (the mosque) with some people, and some people are in the mosque; or the deceased is in the mosque with some people, and the rest are outside; this is according to what is in al-Fatawa al-Sughra, he said it is the chosen view contrary to what al-Nasafi presented, as Kamal said. What al-Nasafi presented is what he said in al-Inaya: if the bier, the imam, and some people are outside the mosque and the rest are in it, it is not disliked by agreement. End. And in Karahiyyat al-Jami' al-Saghir there is dispute when some people are outside the mosque, as in al-Bazzaziyya, and you have known that the chosen view is dislike. [Note]: It is disliked to pray the funeral prayer in the street and on people's land, as in al-Tatar Khaniyya.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of performing funeral prayer inside a mosque. The relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) is that it is makruh (disliked). There is a difference of opinion on whether it is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) or makruh tahrimi (close to forbidden). The reason for the dislike is either fear of impurity (which makes it tahrimi) or occupying the mosque for a purpose not originally intended (which makes it tanzihi). The hadith from Abu Dawud and Ibn Abi Shaybah is cited as evidence. The text also discusses various scenarios: whether the deceased and people are inside the mosque, or some are outside. It concludes that the disliked ruling applies in most cases, except when all (bier, imam, and people) are outside the mosque. A supplementary note adds that funeral prayer is also disliked in the street or on private property.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيهية (karāhah tanzīhiyyah): A slight dislike that does not entail sin, opposite of tahrimi.
العلة (al-ʿillah): The underlying reason for the ruling: either fear of impurity or occupying mosque for non-designated purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible (mubah) without dislike.
B) Disliked (makruh).
C) Forbidden (haram).
D) Recommended (mandub).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi relied-upon ruling is that funeral prayer in a mosque is disliked (makruh), with the degree of dislike depending on the underlying cause.

Rulings for a Newborn Who Cries and a Stillborn
Distinguishes between a child who cries at birth and a stillborn regarding washing and prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a newborn who cries (mustahill) and a stillborn (saqt), explain the condition of istihlal (crying), and apply the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
A child who cries at birth is prayed over; if not, he is washed but not prayed over — crying (istihlal) is the decisive sign of life.

This passage from Nur al-Idah draws a clear distinction between two scenarios at birth: a child who cries and one who does not. The ruling hinges on the presence of a sign of life (istihlal), and even a stillborn (saqt) is washed but not prayed over. Understanding this distinction is essential for performing the correct funeral rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage first gives the ruling for the crying newborn (mustahill) and then for the non-crier (lam yastahill).
2
Determine the condition for prayer
Observing which sign (crying) triggers the obligation of funeral prayer.
3
Trace the evidence
Find the hadith cited (from Jabir) that explicitly conditions prayer on istihlal.
The hadith is marfu' and recorded by al-Tirmidhi.
4
Note the scope
Understand that the ruling applies when most of the body has emerged, and the criterion is the chest or navel depending on birth position.
5
Apply to a stillborn
A miscarriage (saqt) that has not completed its creation is treated similarly: washed, wrapped, buried, no prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن استهل سُمِّي، وغُسل، وصلي عليه، وإن لم يُسْتَهَلْ غُسل في المختار، وأُدرج في خِرْقَةٍ، ودُفِنَ، ولم يُصَلِّ عليه. والعبرة بالصدر إن نزل برأسه مستقيماً، وبسرته إن نزل برجليه منكوساً، فإذا وجد ذلك وقد خرج أكثره سُمِّي، وغُسل وكفن كما علمته وصلي عليه، لما ذكر عن جابر يرفعه ( الطِّفْلُ لا يُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ، وَلا يَرثُ، وَلا يُوَرَّثُ حَتَّى يَسْتَهلَّ ) أخرجه الترمذي، كذا في «الفتح». وفي « البدائع » : لا تقبل الشهادة في الاستهلال إلا من رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين عند الإمام، وقالا : يقبل قول النساء فيه إلا الأم، فلا يقبل قولها في الميراث إجماعاً لجرها المغنم إليها، وإنما يقبل لأن ذلك لا يشهده الرجال، وقول القابلة مقبول في حق الصلاة عليه، وأمه كالقابلة إذا اتصفت بالعدالة، وفي الظهيرية » : ماتت و اضطرب الولد في بطنها تشق ويخرج لا يسع إلا ذلك، كذا في «شرح المقدسي » ( وإن لم يَسْتَهِلْ غُسل في المختار) لأنه نفس من وجه، (وأُدرج في خرقة) وسمي ( ودفن، ولم يُصَلَّ عليه)، وكذا يغسل السقط الذي لم يتم خلقه في المختار، ويـلــف فـي خـرقـة كـمـا في شرح المقدسي
And whoever cries (at birth) is named, washed, and prayed over. And if he does not cry, he is washed in the chosen view, wrapped in a cloth, buried, and not prayed over. The criterion is the chest if he is born headfirst, and the navel if born feet first. If that (i.e., crying) occurs and most of his body has emerged, he is named, washed, enshrouded as you know, and prayed over, because of what is narrated from Jabir in marfu' form: 'The child is not prayed over, does not inherit, and is not inherited from until he cries.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi, as in al-Fath. And in al-Bada'i': Testimony regarding the crying is not accepted except from two men or a man and two women according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: the testimony of women is accepted except the mother, as her testimony regarding inheritance is not accepted by consensus due to her benefiting from it. It is only accepted because men do not witness this. The statement of the midwife is accepted regarding the prayer over him, and his mother is like the midwife if she is just. In al-Zahiriyya: if the mother dies and the child stirs in her womb, the belly is split and the child is removed; there is no alternative but that. As in Sharh al-Maqdisi. (And if he does not cry, he is washed in the chosen view) because he is a soul in some respect, (and wrapped in a cloth) and named, (and buried, and not prayed over). Similarly, a miscarriage (saqt) that has not completed its creation is washed in the chosen view, and wrapped in a cloth as in Sharh al-Maqdisi.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage gives the rulings for a newborn who cries (mustahill) and one who does not (lam yastahill). If the child cries upon birth (indicating life), he is given a name, given the ritual bath (ghusl), enshrouded, and the funeral prayer is performed over him. The condition is that the majority of his body must have emerged. If he does not cry, he is still given a ritual bath and wrapped in a cloth, but no funeral prayer is performed. The same ruling applies to a stillborn (saqt) that has not completed its creation. The proof is the hadith of Jabir that a child is not prayed over until he cries. The passage also discusses issues of testimony regarding the crying: according to Abu Hanifa, only two men or a man and two women can testify; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, women's testimony is accepted except the mother's. The midwife's testimony is accepted for the purpose of prayer.

Key Terms
اسْتَهَلَّ (istahalla): To cry at birth, raising the voice; a sign of life.
سَقْط (saqt): A fetus that is born dead before completing its creation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling for a child who does not cry at birth (lam yastahill)?
A) He is neither washed nor prayed over.
B) He is washed but not prayed over.
C) He is prayed over but not washed.
D) He is washed and prayed over.

Key Takeaway
A sign of life (crying) at birth determines whether funeral prayer is performed; without it, the newborn is washed but not prayed over.

The Dislike of Janazah Prayer in the Mosque: Hanafi Ruling and Its Proofs
Ruling on karaha of janazah prayer in the mosque with citation of Aisha's hadith and tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on janazah prayer inside the mosque using the relied-upon (mukhtar) view and identify the proof and the exception.

Core Idea
The Hanafi opinion that janazah prayer inside a mosque is disliked (makruh tanzih) is the chosen view, despite the precedent of Abu Bakr's prayer.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the Hanafi stance on performing the funeral prayer within a mosque. While some earlier reports suggest permissibility, the later preferred view (mukhtar) maintains karaha (dislike) in most scenarios. We will examine the evidence, the exceptions, and the reasoning behind the tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm level (fard, wajib, sunnah, makruh, etc.) according to the Hanafi school?
The act is performing salat al-janazah inside a mosque.
2
Locate the proof cited
The author cites a hadith from Aisha about Abu Bakr's funeral. Identify the text and consider how it is used as evidence.
The hadith suggests permissibility, but Hanafis do not take it as overriding.
3
Understand the scope and exceptions
The ruling applies in several scenarios. List the scenarios mentioned and note any exception (e.g., al-Nasafi's view).
The mukhtar is karaha in all but one scenario where al-Nasafi said it is not disliked by agreement.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Why is the chosen view (mukhtar) karaha despite the hadith? What is the response to al-Nasafi?
The later authorities (al-Kamal, al-Fatawa al-Sughra) preferred karaha as a precaution.

Or outside it, and some people in the mosque, according to the chosen view. And whoever cries (at birth) is named, washed, and prayed upon, and if he does not cry, he is washed according to the chosen view, wrapped in a cloth, buried, and not prayed upon. And Aisha said: 'Abu Bakr left no dinar nor dirham, and he was buried on Tuesday night and the funeral prayer was performed over him in the mosque.' End. So it is disliked whether the deceased and the people are in the mosque, (or) the deceased is (outside) i.e. the mosque with some of the people, (and) (some people are in the mosque), or the deceased is in the mosque and the people and the imam are outside the mosque, or the deceased is in the mosque with some of the people and the rest are outside. This (according to) what is in 'Al-Fatawa al-Sughra', he said: it is the (chosen view) contrary to what al-Nasafi mentioned, may Allah have mercy on him. Thus said al-Kamal. And what al-Nasafi mentioned is what he said in 'Al-Inayah': 'If the bier, the imam, and some of the people are outside the mosque and the rest inside, it is not disliked by agreement.' End. And regarding the dislike in 'Al-Jami' al-Saghir', there is disagreement when some of the people are outside the mosque. Thus in 'Al-Bazzaziyyah'. And you have known that the chosen view is dislike. [Note]: The funeral prayer in the street and people's lands is disliked, as in 'Al-Tatarkhaniyyah'.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on performing the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) inside a mosque. The author establishes that the relied-upon (mukhtar) position is that it is makruh (disliked) to pray over the deceased inside the mosque. This ruling applies in various scenarios: whether the deceased and all the people are inside the mosque, or the deceased is outside and some people inside, etc. The author cites the narration of Aisha that Abu Bakr was prayed upon in the mosque, which indicates permissibility according to some, but the preferred view remains karaha. The author also notes a disagreement with al-Nasafi, who held that if the bier and imam are outside and only some people inside, it is not disliked. The final sentence adds that praying in the street or on people's land is also disliked, according to al-Tatarkhaniyyah.

Key Terms
المختار (al-mukhtar): The relied-upon or preferred ruling in the Hanafi school, often chosen from among differing views.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible without dislike
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (mustahabb)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi relied-upon view is that janazah prayer inside a mosque is makruh tanzih, based on the chosen view (mukhtar) from later fatwa authorities, despite the narration of Aisha.

The Newborn's Crying (Istihlal) and Its Legal Effects
Rulings on mustahill and stillborn child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for funeral prayer and inheritance for a newborn, identify the difference between a mustahill and stillborn, and apply the Hanafi ruling on testimony regarding istihlal.

Core Idea
A child must show signs of life (istihlal) to be prayed upon and inherit; stillborns are washed and buried without prayer.

This lesson covers the Hanafi rulings for newborn children at birth. The key distinction is whether the child cries or shows any sign of life (istihlal). The hadith from Jabir establishes that without istihlal, no funeral prayer or inheritance applies. We also explore an intra-Hanafi dispute about whose testimony is accepted regarding the crying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the birth of a child. The ruling depends on whether the child shows signs of life (istihlal) after most of the body emerges.
Mustahill: named, washed, shrouded, prayed upon. Stillborn: washed, wrapped, buried, no prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Jabir: 'The child is not prayed upon, does not inherit, nor is inherited from until he cries.'
Sunan al-Tirmidhi.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly mentions crying (istihlal) as the condition for prayer and inheritance. The absence of crying negates these rulings.
The condition is met by any sign of life, not only crying.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on testimony
Imam Abu Hanifa requires two men or one man and two women. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept women's testimony except the mother for inheritance.
The practical effect: under the Sahibayn, prayer can be performed with women's testimony.

(And whoever) meaning a fetus (cries) his crying is raising his voice in weeping at birth. The origin of the term is raising voices upon sighting the crescent. Mentioned in al-Idah: it is that from him appears something indicating life, such as crying, moving a limb, or moving the edge of the eye. What is considered is the presence of that at the emergence of most of him, as in al-Mubtagha. If his head emerges and he cries, then dies before emerging, he does not inherit nor is he prayed upon unless most of his body emerges alive. End. The criterion is the chest if he comes head first, and the navel if he comes feet first. So if that is found and most of him has emerged, he is named, washed, shrouded as known, and prayed upon, due to what was narrated from Jabir raising it (the hadith): 'The child is not prayed upon, does not inherit, nor is inherited from until he cries.' Recorded by al-Tirmidhi. Thus in al-Fath. And in al-Bada'i: Testimony regarding the crying is not accepted except from two men or one man and two women according to Imam Abu Hanifa. But the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the statement of women is accepted regarding it, except the mother, for her statement is not accepted regarding inheritance by consensus because she draws benefit to herself; it is only accepted because men do not witness that. The statement of the midwife is accepted regarding praying upon him, and his mother is like the midwife if she is just. In al-Zahiriyyah: If the woman dies and the child stirs in her womb, she is cut open and the child is taken out; nothing else suffices. Thus in Sharh al-Maqdisi. (And if he does not cry, he is washed according to the chosen view) because he is a soul in one respect, (and wrapped in a cloth) and named (and buried, and not prayed upon). Likewise, a stillborn whose creation is not completed is washed according to the chosen view, and wrapped in a cloth, like a captive child with one of his parents, unless one of them becomes Muslim, or he (the child) becomes Muslim, or one of them was not captured with him. His tongue expresses him. From al-Fath and al-Dirayah - contrary to what al-Karkhi adopted, which is the apparent of the riwayah. And he is named as al-Tahawi mentioned from Abu Yusuf, thus in al-Tabyin. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If part of his creation appears, he will be resurrected; similar in al-Mabsut. And another opinion is mentioned: if the soul is breathed into him, he is resurrected, otherwise not, thus in Sharh al-Maqdisi. (Like a captive child) i.e. taken captive (with one of his parents) from dar al-harb, then dies, because he follows him, due to his saying: 'Every child is born upon the fitrah, then his parents make him a Jew, Christian, or Magian.' So that he is either grateful or ungrateful. Unless one of them becomes Muslim, then the child dies, because he follows the better of them in religion, so he is prayed upon. Or he (the child who understands) becomes Muslim, because his Islam is valid according to us by istihsan, and it is that he affirms the message and oneness, and if the description of faith and its obligations are mentioned to him, and he is asked: 'Do you believe in this?' and he says: 'Yes', that is sufficient, just as it suffices from a sane adult. The condition is not that he describes that from the beginning of himself, since only the elite know it. Or one of his parents (i.e., either father or mother) was not captured with him (the child), because his following to dar al-Islam becomes apparent, so he is ruled to be Muslim like a foundling due to the severance of parental following due to difference of abode. Al-Kamal said: There is disagreement regarding the basis of following: birth-based following (i.e., following one parent) - what is in al-Hidayah is following the dar. And in al-Muhit: If neither parent is with him, he follows the possessor of the hand, and in absence of a possessor, he follows the dar, and perhaps this is more appropriate. For whoever receives a child in his share of booty in dar al-harb and he dies, he is prayed upon and considered Muslim following the possessor of the hand. End. They mentioned that booty is not divided in dar al-harb, based on the fact that ownership is not established before bringing it to our dar, unless it is said that the basis of ownership suffices for placing the hand on what is permissible in dar al-harb. End. And in Kashf al-Asrar: If a dhimmi steals a child and takes him out to dar al-Islam, then the child dies, he is prayed upon and becomes Muslim by following the dar, and the taking is not considered such that it necessitates rescuing him from his hand. End. I say: Perhaps the meaning is rescuing him by paying his value, just as if he became Muslim or a Muslim bought him, he is forced to release him from his ownership in exchange for a substitute. End. And the author of al-Bahr said: He did not report any disagreement on it, and this (ruling) comes contrary to what is in al-Muhit, for its implication is that he should not be prayed upon, giving precedence to following of the hand over the dar, unless it is about the disagreement. The ruling of an insane adult in these matters is like that of a sane child, so there are three aspects of following, as the usuliyyun have stated. End.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage deals with detailed rulings for two categories: (1) the newborn child who cries at birth (mustahill) – he is named, washed, shrouded, and prayed over; (2) the stillborn child (sqt) or child who does not cry – he is washed, shrouded, and buried but not prayed over. The author cites the hadith from Jabir that the child is not prayed upon until he cries. There is also an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding testimony for the crying: Imam Abu Hanifa requires two men or one man and two women, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept women's testimony except the mother's concerning inheritance. The passage then discusses the religious status of a child captured with one parent from dar al-harb. The child follows the better religion: if either parent becomes Muslim, the child is considered Muslim and is prayed upon. If the child himself understands and accepts Islam, it is valid by istihsan. If neither parent is captured with him, he follows the dar (abode of Islam) and is ruled Muslim like a foundling. There is further discussion on following the possessor of the hand versus the dar, with the author favoring the dar in the absence of a possessor. Finally, the insane adult is likened to a child in these rulings.

Key Terms
استهلال (istihlal): The crying or any sign of life from a newborn child at birth, such as weeping, moving a limb, or blinking.
سقط (sqt): A fetus that is miscarried before completion of creation, stillborn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, under which condition is a newborn child prayed upon (salat al-janazah) and inherits?
A) When the child is born alive even without crying
B) When the child cries or shows signs of life at birth (istihlal)
C) When the child is a full-term delivery
D) When the mother was Muslim

Key Takeaway
A newborn must show signs of life (istihlal) to receive funeral prayer and inheritance; a stillborn is washed and buried without prayer.

Religious Status of the Captive Child: Parent, Abode, or Possessor?
Captive child's religious status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the religious status of a child captured in war, identify the three bases of following (tabaiyya), and apply the Hanafi rules to different scenarios.

Core Idea
A captive child's religion follows the parent, the dar, or the possessor, with the child's own Islam valid by istihsan.

This lesson deals with the rulings for children captured from dar al-harb. The general principle is that a child follows his parents in religion, but there are exceptions: if a parent becomes Muslim, if the child himself accepts Islam, or if the child is captured alone. There is also an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the child follows the dar (abode) or the possessor of the hand (the one who captured him).

Guided Path
1
State the basic rule
A child captured with a parent follows that parent in religion. The hadith 'Every child is born upon the fitrah...' is the evidence.
The child is legally attached to the parent until he can choose.
2
Identify the exceptions
Three exceptions: (1) one parent becomes Muslim – child follows the better religion; (2) child himself accepts Islam – valid by istihsan; (3) child captured alone – follows dar al-Islam.
In exception 3, there is ikhtilaf on whether he follows dar or possessor.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf on following
Al-Hidayah says follow the dar; al-Muhit says follow the possessor of the hand; the author prefers the dar.
The dispute affects whether a child captured by a non-Muslim is considered Muslim.
4
Apply to scenarios
Given a concrete scenario, determine the child's status: Muslim or non-Muslim? Then decide if funeral prayer is performed.
Consider parent's religion, child's own acceptance, and abode.

(ومن) بمعنى جنين (اسْتَهَل) استهلاله بأن يرفع صوته بالبكاء عند الولادة، والأصــل فـيـه رفــع الأصوات عند رؤية الهلال، وذكر في الإيضاح هو أن يكون منه ما يدل على حياته من بكاء، أو تحريك عضو أو طرف عين، والمعتبر وجود ذلك عند خروج أكثره، كما في «المبتغى» بالمعجمة، ولـو خــرج رأسه وهو يصيح فمات قبل أن يخرج، لم يرث ولم يصل عليه ما لم يخرج أكثر بـدنـه حـيـاً انتهى، والعبرة بالصدر إن نزل برأسه مستقيماً، الميراث إجماعاً لجرها المغنم إليها، وإنما يقبل لأن ذلك لا يشهده الرجال، وقول القابلة مقبول في حق الصلاة عليه، وأمه كالقابلة إذا اتصفت بالعدالة، وفي الظهيرية » : ماتت و اضطرب الولد في بطنها تشق ويخرج
