فـي خـرقـة كـمـا كصبي سبي مع أحد أبويه، إلا أنْ يُسْلِمَ أحدهما، أو هو أو لم يُسْبَ أحدهما معه. لسانه يعرب عنه «الفتح»، و « الدراية». خلافاً لما أخذ به الكرخي، وهو «ظاهر الروايــة» ويسمى، كمـا ذكــره الطحاوي» عن «أبي يوسف » ، كذا في ( التبيين » ، وفي ( الظهيرية » إذا بان بعض خلقه يحشر، ومثله في « المبسوط » ، وذكر قولاً آخر: إن نفخ فيه الروح حشر، وإلا فلا، كذا في «شرح المقدسي » ، ( كصَبِي سُبِي) أي: أسر (معَ أحد أبويه) من دار الحرب ثـم مـات لأنـه تبـع لـه، لقوله : « كُلُّ مَوْلُودٍ يُولَدُ عَلَى الْفِطْرَةِ، فَأَبَوَاهُ يُهَوِّدَانِهِ، أَوْ يُنَصِّرَانِهِ، أَوْ يُمَجِّسَانِهِ » (4) حتى يكون إما شاكراً و إما كفوراً، إلا أنْ يُسْلِمَ أحدهما ) ثـم يـمـوت الـصـبي، لأنه يتبـع خيرهما ديناً فيصلى عليه، (أو) يسلم ( هو ) أي: الصبي الذي يعقل، لأن إسلامه صحيح عندنــا استحساناً، و ، وهو أن يقرّ بالرسالة والوحدانية، وإذا ذكر له صفة الإيمان وما يوجبه، وقيل له: هل أنت مصدق بهذا؟ فقال: نعم، كان ذلك كافياً، كما يكتفي بـه مـن العـاقـل البـالـغ، ولـيـس الشـرط وصفه ذلك من ابتداء نفسه، إذ لا يعرفه إلا الخواص (أو لم يُسْبَ أحدهما ) أي: أحد أبويه (معه) أي: الصبي لظهور تبعيته لدار الإسلام، فحكم بإسلامه كاللقيط لانقطاع تبعية الأبوين، باختلاف الدار، قال الكمال: اختلف بعد تبعية الولادة أي بعد تبعية أحد الأبوين فالذي في الهداية» تبعية الدار. وفي المحيط » : إذا لم يكن معه أحد أبويه يكون تبعاً لصاحب اليد، وعند عدم صاحب اليد يكون تبعاً للدار ولعله أولى، فإن من وقع في سهمه صـبـي مـن الغنيمة في دار الحرب فمات يصلي عليه، ويجعل مسلماً تبعاً لصاحب اليد انتهى، وقد ذكروا في الغنيمة أنها لا تقسم بدار الحرب، بناء على أنَّ الملك لا يثبت فيها قبل الإحراز بدارنا، إلا أن يقال: أصل الملك كاف لوضع اليد على ما هو مباح بدار الحرب انتهى ، وفي كشف الأسرار»: لو سرق ذمي صبياً وأخرجه إلى دار الإسلام فمات الصبي، فإنه يصلى عليه ويصير مسلماً بتبعـيـة الـدار، ولا يعتبر الأخذ حتى وجب تخليصه من يده انتهى، قلت: ولعل المراد تخليصه بقيمته، كمـا لـو أسلم أو اشتراه مسلماً اً يجبر على إخراجه عن ملكه ببدله .انتهى وقال صاحب « البحر » : ولم يحـك فـيـه خلافاً، وهي واردة على ما في ( المحيط » ، فإن مقتضاه أن لا يصلى عليه تقديماً لتبعـيـة الـيـد عـلـى الـدار، إلا أن يكون على الخلاف، وحكم المجنون البالغ في هذه الأحكام كحكم الصبي العاقل، فيكون فيه الأوجه الثلاثة في التبعية ، كما صرح به الأصوليون انتهى.
(And whoever) meaning a fetus (cries) his crying is raising his voice in weeping at birth. The origin of the term is raising voices upon sighting the crescent. Mentioned in al-Idah: it is that from him appears something indicating life, such as crying, moving a limb, or moving the edge of the eye. What is considered is the presence of that at the emergence of most of him, as in al-Mubtagha. If his head emerges and he cries, then dies before emerging, he does not inherit nor is he prayed upon unless most of his body emerges alive. End. The criterion is the chest if he comes head first, and the navel if he comes feet first. So if that is found and most of him has emerged, he is named, washed, shrouded as known, and prayed upon, due to what was narrated from Jabir raising it (the hadith): 'The child is not prayed upon, does not inherit, nor is inherited from until he cries.' Recorded by al-Tirmidhi. Thus in al-Fath. And in al-Bada'i: Testimony regarding the crying is not accepted except from two men or one man and two women according to Imam Abu Hanifa. But the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the statement of women is accepted regarding it, except the mother, for her statement is not accepted regarding inheritance by consensus because she draws benefit to herself; it is only accepted because men do not witness that. The statement of the midwife is accepted regarding praying upon him, and his mother is like the midwife if she is just. In al-Zahiriyyah: If the woman dies and the child stirs in her womb, she is cut open and the child is taken out; nothing else suffices. Thus in Sharh al-Maqdisi. (And if he does not cry, he is washed according to the chosen view) because he is a soul in one respect, (and wrapped in a cloth) and named (and buried, and not prayed upon). Likewise, a stillborn whose creation is not completed is washed according to the chosen view, and wrapped in a cloth, like a captive child with one of his parents, unless one of them becomes Muslim, or he (the child) becomes Muslim, or one of them was not captured with him. His tongue expresses him. From al-Fath and al-Dirayah - contrary to what al-Karkhi adopted, which is the apparent of the riwayah. And he is named as al-Tahawi mentioned from Abu Yusuf, thus in al-Tabyin. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If part of his creation appears, he will be resurrected; similar in al-Mabsut. And another opinion is mentioned: if the soul is breathed into him, he is resurrected, otherwise not, thus in Sharh al-Maqdisi. (Like a captive child) i.e. taken captive (with one of his parents) from dar al-harb, then dies, because he follows him, due to his saying: 'Every child is born upon the fitrah, then his parents make him a Jew, Christian, or Magian.' So that he is either grateful or ungrateful. Unless one of them becomes Muslim, then the child dies, because he follows the better of them in religion, so he is prayed upon. Or he (the child who understands) becomes Muslim, because his Islam is valid according to us by istihsan, and it is that he affirms the message and oneness, and if the description of faith and its obligations are mentioned to him, and he is asked: 'Do you believe in this?' and he says: 'Yes', that is sufficient, just as it suffices from a sane adult. The condition is not that he describes that from the beginning of himself, since only the elite know it. Or one of his parents (i.e., either father or mother) was not captured with him (the child), because his following to dar al-Islam becomes apparent, so he is ruled to be Muslim like a foundling due to the severance of parental following due to difference of abode. Al-Kamal said: There is disagreement regarding the basis of following: birth-based following (i.e., following one parent) - what is in al-Hidayah is following the dar. And in al-Muhit: If neither parent is with him, he follows the possessor of the hand, and in absence of a possessor, he follows the dar, and perhaps this is more appropriate. For whoever receives a child in his share of booty in dar al-harb and he dies, he is prayed upon and considered Muslim following the possessor of the hand. End. They mentioned that booty is not divided in dar al-harb, based on the fact that ownership is not established before bringing it to our dar, unless it is said that the basis of ownership suffices for placing the hand on what is permissible in dar al-harb. End. And in Kashf al-Asrar: If a dhimmi steals a child and takes him out to dar al-Islam, then the child dies, he is prayed upon and becomes Muslim by following the dar, and the taking is not considered such that it necessitates rescuing him from his hand. End. I say: Perhaps the meaning is rescuing him by paying his value, just as if he became Muslim or a Muslim bought him, he is forced to release him from his ownership in exchange for a substitute. End. And the author of al-Bahr said: He did not report any disagreement on it, and this (ruling) comes contrary to what is in al-Muhit, for its implication is that he should not be prayed upon, giving precedence to following of the hand over the dar, unless it is about the disagreement. The ruling of an insane adult in these matters is like that of a sane child, so there are three aspects of following, as the usuliyyun have stated. End.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage deals with detailed rulings for two categories: (1) the newborn child who cries at birth (mustahill) – he is named, washed, shrouded, and prayed over; (2) the stillborn child (sqt) or child who does not cry – he is washed, shrouded, and buried but not prayed over. The author cites the hadith from Jabir that the child is not prayed upon until he cries. There is also an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding testimony for the crying: Imam Abu Hanifa requires two men or one man and two women, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept women's testimony except the mother's concerning inheritance. The passage then discusses the religious status of a child captured with one parent from dar al-harb. The child follows the better religion: if either parent becomes Muslim, the child is considered Muslim and is prayed upon. If the child himself understands and accepts Islam, it is valid by istihsan. If neither parent is captured with him, he follows the dar (abode of Islam) and is ruled Muslim like a foundling. There is further discussion on following the possessor of the hand versus the dar, with the author favoring the dar in the absence of a possessor. Finally, the insane adult is likened to a child in these rulings.

Key Terms
تبعية (tabaiyya): Legal following: the child follows the parent in religion, or follows the abode (dar) or possessor of the hand in captivity.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory not under Islamic rule, where war may be permissible.
دار الإسلام (dar al-Islam): Territory under Islamic rule where Islamic law is applied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A child is captured without his parents from dar al-harb and brought to dar al-Islam by a non-Muslim soldier. According to the preferred Hanafi view, what is the child's religious status?
A) Non-Muslim, following the captor
B) Muslim, following dar al-Islam
C) Muslim only if he accepts Islam
D) Non-Muslim because no parent

Key Takeaway
A captive child's religion follows the dar of Islam when captured alone; otherwise, it follows the parent unless the parent or child accepts Islam.

Ruling on Janazah for a Captive Child with One Muslim Parent
Explains Hanafi ruling on janazah for a captive child based on parental Islam or dar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which a captive child is ruled Muslim for janazah and identify the Hanafi proofs from the hadith and istihsan.

Core Idea
A captive child is presumed Muslim by fitrah; janazah is performed if one parent is Muslim, the child converts, or he is captured alone.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies a nuanced Hanafi ruling: when a child is taken captive from dar al-harb and dies, should we perform janazah? The answer depends on the child's religious status, which is determined by dependency on parents, personal conversion, or the dar. The Hanafi school, based on the hadith of fitrah, gives the child the benefit of Islamic status in several scenarios. This lesson unpacks those conditions and the intra-madhhab discussion about whether to prioritize the captor's hand or the dar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the janazah prayer for a captive child who died. The ruling is that it is performed (fard kifayah) if the child is ruled Muslim.
Janazah is only valid for a Muslim; determining the child's religion is key.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position: a captive child is considered Muslim in three cases: (1) one parent becomes Muslim, (2) the child personally embraces Islam (if discerning), or (3) the child is captured alone (without parents), relying on dar al-Islam.
This is based on the hadith 'Every child is born on fitrah'—parents alter it.
3
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'كل مولود يولد على الفطرة فأبواه يهودانه أو ينصرانه أو يمجسانه' (Bukhari, Muslim). This indicates the child's original state is Islam, and parents are the ones who change it.
Thubut: zanni (ahad), dalala: zanni, but combined with istihsan it is relied upon.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
There is a difference among Hanafis: some (like al-Karkhi) follow the owner's hand (i.e., if a Muslim captor holds the child, he is Muslim). Others, preferred by al-Kamal and the author of al-Bahr, give precedence to the dar (i.e., if the child is in dar al-Islam, he is Muslim).
The mufta bihi is to follow dependency on dar, as that is more consistently applied.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The practical outcome (thamarah): if the child dies, janazah is performed in all three cases. This differs from other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) who require both parents to be Muslim or the child to personally convert.
The Hanafi view is more inclusive, reflecting the principle of taba'iyya.

لظهور تبعيته لدار الإسلام فحكم بإسلامه كاللقيط لانقطاع تبعية الأبوين باختلاف الدار قال الكمال: اختلف بعد تبعية الولادة أي بعد تبعية أحد الأبوين فالذي في الهداية» تبعية الدار وفي المحيط » : إذا لم يكن الغنيمة أنها لا تقسم بدار الحرب بناء على أنَّ الملك لا يثبت فيها قبل الإحراز بدارنا إلا أن يقال: أصل الملك كاف لوضع اليد على ما هو مباح بدار الحرب انتهى وفي كشف الأسرار»: لو سرق ذمي صبياً وأخرجه إلى دار الإسلام فمات الصبي فإنه يصلى عليه ويصير مسلماً بتبعـيـة الـدار ولا يعتبر الأخذ حتى وجب تخليصه من يده انتهى قلت: ولعل المراد تخليصه بقيمته كمـا لـو أسلم أو اشتراه مسلماً اً يجبر على إخراجه عن ملكه ببدله .انتهى وقال صاحب « البحر » : ولم يحـك فـيـه خلافاً وهي واردة على ما في ( المحيط » فإن مقتضاه أن لا يصلى عليه تقديماً لتبعـيـة الـيـد عـلـى الدار إلا أن يكون على الخلاف وحكم المجنون البالغ في هذه الأحكام كحكم الصبي العاقل فيكون فيه الأوجه الثلاثة في التبعية كما صرح به الأصوليون انتهى. (1) أخرجه البخاري في التفسير باب قوله تعالى: ﴿ لا تَبْدِيلَ لِخَلْقِ اللهِ ﴾ (٤٧٧٥) ومسلم في القدر باب: معنى كل مولود يولد على الفطرة (٢٦٥٨).
Like a child captured with one of his parents, except if one of them becomes Muslim, or he (the child) becomes Muslim, or neither of them was captured with him. His tongue expresses it. Al-Fath and al-Diraya. Contrary to what al-Karkhi adopted, and it is Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is called, as al-Tahawi mentioned from Abu Yusuf, as in al-Tabyin, and in al-Dhahiriyyah: when some of his creation becomes apparent he is gathered, and similar in al-Mabsut, and another saying is mentioned: if the spirit was blown into him he is gathered, otherwise not, as in Sharh al-Maqdisi. (He said: "Like a child captured") i.e., taken captive (with one of his parents) from dar al-harb then dies, because he follows him, due to his statement: "Every child is born upon the fitrah, then his parents make him a Jew, Christian, or Magian" (1) so that he becomes either grateful or ungrateful. Except if one of them becomes Muslim, then the child dies, because he follows the better of them in religion, so prayer is performed over him. (Or) he (the child) becomes Muslim, i.e., the discerning child, because his Islam is valid by istihsan with us, and that he affirms the message and oneness, and when the description of faith and its obligations are mentioned to him, and it is said to him: Are you believing in this? and he says: Yes, that is sufficient, just as it is sufficient from the rational adult. The condition is not that he describes that from his own beginning, since only the elite know it. (Or neither of them was captured) i.e., one of his parents (with him) i.e., the child, due to the apparentness of his dependency on dar al-Islam, so he is ruled to be Muslim like a foundling, due to the severance of parental dependency by difference of dar. Al-Kamal said: There is disagreement after birth dependency, i.e., after dependency on one parent. What is in al-Hidayah: dependency on dar. In al-Muhit: If neither parent is with him, he is dependent on the owner of the hand. In the absence of the owner of the hand, he is dependent on the dar, and perhaps it is more appropriate. For whoever receives a child from the spoils in dar al-harb and he dies, prayer is performed over him and he is considered Muslim by dependency on the owner of the hand. They mentioned concerning spoils that it is not divided in dar al-harb, based on the fact that ownership does not take effect there before bringing it to our dar, unless it is said: the basis of ownership is sufficient for placing the hand on what is permissible in dar al-harb. In Kashf al-Asrar: If a dhimmi steals a child and takes him to dar al-Islam and the child dies, then prayer is performed over him and he becomes Muslim by dependency on the dar, and the taking is not considered, until it is obligatory to rescue him from his hand. I say: Perhaps the meaning is to rescue him with his value, just as if he becomes Muslim or a Muslim buys him, he is compelled to release him from his ownership with compensation. The author of al-Bahr said: No disagreement is reported in it, and it is contrary to what is in al-Muhit, for its requirement is that prayer not be performed over him, giving precedence to dependency on the hand over the dar, unless it is based on disagreement. The ruling of an insane adult in these rulings is like the discerning child, so it has the three aspects of dependency, as the usuliyyun stated. (1) Bukhari in Tafsir, chapter of verse: "No change to the creation of Allah" (4775), and Muslim in Qadr, chapter of meaning of every child born on the fitrah (2658).
Source pages p. 593

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah comments on a ruling from Nur al-Idah regarding the janazah prayer for a child captured from dar al-harb. The key principle is that a captive child's legal status (Muslim or kafir) depends on parental religion or personal Islam. The Hanafi position, based on the hadith that every child is born on fitrah, holds that a child follows the better religion of his parents. If one parent is Muslim, the child is considered Muslim, and janazah is performed. If the child himself becomes Muslim (by declaration of faith, even if young but rational), that also suffices by istihsan. If the child is captured alone (without parents), he is considered Muslim by dependency on dar al-Islam, like a foundling. The passage discusses intra-Hanafi differences: some give weight to the owner's hand (if a Muslim captor), others to the dar. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is to consider the child Muslim in all these cases. The hadith is cited as proof, and the analysis emphasizes that the child's fitrah is not overwritten by kufr until adolescence.

Key Terms
سبي (sabī): A child taken captive from dar al-harb; legal status depends on parental or personal Islam.
تبعية (taba'iyya): Legal dependency that determines the child's religion (on parent, owner, or dar).
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference that allows a departure from strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling; here, accepting a child's Islam without full maturity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a captive child dies with one Muslim parent, what is the ruling on janazah according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Janazah is not performed because the child may be kafir.
B) Janazah is performed because the child follows the better religion (Islam) of that parent.
C) Janazah is only performed if the child was born in dar al-Islam.
D) Janazah depends on whether the child was captured with both parents.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a captive child is presumed Muslim due to fitrah, and janazah is performed if one parent is Muslim, the child converts, or he is captured alone.

Washing and Burying a Non-Muslim Relative
Ruling on washing a non-Muslim relative with detailed conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Muslim must wash a non-Muslim relative and explain why the washing is treated differently from a Muslim's.

Core Idea
A non‑Muslim relative is washed like a filthy rag, not for purification but as a general sunnah for humanity.

This lesson addresses a practical question: what should a Muslim do when a non‑Muslim relative dies? The Hanafi school provides a detailed answer, balancing respect for kinship with the reality of the deceased’s kufr. The ruling depends on whether other non‑Muslim relatives exist and emphasises that the washing is a mere physical cleaning, not a spiritual purification. We will unpack the conditions, the method, and the evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Determine when a Muslim must handle the funeral of a kāfir relative. The text states: if the deceased has no kāfir relatives, the Muslim washes, shrouds, and buries him minimally. If kāfir relatives exist, the Muslim should hand over the body to them.
This is a conditional obligation (wājib kifāyah) on the Muslim community only when no kāfir is available.
2
Understand the nature of the washing
The washing is compared to cleaning a filthy rag (ghasl khirqah naĥisah). It is not a ritual purification (ṭahārah) but a mere removal of filth. Therefore, the water becomes impure, unlike the water used for washing a Muslim.
The purpose is not to honour the deceased but to fulfil a general sunnah and to serve as a proof against him on the Day of Judgement.
3
Analyse the ḥadīth proof
The story of the Jew and his son shows that when the son converted, the Prophet ﷺ took charge of his funeral, preventing the Jewish father from doing so. This indicates that Muslims are responsible for a deceased Muslim even if his relative is a kāfir.
The ḥadīth is cited to support that if a kāfir has no kāfir relatives, Muslims must take over.
4
Distinguish between Muslim and kāfir funeral rites
A Muslim is washed with the sunnah, shrouded properly, and buried in a laḥd. A kāfir is washed without sunnah, shrouded in any rag, and thrown into a pit without niche. The difference arises from the absence of īmān.
The Muslim who handles the kāfir’s body is not rendered impure, but the water used for washing becomes najis.
5
Note the exception for apostates
An apostate (murtadd) is treated even worse: he is not washed at all but thrown into a pit like a dog. This is because an apostate has no religion and is not to be handled with any respect.
The passage explicitly excludes apostates from the ruling on original kuffār.

Source Text

If a kafir has a Muslim relative, the Muslim washes him, like washing a filthy rag, and shrouds him in a rag, and throws him into a pit. Note: The followership of one of the parents is only in worldly rulings, not in the afterlife, so it is not ruled that the children of kafirs are in the Fire; rather there is difference of opinion. It is said: they are servants of the people of Paradise, and it is said: if they said 'Yes' on the day of the covenant of belief, then in Paradise, otherwise in the Fire. And from Muhammad that he said concerning them: I know that Allah does not punish anyone without sin, and this negates this detail. And Imam Abu Hanifa held back from opining on them, as in al-Fath. (And if a kafir) has died and has no kafir relative, (a Muslim relative) is present, he washes him, i.e., the Muslim washes the kafir, (like washing a filthy rag) without observing the sunna of washing. He washes the kafir because it is a general sunna for the children of Adam, and because at the time of his return to Allah it becomes a proof against him, not a purification. So much so that if it falls into water, it spoils it, unlike a Muslim who does not make the water impure. And the prayer of one carrying a washed Muslim is valid, as in ad-Diraya and al-Bahr. And he shrouds him in a rag without observing the sunna of the shroud, and throws him into a pit without a niche, throwing him like a carcass without a niche, and that is out of consideration for kinship. And if he has a kafir relative, it is better for the Muslim not to undertake the matter of his relative, but to hand him over to his kafir relative. (Or he hands him over) i.e., the Muslim relative hands the kafir (to the people of his religion) and follows his funeral from a distance. And by saying 'people of his religion' we indicate that his kufr is original, for an apostate has no religion, and he is not handed over to one who apostatized to their religion. So he is not washed at all but is thrown into a pit like a dog, as stated in many books. And we have indicated that if a Muslim has only a kafir relative, he is not prevented, because undertaking the preparation of his body is a communal obligation upon the Muslims. Do you not see that the Prophet ﷺ was with Abu Bakr and 'Umar when they came upon a Jew reading the Torah, consoling himself about his son who had died, who was the best and most handsome youth. So the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'I adjure you by the One who revealed the Torah, do you find in your book my description and my place of emergence?' He shook his head thus, meaning 'no'. His son said: 'Yes, by the One who revealed the Torah, we indeed find you in our book, your description and your place of emergence, and I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and that you are the Messenger of Allah.' So the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Move the Jew away from your brother.' Then he undertook the prayer over him. And it ended. So the Jew was not given control, and the Muslims took charge of his matter. And in at-Tajnīs: The Muslim should not bury a mahram relative, because curses descend upon the kafir, and the Muslim is in need of mercy especially at this hour. End.
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah provides a detailed ruling on how a Muslim should handle the funeral of a non-Muslim relative. The lesson type is a ruling with proof. The author begins by stating that if a kafir has a Muslim relative present, the Muslim is to wash the body of the kafir, but not with the ceremonial washing of a Muslim; rather it is like washing a filthy rag, without observing the sunnah of washing. The reason given is that it is a general Sunnah for all children of Adam, and it serves as a proof against the kafir on the Day of Judgment, not as a purification. Therefore, if the water used falls onto the ground, it becomes impure (najis), unlike the case of a Muslim whose washing water remains pure. The Muslim shrouds the body in a simple rag and buries it in any pit without the niche (lahd) of a Muslim grave, out of respect for kinship. However, if the kafir has other kafir relatives, it is better for the Muslim to hand the matter over to them. If the kafir has only Muslim relatives, then the Muslims must take charge, as it is a fard kifayah. The author then presents a hadith story: The Prophet ﷺ, Abu Bakr, and 'Umar came upon a Jewish man mourning his son. The Jew denied the Prophet's description in the Torah, but his son affirmed and embraced Islam. The Prophet then led the prayer over the son. The author argues that this shows that even if the deceased is a non-Muslim, if he has no kafir relatives, Muslims must handle the burial. The passage ends with a quote from at-Tajnīs advising against a Muslim burying a mahram relative because the kafir is cursed and the Muslim needs mercy. Throughout, the author contrasts treatment of Muslims and kafirs in funeral rites, emphasizing that kafirs are not purified and their bodies are treated as impure.

Key Terms
غسل الكافر (ghusl al-kāfir): The washing of a non‑Muslim body, done without the sunnah of washing and considered like washing a filthy rag.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) He washes him like a filthy rag, without sunnah.
D) He does not wash him at all; he should be buried as is.

Key Takeaway
When a non‑Muslim relative dies with no kāfir relatives, a Muslim must wash, shroud, and bury him minimally, treating the body as impure and not performing the sunnah washing.

Janazah Prayer and Its Denial: Rebels, Highway Robbers, and Others
Rulings on who is not entitled to janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories of people over whom janazah prayer is not performed in the Hanafi school, and explain the rationale based on the practice of 'Ali and the principle of deterrence.

Core Idea
Janazah prayer is an honor; it is denied to rebels and highway robbers killed in battle as a deterrent, but suicides are prayed over.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah lists specific cases where the janazah prayer is not performed, based on the practice of 'Ali and consensus. The ruling serves as a legal deterrent and marks these deaths as distinct from martyrdom. We will explore each category and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is performing janazah prayer over certain deceased. The ruling is that it is prohibited (makruh tahrimi) for specific categories.
2
Note the proof
The primary proof is ijma from the practice of 'Ali, who did not pray over the rebels at the Battle of the Camel, and no Companion objected.
This constitutes tacit consensus (sukuti).
3
Distinguish the categories
Separate rebels and highway robbers killed in combat (no prayer) from those captured/subdued (prayer performed). Also note assassins, bullies, partisanship victims.
The distinction is based on the condition of the hand of the imam.
4
Differentiate from suicide
Unlike the above, a suicide is washed and prayed over, per the text.
Suicide is a major sin but does not negate Muslim status for janazah.
5
Understand the rationale
The denial is a punishment and deterrent (zajr), not an indication that they are not Muslims. They are still buried in Muslim cemeteries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا يُصَلَّى علی: باغ) اتفاقاً، والبغاة: المسلمون الخارجون عن طاعة الإمام، كما هو معلوم فـي بـابـه، (و) كـذا اتفاقاً على (قاطع طريق) إذا (قتل) الباغي، أو قاطع الطريق (حالة المُحَارَبَةِ)، ولا لأن عليه لم يصل على البغاة ، ولم ينكر عليه، فكان إجماعاً، وقطـاع الطريق بمنزلتهم ، كذا في ( البحر » ، وقيل : يغسل الباغي والقاطع، ولا يصلي عليهما، للفرق بينهما وبين الشهداء، وأما إذا قتلا بعد ثبوت يد الإمام عليهما فإنهما يغسلان ويصلى عليهما، وهذا تفصيل حسن أخذ به الكبار من المشايخ، كذا قاله الزيلعي (وَ) لا يصلى على (قاتل بالخَلْقِ غِيلَةٌ) بالكسر : الاغتيال يقال: قتلة غيلة وهو: أن يخدعه فيذهب به إلى موضع، فإذا صار إليه قتله لسعيه في الأرض بالفساد، (وَ) لا على مُكابر ) في المِصْرِ ليلاً بالسلاح) إذا قتل في تلك الحالة، (وَ) لا يصلى على (مقتول عصبيَّة) إهانة لهم وزجراً لغيرهم، وإنْ غُسلوا) كالبغاة، على أحـد الروايتين: لا يصلى عليهم وإن غسلوا (وقاتلُ نفسِهِ) عمداً (يُغَسَّلُ ويُصَلَّـى عليـه)، وقال أبو لا يصلي يغسل أحد . منهم،
(And prayer is not performed over: a rebel) by agreement, and rebels are Muslims who go out of obedience to the Imam, as known in its place. (And) likewise by agreement (the highway robber) when (killed) the rebel or highway robber (in the state of combat). And because 'Ali did not pray over the rebels, and it was not objected to, so it was consensus. And highway robbers are in their position, as in al-Bahr. And it is said: the rebel and the highway robber are washed but not prayed over, due to the difference between them and martyrs. But if they are killed after the Imam's hand has been established over them, then they are washed and prayed over. This is a good detail adopted by the great scholars, as al-Zayla'i said. (And) no prayer is performed over (one who kills by deceit - ghīla) with kasr: assassination. It is said: qatla ghīla, which is that he tricks him and takes him to a place, and when he reaches him, he kills him, because of his corruption on earth. (And) not over a bully (or overpowerer) in the city at night with weapons, when killed in that state. (And) no prayer is performed over (one killed by partisanship) as an insult to them and a deterrent to others. And Abu said: he does not pray, he washes no one among them.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah lists categories of people over whom the janazah prayer is not performed. The lesson type is a ruling with proof, and the textual operation is expansion probe. The author begins by stating that prayer is not performed over a rebel (baghi) by consensus. Rebels are defined as Muslims who rebel against the rightful Imam. The proof is that 'Ali ibn Abi Talib did not pray over the rebels at the Battle of the Camel, and no Companion objected, so this constitutes ijma. Similarly, highway robbers (qati' al-tariq) killed in the act are not prayed over. However, if they are captured after the Imam has subdued them, then they are washed and prayed over. This distinction is taken from the great scholars. The text then lists: one who kills by deception (ghila), a bully who attacks at night in the city with weapons, and one killed because of partisanship (asabiyya) — none of these receive janazah prayer, even if they are washed. In contrast, a suicide is washed and the prayer is performed over him. The passage ends with a reported disagreement: Abu [Yusuf?] says he does not pray or wash any of them? The text is incomplete, but the relied-upon position is that a suicide is prayed over. The overall ruling is that janazah prayer is a form of honor, and those who die in open rebellion or causing corruption are denied this honor as a deterrent and punishment.

Key Terms
باغ (baghi): A rebel from among the Muslims who exits obedience to the legitimate Imam.
غيلة (ghila): Treacherous killing by deception, akin to assassination.
قاطع طريق (qati' al-tariq): Highway robber or bandit who attacks travelers.
عصبية (asabiyya): Partisanship or tribal solidarity leading to murder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The denial of janazah prayer to rebels and highway robbers killed in battle serves as a legal deterrent and is based on the consensus of the Companions, while suicides are given the prayer.

Funeral Prayer for Parricide and Suicide
States rulings on funeral prayer for parricide and suicide with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer for deliberate parricide and suicide, identify the dalil from hadith, and explain the rationale of disciplinary prevention.

Core Idea
No funeral prayer for deliberate parricide or suicide as a deterrent, not because the person is a disbeliever.

The funeral prayer is a right of every Muslim, but certain grave sins may lead to withholding it as punishment. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on two such cases: a person who deliberately kills a parent (parricide) and one who commits suicide. The school applies a disciplinary measure (ta'zir) based on prophetic example, while affirming the deceased remains a believer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that the funeral prayer is not performed for a person who deliberately killed one of their parents (parricide) or committed suicide. Note that accidental killing or suicide due to pain does not prevent prayer.
The ruling is explicitly stated twice in the passage.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith: a man who killed himself with an arrowhead was brought to the Prophet (ﷺ) and he did not pray over him. This is recorded by Abu Dawud.
The dalil is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut), but it is sufficient for a disciplinary ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's omission of the prayer indicates prohibition. By qiyas (analogy), the same applies to deliberate parricide, as both are major intentional sins that warrant deterrence.
The analogy is based on the common illah: intentional grave sin.
4
Apply the restriction
The ruling is limited to deliberate acts. If the killing was accidental (parricide) or suicide due to unbearable pain, the prayer is performed by consensus.
This shows the distinction is based on intent (niyyah).
5
Understand the rationale
The prayer is withheld as humiliation (ihana) and deterrent (zajr) for others. The deceased is still a believing sinner (mu'min mudhnib), not a disbeliever, so the ruling is disciplinary, not excommunication.
This prevents the misconception that the person is kafir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وَلا) يصلى على قاتل أحد أبويهِ عَمْداً إهانة له وزجراً لغيره انتهى. (1) لما ورد أنه أتي له برجل قتل نفسه بمشقص فلم يصل عليه، أخرجه أبو داود في الجنائز، باب: الإمام لا يصلي على من قتل نفسه (۳۱۸۵)، والمشقص: ج مشاقص نصل السهم إذا كان طويلاً غير عريض. (۲) ما بين الحاصرتين في المخطوطة (ب) (قال) والصواب ما أثبتناه من المخطوطة (م).
And not (prayed over) the one who kills one of his parents deliberately. Yusuf: 'He is not prayed over.' And the judge Imam Ali al-Sa'di (may Allah have mercy on him) used to say: 'The most correct in my view is that he is not prayed over.' And by the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani gave fatwa: 'And it is the most correct because he is a believing sinner, so he becomes like others who commit major sins.' Similarly in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And we restricted (the ruling) to deliberate (killing), because if he kills himself by mistake, he is prayed over by consensus. And whoever kills himself due to pain is prayed over—thus in al-Inaya without narrating any disagreement. And the killer of himself is greater in sin and transgression than the killer of another. End quote. Similarly in Sharh al-Maqdisi. And whoever dies with a debt and has wealth—he is prayed over. And he is not prayed over: the one who kills one of his parents deliberately, as a humiliation for him and a deterrent for others. End quote. (1) Because it was narrated that a man was brought to him who killed himself with an arrowhead, and he did not pray over him—reported by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Jana'iz, Bab: The Imam does not pray over the one who kills himself (no. 3185). Al-Mishqas: plural mashaqis, the blade of an arrow if it is long and not wide. (2) What is between the brackets in manuscript (B) is (said), and the correct is what we have established from manuscript (M).
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding funeral prayer for a parricide and suicide. It begins by stating that funeral prayer is not performed for someone who deliberately killed one of his parents. Imam Abu Yusuf (Yusuf) confirms this ruling. The judge Ali al-Sa'di also considers it more correct. The fatwa is given according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), as chosen by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, because the person is a believing sinner, similar to other major sinners. The passage then adds a restriction: this applies only to deliberate killing. If the killing is accidental, there is consensus that prayer is performed. Similarly, if a person kills himself due to severe pain (i.e., not intentionally), he is prayed over without any reported disagreement. However, intentional suicide is more sinful than killing another, and the hadith of the man who killed himself with an arrowhead (narrated by Abu Dawud) is cited as evidence that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not pray over him. The passage concludes by reiterating the ruling: no funeral prayer for the deliberate parricide, as a humiliation and deterrent. It also notes that a person with debt but sufficient wealth is prayed over (implying the debt is covered).

Key Terms
قاتل أحد أبويه عمداً (qātil aḥad abawayhi ʿamdan): A person who deliberately kills one of his parents.
مشقص (mishqaṣ): A long, narrow arrowhead.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the reason for not performing the funeral prayer over a deliberate parricide or suicide?
A) The person is considered a disbeliever.
B) As a humiliation and deterrent for others, while still considering the person a believing sinner.
C) Because the corpse is ritually impure.
D) Because the family does not request it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school withholds funeral prayer for deliberate parricide and suicide as a disciplinary measure, not because the deceased is a disbeliever, and the ruling is restricted to intentional acts.
